# Foreword
# 前言

have been revised and updated. In the geology notes the local area - in this case Edinburgh - is emphasised, and this is quite deliberate, as it serves as an example of relating what has been learned to the familiar, local area. One might expect lessons on geology to start from a description of Plate Tectonics -- the great discovery arrived at during the 1960s. But this is the point - modern geology had existed for nearly 200 years and was a very advanced science before these discoveries could be made and appreciated. It is all too easy to give children 'ready-made' conclusions; conclusions which, in reality, evolved only gradually. The unfortunate result can then be that the conclusions are indeed accepted, but accepted as somewhat undigested dogma, not truly understood. The consideration of Plate Tectonics might come much better in the ninth grade, when time can be spent considering the diverse evidence -- the 'detective story' which, eventually, led to such astonishing conclusions about the structure of the Earth.

本書的地質學部分經過修訂與更新。書中特別強調了當地區域——此處以 Edinburgh（愛丁堡）為例——這是刻意的安排，旨在示範如何將所學知識與熟悉的在地環境相聯繫。人們或許會期望地質學課程從板塊構造論——這項在一九六零年代取得的偉大發現——開始講起。但關鍵正在於此：現代地質學已存在了將近兩百年，並在這些發現被提出與理解之前，就已是一門非常先進的科學。把「現成的」結論直接交給孩子們，是一件太容易的事；而這些結論實際上是逐步演化而來的。這樣做的不幸結果，是結論雖然被接受了，卻被當作未經消化的教條來接受，並未真正理解。板塊構造論的探討或許更適合放在九年級，屆時可以花時間考察那些多元的證據——那個最終導向關於地球結構之驚人結論的「偵探故事」。


In astronomy too the approach is to start from observations of sun, moon and stars - phenomena which have been experienced and understood -- without special equipment or theories -- for millennia. Once again, the upper grades are a better place to consider how the more recent concepts evolved. The later chapters on discoveries with the telescope are the most difficult to keep up to date, as new discoveries are continually being made, both with more powerful telescopes and with space probes.

在天文學方面，同樣的做法是從對太陽、月亮和星辰的觀察出發——這些現象數千年來無需特殊設備或理論就能被人類感知與理解。同樣地，高年級才是探討較新概念如何演變的更好時機。後面關於望遠鏡發現的章節是最難保持更新的，因為無論是更強大的望遠鏡還是太空探測器，都不斷帶來新的發現。


We hope that these notes can serve as a stimulus to the creativity of individual teachers, rather than be followed as a scheme. This would be in keeping with the wishes of Charles Kovacs.

我們希望這些筆記能夠激發每位教師個人的創造力，而非被當作一套固定方案來遵循。這也符合 Charles Kovacs（查爾斯．科瓦奇）的願望。


---

# 1. The Children of the Earth
# 1. 大地的孩子們

In the winter it can get very cold, but no matter how cold it can get here in our part of the world, there are places where it can get much, much colder. In which direction would we travel to find lands where it gets much colder than here? Would it be east, where the sun rises? South, where the sun stands highest at noon? West, where the sun sets? Or north, the direction in which we never see the sun moving across the sky? To find the colder lands we would travel north.

冬天可以變得非常寒冷，但無論我們所處的這一方天地能冷到什麼程度，世界上還有些地方可以冷得多、冷得多。我們往哪個方向走，才能找到比這裡冷得多的土地呢？是往東方，太陽升起的地方？還是南方，正午時太陽高掛的方向？或者西方，太陽落下的地方？又或是北方，那個我們從未見過太陽掠過的方向？要找到更寒冷的土地，我們得往北走。


Travelling north we would come to lands which are much colder than ours; and the further we go north the colder it would get, until we come to parts of the world which are so cold that the ice and snow never melt completely and the ground is always frozen -- summer and winter. Think of Greenland, Northern Canada, Alaska or Northern Russia. These are the lands around the North Pole, the polar region, the region of everlasting ice and snow.

一路往北，我們會來到比我們這裡冷得多的土地；越往北走就越冷，直到來到世界上那些冷到冰雪永遠不會完全融化、地面四季凍結的地方。想想 Greenland（格陵蘭）、加拿大北部、Alaska（阿拉斯加）或俄羅斯北部。這些就是環繞北極的土地——極地地區，永恆的冰雪之域。


On such a journey to the frozen north we would discover something else. We would notice something about the plants. In our part of the world there are two kinds of trees. First the leafy trees which, every winter, shed their leaves and stand bare. Then there are the trees that have only green "needles" for leaves; in botany we call them conifers or evergreens. Here, in our part of the world, we have these two kinds of trees, but going further north the leafy trees get fewer and fewer. There you would hardly see anything but the dark green of pines, firs and larches; the trees which have green needles as leaves.

在這趟前往冰封北方的旅途中，我們還會發現別的事情。我們會注意到植物的變化。在我們所處的這片土地上，有兩種樹木。首先是闊葉樹，每到冬天就落下葉片，光禿禿地站立著。其次是只有綠色「針葉」的樹；在植物學裡我們稱它們為針葉樹或常綠樹。在我們這裡，這兩種樹都有，但越往北走，闊葉樹就越來越少。在那裡，你幾乎只看得到松樹、冷杉和落葉松那深沉的綠——那些以綠色針葉為葉片的樹。


Can you guess why this is so, why the trees with broad leaves get fewer and fewer the further we go north? Because a broad leaf tree needs more sun and cannot stand being frozen. Where there is less sunlight and it is less warm the trees with narrow leaves, or needles, can live better than the others. One could say that the leaves "shrink" and become needles as we go further north. Not only the leaves shrink as you go north; the trees themselves get smaller. The pines, firs and larches that grow far to the north of us are like dwarfs compared with our trees; they would barely reach to your shoulders. In the regions where these dwarf trees grow there is still a kind of summer. The snow does melt and then plants and flowers grow and have lovely blossoms; but they all have only tiny, tiny stalks, much shorter stalks than our flowers here. If we go still further north we come to the regions where nothing grows at all - not even dwarf trees or tiny flowers. These are the regions near the North Pole, the regions of everlasting ice.

你能猜到為什麼嗎？為什麼越往北走，闊葉樹就越來越少？因為闊葉樹需要更多的陽光，而且受不了凍。在陽光較少、不那麼溫暖的地方，窄葉的樹——也就是針葉樹——比其他樹活得更好。可以說，越往北走，葉片就「縮小」變成了針。不只是葉片縮小了；整棵樹也越來越矮。生長在我們遙遠北方的松樹、冷杉和落葉松，跟我們的樹比起來就像矮人一樣，它們大概只到你肩膀的高度。在這些矮樹生長的地區，還算是有一種夏天。雪會融化，然後植物和花朵就生長開花，綻放出可愛的花朵；但它們全都只有小小的、小小的莖，比我們這裡的花短得多。如果我們再往北走，就來到了什麼也長不出來的地方——連矮樹或小花都沒有。這就是靠近北極的地區，永恆之冰的領域。


But how would things change if we travelled further and further south -- in the direction where the sun stands at its highest at noon? We know of course that it would get warmer and warmer. We would come to lands where people never have winter. How do the plants change as we go further south? Going south the needle trees become fewer and fewer, as they don't like too much sunlight, and the leafy trees increase; we come to trees with very large leaves indeed, like the palm trees. Think how long and broad and thick the palm leaves are. The trees also get taller and the other plants, the flowers, shoot up too. They have long stalks, long leaves and large blossoms in the hot lands of the tropics.

但如果我們越來越往南走——朝著正午太陽最高的方向——事物又會怎樣變化呢？我們當然知道會越來越溫暖。我們會來到人們從不經歷冬天的土地。越往南走，植物會怎麼變化？往南走，針葉樹越來越少，因為它們不喜歡太多陽光，而闊葉樹則越來越多；我們會看到葉片非常大的樹，比如棕櫚樹。想想棕櫚葉有多長、多寬、多厚。樹也長得更高，其他的植物、花朵也一起竄了上去。在炎熱的熱帶地區，它們有著長長的莖、長長的葉和碩大的花朵。


So you see how the whole earth changes from north to south. In the south, in the tropics, it is always summer -- it is sunny and hot and we find tall trees, long stalks, big leaves and large flowers. The further north we go the trees are smaller, the leaves shrink, the stalks get shorter and, in the end, we come to lands where it is always winter and there is always ice and snow. Of course if you go beyond the equator, as far south as you can go, you finally end up at the South Pole and it is again extremely cold.

這樣你就看到了整個地球從南到北是如何變化的。在南方，在熱帶，永遠是夏天——陽光燦爛、炎熱無比，我們看到高大的樹木、長長的莖、大大的葉子和碩大的花朵。越往北走，樹越矮，葉子越縮小，莖越短，到最後，我們來到永遠是冬天、永遠是冰雪的土地。當然，如果你越過赤道、盡可能地往南走，最終會到達南極，那裡又是極度寒冷的了。


What I have just described is about the whole earth. The whole earth changes like this from south to north, or from equator to pole. But think of a very high mountain. Let us take the highest mountains there are in the world; the Himalayas. At the foot of the Himalayas you have a hot climate, the hot weather of India. You would see tall, broad-leaved flowers and trees. But as you go up into the mountains the air gets cooler and cooler, and the trees and plants become smaller. At a certain height you might think you are in Scotland -- there are pines, larches, there is even heather, but there are also oak trees and beech trees. You go still higher and soon there are only needle trees and they become smaller. There are mountain flowers, like gentian, with short stalks. If you go still higher up there is, again, everlasting snow and ice. The summits of such high mountains are just like the polar regions and nothing can grow in the

我剛才描述的是整個地球的情況。整個地球就是這樣從南到北、從赤道到極地發生變化。但想想一座非常高的山。讓我們拿世界上最高的山脈來說——Himalayas（喜馬拉雅山）。在喜馬拉雅山腳下，你會遇到炎熱的氣候，印度的酷暑天氣。你會看到高大的闊葉花卉和樹木。但隨著你走進山裡，空氣越來越涼，樹木和植物也越來越矮小。到了一定的高度，你可能會以為自己身在 Scotland（蘇格蘭）——有松樹、落葉松，甚至有石楠花，但也有橡樹和山毛櫸。再往上走，很快就只剩下針葉樹了，而且越來越矮。有些山地花卉，像是龍膽，莖短短的。如果你再往更高處走，又是永恆的冰雪了。這些高山的山頂就像極地一樣，什麼也長不出來。


---

# 2. The Story that the Mountains Tell
# 2. 山脈訴說的故事

The hills and mountains of Scotland are very beautiful, but even our highest mountains in Scotland, the Cairngorms and Ben Nevis, cannot give you the kind of feeling that you have when you stand before the really high mountains of the world. If you have never seen the Alps before and are in Switzerland for the first time it can happen that you look up into the sky and think, "That's a strangely shaped white cloud up there." But when you look again, you see that it is not a cloud at all, but a range of snow-white mountain peaks, towering in the sky.

Scotland（蘇格蘭）的丘陵和山脈非常美麗，但即使是蘇格蘭最高的山——Cairngorms（凱恩戈姆山脈）和 Ben Nevis（本尼維斯山）——也無法給你那種站在世界真正高山面前時的感受。如果你從未見過 Alps（阿爾卑斯山），第一次來到 Switzerland（瑞士），可能會發生這樣的事：你抬頭望向天空，心想：「上面那朵白雲的形狀真奇怪。」但再看一眼，你會發現那根本不是雲，而是一排雪白的山峰，高聳入雲。


These mighty, powerful, majestic giants, reaching up into the clouds, leave you feeling something like awe before that power and greatness. But looking at these towering peaks you can also feel how immeasurably old these giants are. They have stood there for millions of years and they will stand there for millions of years to come. If these mighty peaks could speak they would tell us the life story of earth itself. We walk on the earth, we build our houses and cities on the earth and we use stones taken from the earth for our buildings, but what do we know about the story of the earth? The ancient, mighty mountains can tell us something about the story of the earth. Let us see what the mountains can tell us.

這些威武、強大、莊嚴的巨人，伸展入雲端，讓你在那力量與偉大面前油然生出一種類似敬畏的感覺。但凝望這些高聳的山峰時，你也能感受到這些巨人是多麼不可估量地古老。它們已經在那裡矗立了數百萬年，還將在那裡矗立數百萬年。如果這些巍峨的山峰能夠開口說話，它們會告訴我們地球自身的生命故事。我們在大地上行走，在大地上建造房屋和城市，用從大地取出的石頭蓋建築，但我們對大地的故事了解多少呢？古老而巍峨的山脈可以告訴我們一些關於大地的故事。讓我們來看看山脈能告訴我們什麼。


The first thing is that the great mountains of the world do not stand alone like proud giants, they are mostly to be found in groups or in long rows. These rows of mountains sometimes curve across the face of the earth for hundreds or even thousands of miles, and are called mountain chains or mountain ranges. The Alps are a mountain range, so are the Urals, and if you look at a map you will find that there are many, many more of these ranges. You can see that the Alps are really part of a much longer range that curves its way far to the east.

首先，世界上的大山並不像驕傲的巨人那樣獨自聳立，它們大多成群或排成長列。這些山列有時在大地表面彎曲延伸數百甚至數千英里，被稱為山鏈或山脈。阿爾卑斯山是一條山脈，Urals（烏拉爾山脈）也是，如果你看地圖，會發現還有許許多多這樣的山脈。你可以看到，阿爾卑斯山其實是一條更長山脈的一部分，那條山脈蜿蜒向東延伸至很遠的地方。


The next thing is that they are extremely old, unimaginably old, but - and this may sound strange -- the mountains are not all of the same age; there are young and old mountains. The Alps are young and the Urals are old. Of course, even a "young" mountain at which you may be looking is much older than anything you can think of, but it is still young compared with another mountain.

其次，它們極其古老，古老到無法想像，但——這聽起來可能很奇怪——山脈並不是都一樣老的；有年輕的山，也有古老的山。阿爾卑斯山是年輕的，烏拉爾山脈是古老的。當然，即使是你正在看的一座「年輕」的山，也比你所能想到的任何事物都要古老得多，但和另一座山相比，它仍然是年輕的。


Now we will compare the earth with the moon, the earth's companion in space. Astronauts have travelled to the moon and scientists have studied the rocks and mountains there. There are many great mountains on the moon, but they are all very old indeed - and they have hardly changed in the millions and millions of years since they were first created. The moon is beautiful, but its surface is like a barren desert, forever dead and unchanging; there are no young mountains at all, everything is very ancient.

現在讓我們把地球和月亮——地球在太空中的伴侶——做個比較。太空人已經到過月球，科學家也研究了那裡的岩石和山脈。月球上有很多大山，但它們全都非常非常古老——自從它們最初形成以來，在千百萬年間幾乎沒有改變。月亮很美，但它的表面就像一片荒涼的沙漠，永遠死寂而不變；完全沒有年輕的山，一切都非常古老。


Here on earth the young mountains are usually the biggest and tallest, with their jagged snowy peaks reaching far up above the clouds. Old mountains are not so big, although, when they were young, they too were just as tall as young mountains -- like the Alps -- are now. The old mountains have changed through time, they have been worn down and "rounded off."

在我們地球上，年輕的山通常是最大最高的，它們鋸齒狀的雪白山峰遠遠伸入雲層之上。古老的山沒有那麼大，儘管在它們年輕的時候，也曾像現在的年輕山脈——比如阿爾卑斯山——一樣高大。古老的山脈隨著時間改變了，它們被磨損了、被「磨圓」了。


So mountains tell us that the earth is not a dead place like the moon, it is active; old ranges are broken down and new ones are created. Always, somewhere on earth, there is destruction going on, but somewhere else there will always be new creation. Our earth is not just like some big lump of stone, it is a living, changing place -- even when it comes to the seemingly lifeless rocks and mountains.

所以山脈告訴我們，地球不是像月球那樣的死寂之地，它是活躍的；古老的山脈被分解，新的山脈被創造出來。在地球的某個地方，總有破壞正在進行，但在另一個地方，也總有新的創造在發生。我們的地球不只是一大塊石頭，它是一個有生命、不斷變化的地方——即使是看似毫無生命的岩石和山脈也是如此。


So that is the third thing: young mountains appear, old mountains wear down, and we learn that the earth is a place where great changes are always happening. And the way that mountains form in ranges tells us that the changes do not happen haphazardly - there is a pattern to them.

這就是第三件事：年輕的山出現，古老的山被磨損，而我們由此了解到，地球是一個不斷發生巨大變化的地方。而山脈排列成列的方式告訴我們，這些變化並非雜亂無章地發生——其中有一種模式。


---

# 3. Young and Old Rocks: Granite
# 3. 年輕與古老的岩石：花崗岩

There are young mountains and old mountains but -- and this is not the same thing - there are also young rocks and old rocks. Old mountains are made of old rocks and so you might think that young mountains must be made of young rocks, but this is not necessarily so. When nature makes a new mountain it uses rocks that are already there, just as a builder can use blocks of old stone to make a new house. In nature it is normal to recycle everything, and a young mountain range will be made of many different ages of older rocks. So there are young rocks, there are very ancient rocks and there is everything in between. What, then, are the oldest rocks?

有年輕的山，也有古老的山，但——這是不同的事——也有年輕的岩石和古老的岩石。古老的山由古老的岩石構成，所以你可能會以為年輕的山一定是由年輕的岩石構成的，但事實未必如此。大自然造一座新山的時候，用的是已經存在的岩石，就像建築師可以用舊石塊蓋新房子一樣。在大自然中，回收利用一切是正常的事，一條年輕的山脈會由許多不同年齡的古老岩石組成。所以有年輕的岩石，有非常古老的岩石，還有介於兩者之間的一切。那麼，最古老的岩石是什麼呢？


To find the oldest rocks you need to look deep down into the earth. The oldest rock of all, the rock which lies under all the land and mountains of the earth under all our lakes and land, fields and forests, cities and roads - that kind of rock is a light-coloured rock called granite. Granite lies deep within all the continents of the earth. Beneath the soil on which we walk there may be clay and beneath the clay there may be limestone or sandstone and beneath that there may be something else -- but if we go deep enough we shall always find granite. (Later we shall look at what is below the granite.)

要找到最古老的岩石，你得往地球深處去看。最古老的岩石——那種躺在地球上所有陸地和山脈之下、所有湖泊與田野、森林與城市、道路之下的岩石——是一種淺色的岩石，叫做 granite（花崗岩）。花崗岩深藏在地球所有大陸的深處。在我們腳下的土壤之下可能是黏土，黏土之下可能是石灰岩或砂岩，再之下可能是別的什麼——但只要我們挖得夠深，就一定會找到花崗岩。（稍後我們會看看花崗岩下面是什麼。）


But granite is not only to be found deep down, it can sometimes be found around us or at great heights. The Alps are partly limestone and other kinds of rock, but their highest peaks are of granite. Granite can reach from the deepest depth below to the highest heights above. We have granite in Scotland also: our Highlands, the Cairngorms for instance, are granite mountains. If you walk on this granite you walk on very old rock, you walk on rock that reaches deep into the earth and you walk on something that belongs to the very beginning of our earth.

但花崗岩不只在地底深處才找得到，有時在我們周圍或很高的地方也能發現它。阿爾卑斯山有一部分是石灰岩和其他種類的岩石，但它們最高的山峰是花崗岩。花崗岩可以從最深的深處延伸到最高的高處。蘇格蘭也有花崗岩：我們的高地，例如凱恩戈姆山脈，就是花崗岩山。如果你走在這花崗岩上，你走在非常古老的岩石上，你走在深入地球深處的岩石上，你走在屬於我們地球最初始的東西上面。


There is a beautiful legend about granite.

關於花崗岩有一個美麗的傳說。


God wanted to create the strong, solid stone and rock upon which man should walk firmly through life. He turned to his helpers, the spirits and angels who serve him and he said, "Bring to me the gifts which you have so that the first of all rocks may be made."

上帝想要創造堅強、堅固的石頭和岩石，讓人類可以穩穩地走過一生。祂轉向祂的助手們——那些服侍祂的精靈和天使——說：「把你們的禮物帶來給我，好讓最初的岩石得以被造出來。」


Now there were three groups of angels around God. The first group were the angels of wisdom. The highest of the angels of wisdom came forward and he brought God the Father a stone that was as clear as water -- it was transparent. The Angel said, "You, Father have given us the light of wise thought. This is the stone which is like the light of wisdom and the thought of man shall be like this shining crystal."

在上帝身邊有三組天使。第一組是智慧天使。智慧天使中最高的那位走上前來，帶給天父一塊像水一樣清澈的石頭——它是透明的。天使說：「父啊，祢賜給了我們智慧思想的光芒。這就是那塊如同智慧之光的石頭，人的思想將如同這閃耀的水晶。」


Then came the second group, these were angels of strength and power. The highest of these angels came before God and carried in his right hand a black stone, and in his left hand a white stone. The angel said, "These two stones, black and white, are the stones of strength. They will give man energy and strength so that his wise thoughts will lead him to deeds."

然後來了第二組，這些是力量與權能的天使。這些天使中最高的那位來到上帝面前，右手拿著一塊黑色的石頭，左手拿著一塊白色的石頭。天使說：「這兩塊石頭，一黑一白，是力量之石。它們將賦予人類能量和力量，使他智慧的思想能引導他去行動。」


The third group were the angels of warmth and love. The highest of them brought a green stone and a red stone. He said, "In these stones we have put the warmth of our hearts. These stones can have many forms and will serve man in many ways."

第三組是溫暖與愛的天使。其中最高的那位帶來一塊綠色的石頭和一塊紅色的石頭。他說：「在這些石頭裡，我們注入了我們心中的溫暖。這些石頭可以有很多形態，將以許多方式服務人類。」


And from these three gifts of the angels God made the first, the oldest of all the rocks, granite - from the gift of light, the gift of strength and the gift of warmth.

上帝用天使的這三份禮物造出了最初的、最古老的岩石——花崗岩——由光之禮、力量之禮和溫暖之禮而成。


There are many varieties of granite, but it always is a mixture of these three things: a clear, transparent stone called quartz, a black or white stone called mica (which glistens and sparkles in the light), and lastly a pinkish, white or greenish stone called feldspar (which gives granite its colour). As we shall find out later, the best soil for farming comes from feldspar. The bread we eat comes from feldspar earth.

花崗岩有很多種類，但它始終是這三樣東西的混合：一種清澈透明的石頭叫做 quartz（石英），一種黑色或白色的石頭叫做 mica（雲母，在光線下閃閃發亮），以及一種粉紅、白色或帶綠色的石頭叫做 feldspar（長石，它賦予花崗岩顏色）。我們稍後會發現，最好的農業土壤就來自長石。我們吃的麵包，來自長石化成的泥土。


The mighty granite rock, the oldest of rocks, is made up of three parts: quartz, the gift of light, mica, the gift of strength and feldspar, the gift of warmth.

巍峨的花崗岩，最古老的岩石，由三個部分組成：石英——光之禮，雲母——力量之禮，長石——溫暖之禮。


---

# 4. The First Rocks
# 4. 最初的岩石

When a house is built the first thing is that a foundation is laid for the house. The foundation carries the whole weight of the house. Granite, the oldest of the rocks, is the foundation, the mighty giant that carries all other stones, rocks, earth and seas on its back. Beneath the oceans of the world, it is slightly different: the rock that supports the great oceans is a dark rock called basalt. Basalt is a relative of granite; you could say that it is like a younger brother. Basalt is dark in colour while granite is light, because basalt contains more iron and less of the clear quartz than granite. Iron is to be found in the basalt which forms the rocky bed of the great oceans. So the continents are supported on light-coloured granite and the oceans on dark-coloured basalt. Together these two "brothers" make up the foundations of the earth.

蓋房子的時候，首先要做的是打地基。地基承載著整座房屋的重量。花崗岩，最古老的岩石，就是這個地基——那個背上扛著所有其他石頭、岩石、泥土和海洋的巨人。在世界大洋之下，情況略有不同：支撐著大洋的岩石是一種深色的岩石，叫做 basalt（玄武岩）。玄武岩是花崗岩的親戚，你可以說它像是一個弟弟。玄武岩顏色暗，而花崗岩顏色淺，因為玄武岩含有更多的鐵，而清澈的石英比花崗岩少。鐵存在於構成大洋岩石床的玄武岩中。所以大陸被支撐在淺色的花崗岩上，大洋被支撐在深色的玄武岩上。這兩個「兄弟」合在一起，構成了大地的基礎。


When you look at a granite mountain - in the mighty Alps, or the Highlands of Scotland, or even at small pieces of granite -- you are looking at something so unbelievably old, so ancient, something that came into existence so long ago, that no one can know for certain how it happened. So there are two different ways of explaining how granite came to be.

當你看著一座花崗岩山——在巍峨的阿爾卑斯山，或蘇格蘭高地，甚至只是看著小塊的花崗岩——你正在看的東西是如此難以置信地古老、如此遠古，它的誕生是如此久遠以前的事，沒有人能確切地知道當時發生了什麼。因此，對於花崗岩是怎麼來的，有兩種不同的解釋方式。


Before the first explanation I want to tell you of something I saw as a child in Austria. During the holidays my parents used to take us to a little town called Baden, which means bath. Why was it called that? Because this town had a spring of water that came from deep down in the earth and this spring of water was hot. It was nearly boiling hot as it came from the earth. It was not heated by people but by the earth itself. It also had a peculiar smell, like eggs going bad. To take a bath in this hot, smelly water was a very good cure for rheumatism and so people came from far and wide to take these baths. And there are hot springs in many other parts of the world: England, Iceland, New Zealand, America, Japan.

在講第一種解釋之前，我想告訴你們一件我小時候在 Austria（奧地利）看到的事。假期裡，我父母常帶我們去一個叫 Baden（巴登）的小鎮，這個名字的意思是「沐浴」。為什麼這樣叫呢？因為這個鎮上有一股從地底深處湧出的泉水，而且這泉水是熱的。它從地底湧出時幾乎滾燙。這不是人加熱的，而是大地本身把它加熱的。它還有一種奇特的氣味，像是雞蛋壞掉的味道。在這又熱又臭的水裡泡個澡，是治療風濕的好方法，所以人們從各地趕來泡這些溫泉。世界上很多其他地方也有溫泉：英國、Iceland（冰島）、New Zealand（紐西蘭）、美國、日本。


This water is heated deep down in the earth. When people dig deep mines for coal and for iron they find that the deeper a mine-shaft goes, the warmer it gets. In some mines the shafts go so deep that they need special cooling systems, or the men could not work there at all. We saw earlier that the higher we go the colder it gets; now we can see that the deeper down we go the hotter it gets.

這些水是在地球深處被加熱的。當人們為了煤和鐵而挖掘深深的礦井時，他們發現礦井越深，就越溫暖。有些礦井的通道深到必須安裝特殊的冷卻系統，否則工人根本無法在裡面工作。前面我們看到越往高處走越冷；現在我們可以看到越往地底走越熱。


In steel-works the furnaces produce a heat in which iron melts and flows like water, it becomes a white-hot liquid. If one could dig down deep enough it would be so hot that there would no longer be any hard, solid rock. Even rock would melt and be a red-hot liquid. In our time one would have to dig a shaft of about two thousand miles through the rock to get there and, of course, no one can do that. But some people who study these things say that in a far-away past, millions of years ago, you did not have to dig down to find this great heat in which even stones and rocks were flowing like water. They say that the surface of the earth, where we walk about now, was like that, was so hot that there were no rocks or stones. It was all a fiery-hot liquid. Now in time this surface of the earth began to cool down - at first only the outside, then a bit deeper down, and then still deeper down. As the outside surface slowly, very slowly, cooled down over thousands and thousands of years, it hardened - just as molten iron hardens when it cools down - and a hard skin, a hard crust formed on the surface of the earth. Now this first, hard, solid skin of the earth was granite.

在煉鋼廠裡，爐火產生的高溫能讓鐵熔化、像水一樣流動，變成白熱的液體。如果能挖得夠深，那裡的溫度會高到不再有堅硬的固態岩石。連岩石都會熔化，變成灼熱的液體。在我們的時代，要到達那裡得穿過岩石挖掘大約兩千英里深的通道，當然，沒有人做得到。但有些研究這些事情的人說，在遙遠的過去，數百萬年前，你不必往下挖就能找到那種連石頭和岩石都像水一樣流動的巨大高溫。他們說，地球的表面——我們現在走來走去的地方——曾經就是那個樣子，熱到沒有岩石或石頭，全是一片火熱的液體。後來，隨著時間推移，地球的表面開始冷卻——起初只有最外層，然後稍微深一點，再更深一點。當外面的表面在千千萬萬年間慢慢地、非常慢地冷卻下來，它就硬化了——就像熔化的鐵冷卻後會硬化一樣——一層堅硬的皮、一層堅硬的外殼在地球表面形成了。這第一層堅硬的、固態的地球表皮，就是花崗岩。


That is one way of explaining how granite came to be; it is called the "hot-earth" theory. But there are people who think differently, they prefer the "cold-earth" theory. They say it is not surprising that it is terribly hot in the depths down there: if you press with your hand hard on the desk, it will get quite hot - and so if all the heavy mountains and oceans and rocks press down, it must get hotter and hotter the deeper down you go. But, they say, this does not mean that it was ever so hot on the surface. Now these people say that the earth is not just a great dead chunk but is more like a living being. We know how, for example, shellfish -- crabs, lobsters, sea urchins, -- form a hard shell around themselves, well perhaps the earth could have formed a hard shell around itself, and that shell is granite.

這是解釋花崗岩如何形成的一種方式，它被稱為「熱地球」理論。但也有人想法不同，他們偏好「冷地球」理論。他們說，地底深處極其炎熱並不奇怪：如果你用手用力壓在桌面上，桌面會變得很熱——那麼如果所有沉重的山脈、海洋和岩石向下壓，越深就必然越熱。但是，他們說，這並不意味著地表曾經那樣炎熱。這些人認為，地球不只是一大塊死氣沉沉的東西，更像是一個活的生命體。我們知道，例如有殼的海洋動物——螃蟹、龍蝦、海膽——會在自己周圍形成堅硬的外殼，也許地球也在自己周圍形成了一層堅硬的外殼，而那層外殼就是花崗岩。


But the time when the first granite came into being is so terribly long ago that no one can say for certain how it was. Granite, that oldest of rocks, that mixture of three stones, is still keeping the secret of how it first came into existence.

但最初的花崗岩誕生的時間是如此遙遠久遠，沒有人能確切地說出它是怎麼形成的。花崗岩，這最古老的岩石，這三種石頭的混合物，至今仍保守著它最初如何誕生的秘密。


---

# 5. Volcanic Rocks
# 5. 火山岩

Think of a very high granite mountain. Its peak is so high up that it is forever winter, covered with ice and snow. But the granite goes on under the earth, deeper and deeper down, so far down that it comes to the terrible heat below where the rocks and metals are burning hot. The granite mountain reaches from the terrible heat below to the terrible cold above. But we living beings, humans and animals and plants, we live on the surface of the earth, just between the two extremes -- we live in between the terrible cold of the heights and the terrible heat of the depths. You see, life is always something that keeps to a middle path between the extremes of too much or too little. That is something to remember for our own life; that the middle path is the best.

想想一座非常高的花崗岩山。它的山峰高到永遠是冬天，覆蓋著冰雪。但花崗岩繼續在地底延伸，越來越深，深到觸及下方岩石和金屬燃燒般灼熱的可怕高溫。花崗岩山從下方可怕的高溫延伸到上方可怕的寒冷。但我們這些活的生命——人類、動物和植物——我們生活在地球表面，恰好介於兩個極端之間——我們生活在高處可怕的寒冷和深處可怕的炎熱之間。你看，生命總是在「太多」和「太少」兩個極端之間走一條中間的路。這是值得我們在自己的人生中記住的事：中間之道是最好的。


In some parts of the earth's crust -- not everywhere, only in certain places -- the heat is so great only a few miles down that the rock has melted and become a red-hot thick liquid. This molten rock is called magma and it forms an underground magma chamber. The magma can remain there for long times, but it does not always stay down in the depths. At certain places and at times which no one can foretell this magma comes spurting up from the depths. And it is always an awe-inspiring thing when this happens. Many years ago, magma came spurting out at one place. It had such a terrific strength that it forced a path, like a long pipeline, through the rock, through the soil and everything on top, then came spurting out through a big hole in the ground. It was fiery-hot, but in the cool air on the surface the magma soon cooled down and hardened. It hardened into stone, into rock. What remained was a little hill of hardened rock with a hole in the middle where the magma came out. The next time there was such a spurting of magma from the depths it did not force a new path; it came out where there was already a hole. So a new hill was formed on top of the old one, but the old hole still remained. The next time the same thing happened the hill grew and, in time, became a great mountain with a crater. The deep hole through which the eruptions come is called a crater -- the Greek word for a mixing-bowl.

在地殼的某些地方——不是到處都是，只在某些特定的地方——僅僅往下幾英里，熱度就已經大到岩石熔化，變成灼熱的濃稠液體。這種熔化的岩石叫做 magma（岩漿），它形成一個地下岩漿庫。岩漿可以在那裡停留很長時間，但它並不總是待在地底深處。在某些地方，在沒有人能預知的時刻，這些岩漿會從深處噴湧而出。每當這種事發生，總是令人敬畏的。很久以前，有個地方岩漿噴了出來。它有著極其巨大的力量，像一條長長的管道一樣，穿過岩石、穿過土壤和上面的一切，強行開出一條路，然後從地面上一個大洞噴湧而出。它灼熱無比，但在地表涼爽的空氣中，岩漿很快冷卻硬化了。它硬化成了石頭、岩石。留下的是一個硬化岩石的小山丘，中間有一個岩漿噴出的孔洞。下一次從深處噴出岩漿時，它不會另開新路，而是從已有的孔洞噴出。於是一座新的小丘在舊的上面形成了，但原來的孔洞仍然存在。再下一次，同樣的事情發生，小丘越來越大，最終變成了一座有火山口的巨大山峰。那個噴發通過的深孔叫做 crater（火山口）——這個詞來自希臘語，意思是「混合碗」。


Now the Romans had a god who was a metal-smith called Vulcan. He made the weapons for the other gods. They said, "As a human smith has a smithy where he heats iron until it is soft so that he can work on it, so this god has an enormous smithy, deep down in the earth. Magma comes from the smithy of this god Vulcan." The mountains formed by magma are called volcanoes after this god. So you see, a volcano is quite different from other mountains. A volcano is like a man who is quarrelsome, an ill-tempered person who does not get on with other people and so has to keep to himself; the mountain ranges on the other hand are like friends who stand together. Volcanoes are not formed by the slow process that forms mountain ranges but by sudden fiery outbursts called eruptions -- quite a different story!

羅馬人有一位金屬匠之神，名叫 Vulcan（伏爾坎）。他為其他眾神打造武器。人們說：「正如凡間的鐵匠有鍛造鋪，在那裡加熱鐵使它變軟以便加工，這位神也有一座巨大的鍛造鋪，在地底深處。岩漿就是從伏爾坎這位神的鍛造鋪裡來的。」由岩漿形成的山就以這位神的名字命名為 volcano（火山）。所以你看，火山和其他山脈是很不一樣的。火山就像一個愛爭吵、脾氣暴躁、和別人處不來因而只能獨來獨往的人；而山脈則像是站在一起的朋友。火山不是由形成山脈的那種緩慢過程造成的，而是由突然的、猛烈的爆發——稱為噴發——所形成的，完全是另一回事！


A volcanic eruption can be a fearful thing. First there is a deep rumbling noise from inside the earth, then a puff of steam, ash and smoke comes from the crater. Another deep rumbling comes and the earth is shaken for miles around. Then from the crater a fountain of fiery liquid erupts and runs down the mountain slope, like red-hot snakes. At the same time an enormous cloud of fiery smoke and ash forms above the volcano's peak. This cloud darkens the sky until it is dim as night, and a rain of ash falls down on the surrounding countryside for miles around. But this terrible, fiery-hot cloud can also come right down to earth, rolling down the mountain-side with unstoppable force and speed. When this happens it burns and destroys everything in its path; it can even destroy a whole town if it happens to be in the way.

火山噴發可以是一件可怕的事。首先是從地底傳來一陣深沉的隆隆聲，接著一團蒸汽、火山灰和煙霧從火山口冒出。又是一陣深沉的隆隆聲，方圓數英里的大地都在震動。然後從火山口噴出一道火熱液體的噴泉，沿著山坡流下，如同灼紅的蛇。同時，一團巨大的烈焰煙灰雲在火山頂上方形成。這片雲遮天蔽日，天色暗如黑夜，火山灰如雨般灑落在方圓數英里的鄉間。但這可怕的、灼熱的雲也可能直接撲向地面，以不可阻擋的力量和速度沿山坡滾滾而下。當這種情形發生時，它燒毀並摧毀沿途的一切；如果一座城鎮恰好擋在路上，甚至可能整個被毀掉。


The fiery stuff that comes from the crater and flows down like snakes is called lava. Lava is really the same as magma -- it is called magma when it is beneath the earth and lava when it comes out on the surface. After a while the lava cools enough to become solid rock. Often, as it cools and hardens, it forms big wrinkles on its surface, looking like piles of rope; this is called "ropy lava." From lava, different varieties of rock are formed. It can happen that the magma does not reach the surface; then, because it is deep in the earth, it cools down slowly and becomes basalt, the dark rock which also makes up the crust of the earth beneath the oceans. Then there is obsidian, a kind of natural glass that forms when lava cools quickly - it looks like dark bottle-glass and can be found in many colours. The Native Americans had not discovered the use of iron before Europeans came, but they made razor-sharp knives and arrowheads out of obsidian. Just as sea water foams or beer froths, so the liquid red-hot lava can also make a bubbling froth and when that hardens it becomes pumice, the stone you use to rub ink-stains off your fingers. It is a strange kind of stone -- full of bubbles and so light that it floats on water.

從火山口噴出、像蛇一樣流下的熾熱物質叫做 lava（熔岩）。熔岩其實和岩漿是同一樣東西——在地底叫岩漿，出了地表就叫熔岩。過了一段時間，熔岩冷卻到足以變成固態岩石。通常在冷卻硬化的過程中，表面會形成大皺褶，看起來像一堆繩子；這叫做「繩狀熔岩」。從熔岩中，形成了各種不同的岩石。有時候岩漿不會到達地表；那麼因為它深在地底，會慢慢冷卻，變成玄武岩——那種深色的岩石，同時也構成了海洋底下的地殼。還有 obsidian（黑曜石），一種天然玻璃，在熔岩快速冷卻時形成——看起來像深色的瓶玻璃，有多種顏色。美洲原住民在歐洲人到來之前還沒有發現鐵的用途，但他們用黑曜石製作鋒利無比的刀子和箭頭。就像海水會起泡沫、啤酒會冒泡一樣，灼熱的液態熔岩也會冒出泡沫，當那泡沫硬化後就變成了 pumice（浮石），就是你用來擦掉手指上墨漬的那種石頭。它是一種奇特的石頭——滿是氣泡，輕到能浮在水面上。


If a volcano erupts regularly it is called an active volcano. But a volcano can be quiet, without any eruptions for a hundred years or longer, and then it suddenly erupts again. A volcano that has not erupted for a long time but that -- one day - will erupt again, is called dormant, which means "sleeping." A volcano that is completely dead and will never erupt again is called an extinct volcano. As it happens, around Edinburgh there are a good many of these ancient volcanoes -- Arthur's Seat, the Castle Rock, Calton Hill and, farther to the east, Berwick Law and the Bass rock. They are all dead, extinct volcanoes - but once they were fire-spouting and active.

如果一座火山定期噴發，它就被稱為活火山。但火山也可以安靜下來，一百年甚至更久都不噴發，然後突然再度噴發。一座已經很久沒有噴發，但有朝一日會再度噴發的火山，被稱為 dormant（休眠的），意思是「沉睡中的」。一座完全死去、永遠不會再噴發的火山，被稱為 extinct volcano（死火山）。恰巧在愛丁堡周圍就有不少這類古老的火山——Arthur's Seat（亞瑟王座）、Castle Rock（城堡岩）、Calton Hill（卡爾頓山），以及更東邊的 Berwick Law（貝里克法）和 Bass Rock（巴斯岩）。它們全都是死了的、熄滅了的火山——但它們曾經噴火四射、活躍無比。


It is a strange thing to go up a volcano which is still active but, for the time being, not erupting -- like Mount Vesuvius, near Naples in Italy. On the lower slopes of the mountain are fields and vineyards, for volcanic soil is very rich. You walk further up on bleak, desolate slopes, raised in heaps like the waves of the sea -- it is all hardened lava. In many places you walk on a layer of clinker. Every now and then the ground under you trembles and a rumbling noise comes from the earth. It is a very tiring walk up but at long last you reach the top and you look down into the immense crater. It is like an enormous basin with sheer sides and you can see that it is made of layers of lava one on top of the other. In places there are wisps of steam and there is the constant sound of small stones falling down into the crater. You climb down a short way into the big crater of Vesuvius. The walls are hot to the touch: the heat of the earth. As you get down into the crater little lizards run away in different directions; they like the warmth in the crater.

攀登一座仍然活躍但暫時沒有噴發的火山，是一件奇妙的事——比如義大利 Naples（那不勒斯）附近的 Mount Vesuvius（維蘇威火山）。在山的低坡是田野和葡萄園，因為火山土壤非常肥沃。再往上走，是荒涼、蕭條的山坡，堆疊起伏如海浪——全是硬化的熔岩。很多地方你走在一層爐渣上。不時地，腳下的地面顫動，一陣隆隆聲從大地中傳來。往上走非常累人，但終於你到達了山頂，俯瞰那巨大的火山口。它像一個巨大的盆地，壁面陡峭，你可以看到它是由一層又一層的熔岩堆疊而成。有些地方飄著絲絲蒸汽，小石頭不斷落入火山口的聲音持續不斷。你順著維蘇威火山的大火山口往下爬了一小段。岩壁摸起來是熱的：這是大地的溫度。當你走進火山口時，小蜥蜴四散奔逃；牠們喜歡火山口裡的溫暖。


Throughout history Vesuvius has erupted many times, but the most famous eruption was around two thousand years ago. About 10 km or 6 miles from Vesuvius (quite a long way!) lay the wealthy Roman town of Pompeii. In the summer of AD 79 a great eruption of the volcano threw up huge quantities of smoke and ash high into the sky. Day was turned into night and a heavy rain of ash came down until the town was completely buried. In our time it has been dug up again, revealing a lot about life in Roman times (it is said that the science of archaeology was born in the ruins of Pompeii). It is fascinating to visit Pompeii and walk around the streets of the ancient town.

在整個歷史上，維蘇威火山噴發了很多次，但最著名的一次噴發是大約兩千年前。距維蘇威火山約十公里或六英里遠（相當遠的距離！）的地方，有一座富裕的羅馬城鎮 Pompeii（龐貝）。在西元七十九年的夏天，火山的一次大噴發將巨量的煙塵和火山灰拋向高空。白晝變成了黑夜，一場濃重的火山灰雨不斷降下，直到整座城鎮被完全掩埋。在我們的時代，它被重新挖掘出來，揭示了許多關於羅馬時代生活的資訊（據說考古學這門科學就誕生在龐貝的廢墟中）。造訪龐貝、漫步在這座古城的街道上，是一件令人著迷的事。


In some other volcanoes -- as on the Hawaiian Islands -- you discover that there is almost continuous but much less violent activity. Inside the big crater there is liquid lava that spurts up in a red fountain - especially at night it is a spectacular sight. The fountain can be quite high, thirty metres (100 ft) or so and it throws out red-hot drops of lava that harden quickly once they are out and fall as "bombs." Again you feel the trembling of the earth and hear the rumbling below. Here and there you can see patches of yellow sulphur around the cracks where steam is coming out of the ground and there is a pungent smell in the air. When you see and hear and smell this, then you know that one does not have to dig deep down to reach the magma below the earth -- in a volcano it is as if the inside of the earth comes up to the surface.

在其他一些火山——比如 Hawaiian Islands（夏威夷群島）上的——你會發現那裡幾乎持續不斷但暴烈程度低得多的活動。在大火山口裡面，有液態的熔岩噴射成一道紅色的噴泉——尤其在夜晚，那是一幅壯觀的景象。噴泉可以相當高，大約三十公尺（一百英尺）左右，它噴出灼紅的熔岩水滴，一噴出就迅速硬化，以「火山彈」的形式落下。你再次感受到大地的顫動，聽到地底的隆隆聲。到處可以看到裂縫周圍有一片片黃色的硫磺，蒸汽從地面冒出，空氣中瀰漫著刺鼻的氣味。當你看到、聽到、嗅到這一切的時候，你就知道，不必往地底深挖就能觸及地底的岩漿——在火山裡，就彷彿大地的內部升到了地表。
# 6. The Restless Earth
# 6. 不安分的大地

If you visit the seaside town of Pozzuoli (a suburb of Naples, not far from Vesuvius) you are at another place where you can see and feel that the activity of the earth comes near the surface. On the edge of town is the Solfatara. When you approach this place, you will probably smell it before you see it, for there is an unpleasant smell, like rotten eggs. The Solfatara is a large shallow crater full of light coloured sand, but in places there is steam hissing furiously from the ground, as if there were great kettles boiling just below the surface. Around the steaming vents are puddles of spitting, boiling mud and there are coloured deposits of sulphur and other minerals, most of them very poisonous. If someone throws down a ball of lighted paper, the ground in that place "answers" with its own smoke and steam; it can be so strong a reaction that you are surrounded by a cloud of it. At times it gets so active that it has to be closed off because the fumes are too dangerous. It almost feels as if the earth there is showing its anger.

如果你造訪海濱小鎮 Pozzuoli（波佐利）——它是 Naples（那不勒斯）的一個郊區，離 Vesuvius（維蘇威火山）不遠——你就來到了另一個可以親眼看見、親身感受到大地活動逼近地表的地方。在城鎮邊緣有一處名為 Solfatara（索爾法塔拉）的地方。當你走近時，很可能還沒看到它，就先聞到了——那裡瀰漫著一股像臭雞蛋般令人不舒服的氣味。索爾法塔拉是一個寬闊的淺火山口，滿是淡色的沙子，但有些地方蒸氣正猛烈地從地底嘶嘶噴出，彷彿地面下方就有巨大的水壺在沸騰。蒸氣噴口周圍是一灘灘啪啪作響、翻滾沸騰的泥漿，還有五顏六色的硫磺和其他礦物沉積物，其中大部分都有劇毒。如果有人丟下一團點燃的紙球，那個地方的地面就會用自己的煙霧和蒸氣來「回應」；反應可以強烈到讓你整個人被一團煙霧包圍。有時候它變得太活躍了，不得不封閉起來，因為噴出的氣體太危險了。那裡的大地幾乎讓人感覺，它正在展示自己的怒氣。


We have looked at the great changes, the complete transformations, that have come about over long periods of time. The whole "face of the earth" is in slow but powerful movement. Not only the dry land is going through such movements which after thousands and thousands of years produce mountains and valleys. The sea-bed, the solid rock under the sea, rises in places and so the sea-bed that used to be underwater comes up and becomes dry land. And the opposite also happens: dry land sinks down becoming the sea-bed.

我們已經看過那些經歷漫長歲月才產生的巨大變化、徹底的轉變。整個「大地的面容」都在緩慢卻強大地運動著。不只是陸地在經歷這樣的運動——經過成千上萬年後造就了山脈和谷地。海床，也就是海洋之下的堅硬岩石，在某些地方隆起，於是原本沉在水下的海床升上來，變成了乾燥的陸地。相反的事情也會發生：陸地下沉，成為海床。


On the other side of Pozzuoli are the remains of an ancient Roman building, the so-called Temple of Serapis. Not far from the sea there are three tall marble columns, still standing today where they have stood for about two thousand years. If you look more closely at these columns, there is something rather strange about them. About 4 metres (12 ft) from the base of the columns there is a band of discolouration and roughening of the marble. What can have caused this damage? The surprising answer is that the columns are pitted with holes made by a kind of shell fish which lives only in the sea. Now this shellfish could only have made its marks under the water, so the pillars must have been deep in the sea, and then came out of it again. It means that the sea bottom went down, then it rose again — and this may have happened more than once. At present the marks on the pillars are roughly 7 m (24 ft) above sea-level, — yet this is not fixed, there is always a slow change going on.

在波佐利的另一邊，有一座古羅馬建築的遺跡，人們稱之為 Temple of Serapis（塞拉匹斯神殿）。離海不遠處有三根高大的大理石柱，至今仍矗立在它們站了大約兩千年的地方。如果你更仔細地觀察這些石柱，會發現它們有些相當奇怪的地方。在石柱底部往上大約四公尺（十二英尺）處，有一條大理石變色、變得粗糙的帶狀區域。是什麼造成了這種損壞？令人驚訝的答案是：石柱上佈滿了一種只生活在海裡的貝類所鑽出的孔洞。這種貝類只有在水下才能留下痕跡，所以這些石柱一定曾經深深沒入海中，然後又再度露出來。這意味著海底曾經下沉，然後又升了起來——而且這可能不只發生過一次。目前石柱上的痕跡大約在海平面以上七公尺（二十四英尺）處——但這並不是固定的，緩慢的變化一直在進行著。


But these up-and-down movements of the earth can also be sudden. In 1984 there were earthquakes in the area and afterwards it was found that the sea bottom at Pozzuoli had come up by nearly 2 m (6 ft), making the bay too shallow for big ships. So in this part of Italy the earth is more restless, rising and sinking faster than in other places.

但是大地的這些上下運動也可能是突然的。一九八四年，該地區發生了地震，之後人們發現波佐利的海底上升了將近兩公尺（六英尺），使得海灣變得太淺，大船無法通行。所以在義大利的這個地方，大地更加不安分，升降的速度比其他地方都快。


The so-called Temple of Serapis, Pozzuoli, was actually a market place.

所謂的波佐利「塞拉匹斯神殿」，其實是一座市場。


# 7. Some Different Rocks
# 7. 各種不同的岩石

One could say that in granite you see the good temper of the earth, the love of the earth. In volcanic eruptions, in volcanoes, you see the bad temper of the earth, the anger of the earth. It may well be that the great, terrible eruptions and earthquakes — not the slight rumbling which goes on in some parts of the world all the time — are outbursts of bad temper from the earth over the evil things done by people on earth. The earth wants us to be like granite — wise, strong-willed, kind; but if there is much evil in the world then sooner or later the earth will burst out with bad temper, to show that it is annoyed.

可以這麼說：在花崗岩裡，你看到的是大地的好脾氣，大地的愛。在火山爆發中、在火山裡，你看到的是大地的壞脾氣，大地的怒氣。那些巨大而可怕的噴發和地震——不是世界上某些地方一直在發生的輕微隆隆聲——很可能是大地對人們在地球上所做的壞事發的脾氣。大地希望我們像花崗岩一樣——智慧、意志堅定、善良；但如果世界上有太多邪惡，那麼遲早大地會發一場脾氣，來表示它的不滿。


Basalt, the dark-coloured relative of granite, sometimes shows another side of its nature. When you look at Arthur's Seat in Edinburgh you can see Samson's Ribs — great curving columns of rock that look like the ribs of an enormous giant. These basalt columns are not round, they have a hexagonal form — they have six flat faces, like giant crystals. Another place where you can see these basalt columns is on the little island of Staffa in the Inner Hebrides, in the famous Fingal's Cave that is like a vast natural cathedral. When the great musician Felix Mendelssohn visited Staffa he was so moved by the sight of the towering columns and by the strange echoes inside the cave that he wrote a wonderful piece of music — it is known as the Fingal's Cave Overture. Painters and poets have also been inspired by it. In Northern Ireland there is another natural wonder, the Giant's Causeway, that is also made of these hexagonal basalt columns. Long ago Fingal's Cave and the Giant's Causeway were connected; they were once part of a huge lava flow that happened millions of years ago. It is hard to imagine such a gigantic lava flow happening — no lava flow today is so huge.

玄武岩，花崗岩那深色的親戚，有時會展現它性格的另一面。當你在 Edinburgh（愛丁堡）觀看 Arthur's Seat（亞瑟王座）時，可以看到 Samson's Ribs（參孫之肋）——巨大的弧形岩柱，看起來就像一個龐大巨人的肋骨。這些玄武岩柱並不是圓的，而是六角形的——它們有六個平面，就像巨大的晶體。另一個可以看到這些玄武岩柱的地方，是在 Inner Hebrides（內赫布里底群島）的小島 Staffa（斯塔法島）上，那裡有著名的 Fingal's Cave（芬格爾洞穴），宛如一座巨大的天然大教堂。偉大的音樂家 Felix Mendelssohn（孟德爾頌）造訪斯塔法島時，被那些高聳的岩柱和洞穴裡奇特的回聲深深打動，寫下了一首美妙的樂曲——人們稱之為《乘格爾洞穴序曲》。畫家和詩人也同樣深受啟發。在北愛爾蘭還有另一個自然奇觀—— Giant's Causeway（巨人堤道），也是由這些六角形玄武岩柱構成的。很久以前，芬格爾洞穴和巨人堤道曾經相連；它們曾是數百萬年前一次巨大熔岩流的一部分。很難想像如此巨大的熔岩流——今天沒有任何熔岩流能達到那樣的規模。


The dark rock, basalt, is dark because it contains iron. But it also contains another metal called magnesium. We have iron in our blood, it is iron that gives our blood its red colour. But magnesium is just as important for the plants — it is magnesium that gives them their green colour and their ability to take in sunlight. Earlier we wondered what lies below the earth's crust, below the granite of the continental crust and below the basalt of the ocean crust. Sometimes this deep rock comes to the surface through volcanic activity, and it is also a rock that contains iron and magnesium, these essentials of life.

深色的岩石——玄武岩——之所以深色，是因為它含有鐵。但它也含有另一種叫做鎂的金屬。我們的血液裡有鐵，正是鐵賦予了血液紅色。但鎂對植物同樣重要——正是鎂賦予了植物綠色，以及吸收陽光的能力。前面我們曾好奇，在地殼之下，在大陸地殼的花崗岩之下，在海洋地殼的玄武岩之下，到底是什麼。有時候，這些深層的岩石會透過火山活動來到地表，而它同樣是一種含有鐵和鎂的岩石——這些生命不可或缺的元素。


But there are many other substances in the rocks and there are many other different kinds of rocks. In the crust of the earth there is abundant feldspar; and feldspar contains calcium. We all have calcium in us because it is calcium that builds our bones and makes them strong. Calcium is also found in the shells of sea creatures, crabs, sea-urchins, molluscs. This brings us to a kind of rock that was made in a quite different way to granite or basalt.

但岩石中還有許多其他物質，也有許多其他不同種類的岩石。在地殼中有大量的長石；而長石含有鈣。我們每個人體內都有鈣，因為正是鈣構建了我們的骨骼並使之堅固。鈣也存在於海洋生物的外殼中——螃蟹、海膽、軟體動物的殼裡都有。這就帶我們來到一種以截然不同於花崗岩或玄武岩的方式形成的岩石。


Imagine a shallow tropical sea that existed long ago, many things live in it — fish, corals, shell-fish. Floating in this sea, making it slightly cloudy, are millions of very tiny creatures with beautiful white shells. When these tiny animals lived their lives and died, they sank to the bottom of the sea and their shells made a kind of chalky ooze. This went on for hundreds or thousands of years so that great heaps of these shells made a thick covering on the bottom of the sea. Over time these heaps were pressed down so much that they became a kind of rock called chalk which is a soft variety of limestone. So chalk and limestone begin life at the bottom of the sea.

想像一片很久以前存在的淺熱帶海洋，裡面住著很多生物——魚、珊瑚、貝類。漂浮在這片海中，讓海水微微混濁的，是數以百萬計極其微小的生物，牠們有著美麗的白色外殼。當這些微小的動物過完一生、死去之後，牠們沉到海底，牠們的外殼形成了一種白堊般的軟泥。這樣的過程持續了數百年甚至數千年，大量的外殼在海底堆積成一層厚厚的覆蓋物。隨著時間推移，這些堆積物被壓得越來越緊實，終於變成了一種叫做白堊的岩石，它是石灰岩中較軟的一種。所以，白堊和石灰岩的生命，是從海底開始的。


The White Cliffs of Dover, the Downs and the Cheddar Caves in the South of England are all made of limestone. And limestone is a very widespread rock — it can be found making high mountains like the Jura — and it can be found deep under the ground over large areas of Europe and other parts of the world. But these hard limestone rocks were originally made by little sea creatures — you could say that limestone is a kind of animal-rock. So, although the limestone rocks we see now are lifeless, they were formed originally by living creatures.

英格蘭南部的 White Cliffs of Dover（多佛白崖）、Downs（丘陵地）和 Cheddar Caves（切達洞穴）都是石灰岩構成的。石灰岩是一種分布非常廣泛的岩石——它可以形成像 Jura（侏羅山脈）那樣的高山——也可以在歐洲和世界其他地方的大片地區深深埋藏在地下。但這些堅硬的石灰岩，原本是由小小的海洋生物造就的——你可以說，石灰岩是一種「動物岩石」。所以，雖然我們現在看到的石灰岩是沒有生命的，但它們最初是由活生生的生物所形成的。


We may not think it makes much difference to people whether they live on granite or limestone, but there is a difference. People living near granite feel more awake, feel more strength in their limbs, feel more active, and want to do things. But those living in limestone country feel more dreamy, and not so energetic. Some people prefer one, some the other.

我們可能覺得人們住在花崗岩地區還是石灰岩地區沒什麼差別，但其實是有差別的。住在花崗岩附近的人會覺得更清醒，四肢更有力量，更活躍，想要做事情。而住在石灰岩地區的人則會覺得更夢幻，沒有那麼精力充沛。有些人偏愛這種感覺，有些人偏愛那種。


# 8. More about Limestone
# 8. 更多關於石灰岩的故事

Just think of the different ways that rocks and mountains form. Limestone mountains, which are made of millions of tiny shells pressed together, have come about in a quite different way to volcanoes. Now they are both part of the hard crust of the earth, but volcanoes have their origin, their beginning in fire and limestone mountains have their origin in water. You remember the four elements: fire, air, water, earth; each has its part to play in forming the world around us.

想一想岩石和山脈形成的不同方式。石灰岩山脈，由數以百萬計的微小外殼壓在一起而成，它的形成方式和火山截然不同。現在它們都是堅硬地殼的一部分，但火山的起源、它的開端在於火，而石灰岩山脈的起源在於水。你還記得四大元素嗎：火、空氣、水、土；每一種都在塑造我們周圍的世界中扮演著自己的角色。


The White Cliffs of Dover were originally formed at the bottom of the sea, but now they stand high over it — so how is limestone found far above sea level? As our chest goes up and down when we breathe, so the earth can sometimes rise slowly and then go down — but it may go down in one place and in another it may go up. In some places the sea-bed has risen up and become land (as we saw with the Temple of Serapis near Naples). The sea-shell rocks now stand on dry land as hills such as the Pennines (limestone) or the Downs (chalk). And this "breathing of the earth" happened not only here in Britain; large parts of Europe, America, Africa which are now dry land were at one time seas.

多佛白崖原本是在海底形成的，但現在它們高高矗立在海面之上——那麼石灰岩怎麼會出現在遠高於海平面的地方呢？就像我們呼吸時胸腔會上下起伏一樣，大地有時也會緩慢地升起，然後再下沉——但它可能在一個地方下沉，在另一個地方卻升起。有些地方，海床升了上來變成了陸地（就像我們在那不勒斯附近的塞拉匹斯神殿所看到的那樣）。那些由海洋貝殼構成的岩石，現在以丘陵的形態矗立在乾燥的陸地上，像是 Pennines（奔寧山脈，石灰岩）或 Downs（丘陵地，白堊）。而大地的這種「呼吸」不僅僅發生在英國；歐洲、美洲、非洲的大片地區，那些現在是乾燥陸地的地方，曾經一度都是海洋。


And limestone can be found much higher than the Pennines. It is an important part of the Alps and it is at the top of the highest mountains of all, the Himalaya. It seems strange that you can find the remains of ancient sea-shells high up above the clouds in these mountains. But there is another reason for this. When the earth makes a new, young mountain range, it uses rocks which are already there. Limestone was among the rocks which were already there — it was already quite old when these young mountains were formed — and so it was taken up in the great squeezing and folding that formed the Alps and Himalayas.

而且石灰岩可以出現在比奔寧山脈高得多的地方。它是 Alps（阿爾卑斯山）的重要組成部分，也出現在世界最高山脈—— Himalaya（喜馬拉雅山）的山頂。在這些山峰雲端之上找到古老海洋貝殼的遺跡，看起來確實很奇怪。但這背後還有另一個原因。當大地造出一條新的、年輕的山脈時，它會利用已經存在的岩石。石灰岩就是那些早已存在的岩石之一——在這些年輕山脈形成時，它已經相當古老了——因此它被捲入了形成阿爾卑斯山和喜馬拉雅山的巨大擠壓與褶皺之中。


Limestone was formed in warm tropical seas, but it can be found in all the different climates of the world, not just in the tropics. The sea around Dover is certainly not tropical — so how did limestone come to form there at all? Not only can the land rise and fall above or below the sea, it also moves across the face of the earth. A land that was once freezing cold might now be a hot desert, or a place that was once a tropical sea might now be somewhere far to the north with a cold climate. As the continents slowly move on the face of the world, everything changes.

石灰岩是在溫暖的熱帶海洋中形成的，但它卻可以在世界上各種不同的氣候中被找到，不僅僅在熱帶。多佛附近的海洋顯然不是熱帶的——那麼石灰岩究竟是怎麼在那裡形成的呢？陸地不僅能在海平面上下升降，它還會在地球表面上移動。一塊曾經冰天雪地的土地，現在可能是炎熱的沙漠；一個曾經是熱帶海洋的地方，現在可能位於遙遠的北方，有著寒冷的氣候。隨著大陸在地球表面緩慢地移動，一切都在改變。


These rocks and mountains that came from water differ among themselves very much in hardness. It depends how hard they were pressed down and how well the little shells were stuck together. Chalk is the softest — it crumbles, as we know, very easily. Limestone is harder and does not crumble so easily. Marble, the beautiful white stone from which the Greeks and Romans made their statues and their gleaming white temples is also a kind of limestone, but it has changed. During the slow movements of the earth, limestone can sometimes be pushed deep underground (some rocks are pushed up and others are pushed down). Down there in the earth the limestone was heated so much that later, when it came to the surface again, it had been transformed into beautiful crystalline marble. But limestone and marble are not always white, they can become mixed with other substances — sand, clay, plant-remains — and these mixtures cause many beautiful colours and patterns in the marble.

這些從水中誕生的岩石和山脈，彼此之間的硬度差異很大。這取決於它們被壓得有多緊，以及那些小小的外殼黏合得有多好。白堊是最軟的——如我們所知，它非常容易碎裂。石灰岩更硬，不那麼容易碎裂。大理石，那種希臘人和羅馬人用來雕刻雕像、建造閃耀白色神殿的美麗白色石材，其實也是一種石灰岩，只是它發生了變化。在大地緩慢的運動過程中，石灰岩有時會被推到地底深處（有些岩石被推上去，有些則被推下來）。在地底深處，石灰岩被加熱到如此高的溫度，以至於後來，當它再度回到地表時，已經被轉化成了美麗的結晶大理石。但石灰岩和大理石並不總是白色的，它們可能會與其他物質混合——沙子、黏土、植物殘骸——而這些混合物造就了大理石中許多美麗的色彩和紋理。


But all these rocks and mountains that came from the sea, even the hardest of them, are softer than granite or basalt. Wind and water can gnaw and nibble at them more easily than at the harder stones. That is why limestone rocks often take on strange shapes: they may look like castles or knights. And limestone can, slowly, dissolve in rainwater. Rain soaks deep down into the ground and in the limestone regions of the world there are all kinds of underground streams and tunnels, fantastic caverns with stalagmites and stalactites, and even underground lakes. Some people, called potholers, love to spend their time exploring these strange and wonderful — but sometimes also dangerous — underground worlds.

但所有這些從海洋中誕生的岩石和山脈，即使是其中最硬的，也比花崗岩或玄武岩來得軟。風和水能更容易地啃咬、侵蝕它們，比對付那些更堅硬的石頭要容易得多。這就是為什麼石灰岩常常呈現奇特的形狀：它們可能看起來像城堡或騎士。而且石灰岩可以慢慢地溶解在雨水中。雨水深深滲入地下，在世界上的石灰岩地區，有各種各樣的地下河流和隧道、有石筍和鐘乳石的奇幻洞穴，甚至還有地下湖泊。有些人被稱為「洞穴探險者」，他們喜歡花時間去探索這些奇妙而美麗——但有時也很危險——的地下世界。


Limestone is also very useful to us; it is used a lot as a building stone. The pyramids of Egypt and the Houses of Parliament in London are both made of limestone. It is also used in making important modern building materials: cement and concrete. Altogether limestone is one of our most essential building materials, and your own strong bones are really a kind of living limestone. You see how every kind of rock has its own story.

石灰岩對我們也非常有用；它被大量用作建築石材。埃及的金字塔和倫敦的國會大廈都是石灰岩建造的。它還被用來製造重要的現代建築材料：水泥和混凝土。總的來說，石灰岩是我們最不可或缺的建築材料之一，而你自己堅強的骨骼，其實就是一種活的石灰岩。你看，每一種岩石都有它自己的故事。


# 9. Coal
# 9. 煤

Limestone is a kind of "animal rock" because it is made of the shells of sea animals. You can also find some kinds of limestone which started out as ancient coral reefs. (Coral is also an animal, even though it looks a bit like a plant — with some of these ancient life-forms it is not always easy to tell plants from animals.) Is there also a kind of rock made from the remains of plants? Yes, there is, it is the black rock which we know as coal.

石灰岩是一種「動物岩石」，因為它是由海洋動物的外殼構成的。你也可以找到一些石灰岩，它們最初是古老的珊瑚礁。（珊瑚也是動物，儘管它看起來有點像植物——對於這些古老的生命形態，要分辨植物和動物並不總是容易的。）那麼，有沒有一種岩石是由植物遺骸構成的呢？有的，那就是我們所知的黑色岩石——煤。


We burn coal in our power stations by the millions of tons because the heat given out by the burning coal can be changed into electricity — and we need this electric power to keep our modern world running. There are other ways of making electricity, but we still depend on coal to make the huge amounts of electricity that we need. But we have also learned that if we burn too much coal it is a bad thing — the burning of the coal changes the air: it increases the carbon dioxide and that causes changes to the climate. This is one of the problems of the present day and also of the future.

我們在發電廠裡燃燒數百萬噸的煤，因為煤燃燒釋放的熱量可以轉化為電力——而我們需要這些電力來維持現代世界的運轉。還有其他發電的方式，但我們仍然依賴煤來生產我們所需的大量電力。然而我們也已經認識到，如果燃燒太多的煤，那是一件壞事——煤的燃燒改變了空氣：它增加了二氧化碳，而二氧化碳導致氣候變化。這是當今以及未來的問題之一。


Of course plants are mainly green, so why is coal black? If you look at a compost heap, you will see that when plants have died and turn into compost, they first go brown and then black; by then they have become good "humus" for the soil. Or think of a piece of charcoal, it is made of wood which has been charred, but not completely burnt to ash. The black colour of charcoal is a substance called carbon — and all living things, both plant and animal, contain carbon. The best quality coal is nearly pure carbon, but this carbon was once part of living plants.

當然，植物主要是綠色的，那麼煤為什麼是黑色的呢？如果你看一個堆肥堆，你會發現當植物死去、變成堆肥時，它們先是變成褐色，然後變成黑色；到那時候它們就成了良好的土壤「腐殖質」了。或者想想一塊木炭，它是由木頭經過燒焦、但沒有完全燒成灰燼而製成的。木炭的黑色來自一種叫做碳的物質——所有的生物，無論是植物還是動物，都含有碳。最好品質的煤幾乎是純碳，但這些碳曾經是活生生的植物的一部分。


But what sort of plants were they and how did they become coal? Just as there was a time in the history of the earth when huge amounts of chalk were created, so there was an even earlier time — the carboniferous time — when huge amounts of coal were formed. (These were not the only times when limestone and coal were made, but they were the main ones.) In those days there were great forests, not just here or there, but covering large parts of the earth. These forests were not like the ones we know today, the plants that grew in them looked different. Today we have ferns and horsetails but in the carboniferous time there was a much greater variety of ferns and horsetails, many of them were big trees, and there were other strange trees, not much like anything we have today. Nowadays there are still some tree-ferns, but the trees we know so well — oak, ash, sycamore, birch — did not yet exist in those days. Not only that, but there were no flowering plants at all — they had not yet come into existence — there was not a single flower anywhere in the world. So the hot swampy forests of the carboniferous time would have seemed very strange to us.

但那是什麼樣的植物？它們又是怎麼變成煤的？就像在地球歷史上有一個時期形成了大量的白堊一樣，還有一個更早的時期——石炭紀——形成了大量的煤。（這些並不是石灰岩和煤形成的唯一時期，但是最主要的時期。）在那個年代，有大片的森林，不只是零星分布，而是覆蓋了地球的大片區域。這些森林不像我們今天所知道的森林，生長在其中的植物看起來很不一樣。今天我們有蕨類和木賊，但在石炭紀，蕨類和木賊的種類豐富得多，其中許多是大樹，還有其他奇怪的樹木，和我們今天所見的很不一樣。如今仍然有一些樹蕨存在，但我們非常熟悉的那些樹——橡樹、梣樹、楓樹、樺樹——在那個年代還不存在。不僅如此，根本沒有任何開花植物——它們還沒有出現——全世界沒有一朵花。所以石炭紀那些炎熱潮濕的沼澤森林，對我們來說會顯得非常奇怪。


How did these swampy, peaty forests become the coal-seams which we can dig up today? It is always difficult to be sure about what happened so long ago, but it seems that the sea-level changed many times. The sea rose until large parts of the forest were completely flooded and lay under water. On the sea-bed the plants died and lay in heaps, getting slowly covered by layers of mud or sand or shells. The plant remains were pushed down by the weight of the water and the layers of mud above them until they were squeezed together and formed a thick black layer, sandwiched by mud above and below. Eventually the sea-level fell again, leaving muddy, sandy land with no plants growing on it. But soon new seeds fell in the mud; plants began to grow and — in time — there was a whole new forest, just as big as the old one.

這些潮濕泥濘的沼澤森林是怎麼變成我們今天可以挖掘的煤層的？對於那麼久遠的事情，總是很難確定到底發生了什麼，但看起來海平面曾經多次變化。海水上升，直到大片森林被完全淹沒，沉在水下。在海底，植物死亡並堆積成堆，慢慢被一層層泥沙或貝殼覆蓋。植物遺骸被上方水和泥層的重量壓下去，直到它們被擠壓在一起，形成一層厚厚的黑色地層，上下都被泥沙夾住。最終海平面再度下降，留下沒有植物生長的泥濘沙地。但很快新的種子落入泥中；植物開始生長，隨著時間推移，一片全新的森林出現了，和舊的一樣廣闊。


More time passed and the sea came up again, drowning the new forest and making a new layer of black plant-remains at the bottom of the sea. This slow rhythm of land, sea, land, sea, went on for millions of years until there were many layers, one above the other. You can find 40 seams of coal (or even more in some places) with sandstone or limestone in between. These repeated layers in the crust of the earth are a bit like the growth-rings in the wood of a tree, they are formed by the slow, rhythmic ebb and flow of life. And, like the growth rings, the layers are all slightly different; some are thinner and some are thicker. But there are two big differences.

更多的時間過去了，海水再度上升，淹沒了新的森林，在海底形成新一層黑色的植物遺骸。這種陸地、海洋、陸地、海洋的緩慢節奏，持續了數百萬年，直到形成了許多層，一層疊著一層。你可以找到四十層煤層（有些地方甚至更多），中間夾著砂岩或石灰岩。地殼中這些重複的地層，有點像樹木木頭中的年輪，它們是由生命緩慢而有節奏的漲落形成的。而且，就像年輪一樣，這些地層各不相同；有些薄一些，有些厚一些。但有兩個大的區別。


Firstly, the layers of the rock are far bigger than tree-rings, 3 metres (10 feet) is not unusual and some are much thicker. Secondly, one tree-ring is made in one year, but the layers in the earth are made very slowly — thousands and thousands of years for each one. We are used to living with only two rhythms of planet earth — the day and the year — but there are other, much longer, rhythms too. There is an important one (precession) which lasts about 26,000 years — you will hear about it when we study astronomy. There are other, even longer rhythms in the life of planet earth: 40,000 years, 100,000 years. It may be that these are the very slow rhythms which have left their mark in the coal measures.

首先，岩石的地層遠比年輪大得多，三公尺（十英尺）厚並不罕見，有些還要厚得多。其次，一個年輪是一年之內形成的，但地層中的每一層卻是極其緩慢形成的——每一層要經歷成千上萬年。我們習慣了地球上只有兩種節奏——日與年——但還有其他更長久的節奏。有一個重要的節奏（歲差）大約持續兩萬六千年——等我們學天文學時你會聽到它。在地球的生命中還有其他更長的節奏：四萬年、十萬年。也許正是這些極其緩慢的節奏，在煤田中留下了它們的印記。


There are also different kinds of coal, depending on how much the coal seam has been pressed down by the layers above. The coal which is found very deep in the earth has been pressed down hardest, it has also been heated most and it is the best kind of coal. It is called anthracite — it gives better heat and it burns cleanly, without much smoke — but it is difficult to get at it, and so it is scarce. Most coal is of a type known as bituminous; it has not been pressed down so much so it is softer — and it burns with a smoky flame. The softest coal is dark brown; it is called lignite and it is like peat which has been compressed.

煤也有不同的種類，取決於煤層被上方地層壓得有多緊。在地球深處發現的煤被壓得最緊，也被加熱得最厲害，是品質最好的煤。它被稱為無煙煤——它提供更好的熱量，燃燒得很乾淨，幾乎沒有煙——但很難開採到它，所以很稀少。大部分的煤是一種叫做煙煤的類型；它沒有被壓得那麼緊，所以比較軟——燃燒時會冒出煙霧繚繞的火焰。最軟的煤是深褐色的，叫做褐煤，就像被壓縮過的泥炭一樣。


Finally, why does coal contain so much power — why is it that we can use the heat and power of coal, but not any other kind of rock which we dig from the ground? It is because the plants in those ancient forests soaked up a little of the heat and power that streamed down on them from the sun. In coal some of the heat and power of the sun are "locked up." And when the coal is set on fire it is actually the warmth of the sun which is released from its long "enchantment" in the black rock.

最後，為什麼煤蘊含著這麼大的力量——為什麼我們可以利用煤的熱能和動力，卻不能利用從地下挖出的其他任何岩石呢？那是因為那些遠古森林中的植物，吸收了一點點從太陽傾瀉而下的熱和力量。在煤裡，太陽的一些熱和力量被「鎖」了起來。當煤被點燃時，實際上釋放出來的，是太陽的溫暖——它從黑色岩石中漫長的「沉睡」裡被喚醒了。


It is really the same with each one of us — inside each one of us there are hidden powers, gifts or talents, which can be released if something "sets us on fire." All we need is to be open for the hidden powers and potential in ourselves and in others.

其實我們每一個人也是如此——在我們每個人的內心深處，都隱藏著力量、天賦或才能，只要有什麼東西「點燃」了我們，它們就能被釋放出來。我們所需要做的，就是對自己和他人內在隱藏的力量和潛能保持開放。


# 10. The Work of Water
# 10. 水的工作

We have heard how mountains and rocks came into existence, but nothing in the world stays as it is. Mountains are "born" and they "pass away" as we do. All things change; and even the most mighty and ancient mountains of the world change; and what changes them more than anything else is water.

我們已經聽過山脈和岩石是如何誕生的，但世界上沒有任何事物能永遠保持原樣。山脈會「誕生」，也會像我們一樣「消逝」。萬物都在變化；即使是世界上最雄偉、最古老的山脈也在變化；而改變它們最多的，莫過於水。


Think of a big rock. Like all rocks, it is full of tiny cracks. In the rain the tiny cracks fill with water. When the cold winter comes the water in the cracks freezes and turns into ice. It's a strange thing, but when water turns into ice it expands, it grows bigger — and it does so with an enormous, unstoppable force. With such a force the crack is widened. In summer the ice melts, but sooner or later it freezes again and, after this has happened many times, the crack is so big that a bit of rock breaks off. You can often see scree in the mountains — a slope of loose rubble and stones. All these stones of the scree have been broken off from the big rocks by the freezing and thawing of water.

想像一塊大岩石。像所有岩石一樣，它佈滿了微小的裂縫。下雨時，這些微小的裂縫灌滿了水。當寒冷的冬天來臨，裂縫中的水結凍變成冰。這是一件奇妙的事：當水變成冰時，它會膨脹，變得更大——而且它以一種巨大的、不可阻擋的力量這樣做。帶著這樣的力量，裂縫被撐大了。夏天冰融化了，但遲早它會再度結凍，經過許多次這樣的循環之後，裂縫大到一塊岩石碎片斷裂脫落。你在山上常常可以看到碎石坡——一個堆滿鬆散碎石和石塊的斜面。碎石坡上所有的石頭，都是被水的結凍和融化從大岩石上崩裂下來的。


When the rain falls it runs down the slope in little runnels, and the little streams come together and form a bigger stream, and the bigger stream pushes the stones along — but all the time these stones are being rubbed against each other. As the water pushes the stones and rubs them against each other, the corners get knocked off and, eventually, they become round pebbles. That's what you can see in any stream. The smooth, round pebbles were once sharp-edged stones. They have been rounded off in the running water.

當雨水落下，它沿著斜坡在小溝渠中流淌，小溪匯聚在一起形成較大的溪流，較大的溪流推著石頭前進——但在這整個過程中，這些石頭一直在互相摩擦。當水推動石頭、讓它們互相摩擦時，稜角被磨掉了，最終它們變成了圓滾滾的卵石。這就是你在任何溪流中都能看到的景象。那些光滑圓潤的卵石，曾經是稜角分明的石頭。它們在流水中被磨圓了。


The water of the rushing stream keeps on rubbing the little stones against each other — small bits are rubbed off — and so they get smaller and smaller until they become little grains; we call them sand. Sand is rock that has been ground smaller and smaller by the running water. All the time the water carries the pebbles, gravel and sand further downstream. The smaller the stones become, the more easily the water can sweep them along, so that upstream there will be more pebbles and downstream there will be more sand.

奔流的溪水持續不斷地讓小石頭互相摩擦——小碎片被磨掉——於是它們變得越來越小，直到變成小小的顆粒；我們稱之為沙。沙就是被流水研磨得越來越細小的岩石。水一直把卵石、礫石和沙帶往下游。石頭越小，水就越容易把它們沖走，所以上游會有更多的卵石，下游則會有更多的沙。


As the granite (for instance, from the Cairngorms) is broken down, the quartz and feldspar are separated. Quartz is harder than feldspar and so it does not break down so much, it becomes sand. The feldspar is less hard and the pieces of feldspar get smaller still until they are like grains of dust, and in the water these tiny grains of dust become something like mud. The proper name for this mud is clay. If you rub sand between your fingers it feels rough and gritty, but clay is so fine that it feels quite smooth.

當花崗岩（比如來自 Cairngorms（凱恩戈姆山脈）的花崗岩）被分解時，石英和長石就分離開了。石英比長石硬，所以不會被磨碎得那麼厲害，它變成了沙。長石沒那麼硬，長石的碎片會被磨得更小，直到變得像塵埃顆粒一樣，在水中這些微小的塵埃顆粒變成了像泥巴一樣的東西。這種泥巴的正式名稱是黏土。如果你在手指間搓揉沙子，感覺粗糙而有沙礫感，但黏土細緻到摸起來十分滑順。


So, the water breaks the rocks when it is ice. It sweeps the broken bits of rock downstream and they become gravel, then they become sand, then they become clay. Then the sand and the clay are taken further downstream by the river. As the river gets nearer to the sea it usually gets wider and it slows down. The slow-moving water does not carry the mud so well and a great part of the sand and clay is "deposited," that means it falls to the bed of the river and lies on the river banks. We have all seen sand and mud on the banks of a river. When the river gets to the sea, it brings sand and clay with it and a lot goes right out into the sea, finally landing on the sea bed.

所以，水在結成冰時破碎岩石。它把碎裂的岩石沖往下游，先變成礫石，再變成沙，然後變成黏土。接著沙和黏土被河流帶往更遠的下游。當河流越來越接近大海時，它通常會變寬、流速變慢。流速緩慢的水不太能攜帶泥巴，於是大部分的沙和黏土就「沉積」下來——意思是它們沉到河床上，堆在河岸邊。我們都見過河岸邊的沙子和泥巴。當河流到達大海時，它帶著沙和黏土一起，其中很多一路流到海裡，最終落在海床上。


When sand, clay or mud fall to the bottom of the sea or a lake and make a layer there, the layer is called sediment. As we know from the example of limestone, sediment can be pressed down and in time turn to rock. So rocks which form in this way below water are called sedimentary rocks. Limestone is one kind of sedimentary rock and now sandstone is another. Sandstone can form if the piles of sand are pressed down hard over long ages. But not all the sand is under the sea; by the action of the waves in the sea, some of it spreads along the shore; that's how you get sandy beaches.

當沙、黏土或泥巴沉到海底或湖底，在那裡形成一層，這一層就叫做沉積物。正如我們從石灰岩的例子中所知道的，沉積物可以被壓實，隨著時間變成岩石。所以以這種方式在水下形成的岩石，就叫做沉積岩。石灰岩是一種沉積岩，現在我們知道砂岩是另一種。如果沙堆在漫長的歲月中被狠狠壓實，就能形成砂岩。但並不是所有的沙都在海底；由於海浪的作用，有些沙被推散到海岸邊；沙灘就是這樣形成的。


All this has been going on for hundreds of thousands of years, the rivers making sand and clay. When it lies on dry land, plants grow on it and creatures burrow in it — they live and die year after year — and the top layer of sand and clay becomes soil. All the good soil in the world, the soil in which plants can grow strong, the soil which gives us all the crops we need for our food — all the soft fertile soil in the world is possible because of the sand and clay which the water has brought down from the mountains.

這一切已經持續了數十萬年，河流不斷地製造沙和黏土。當它們躺在乾燥的陸地上，植物在上面生長，生物在其中挖掘洞穴——它們年復一年地活著、死去——於是沙和黏土的最上層就變成了土壤。世界上所有的好土壤，那些能讓植物茁壯生長的土壤，那些為我們提供所需一切糧食作物的土壤——世界上所有鬆軟肥沃的土壤之所以存在，都是因為水從山上帶下來的沙和黏土。


No plants could grow, no animal and no man could find food if the water did not nibble away at the mountains and if the water did not rub stones together until they became tiny grains of sand and clay.

如果水不去啃咬山脈，如果水不把石頭互相摩擦直到它們變成微小的沙粒和黏土顆粒，那麼就沒有植物能夠生長，沒有動物、也沒有人能夠找到食物。
# 11. The Circulation of Water
# 11. 水的循環


Now we must get to know a bit more about the waters of the earth. We have all seen water boiling and — rising up from it — the clouds of hot white mist we call steam. If a kettle boils long enough all the water would boil away and go up in steam. If you hang your wet washing out on the line, the washing will dry; the water in it will also disappear, it will also rise as "steam," but such a fine steam that you can't see it. And if I put a drop of water here it will also dry up after a time — it will disappear. How? It also rises up as invisible steam. In Latin, vapor is a word for steam, and the disappearance of water is called evaporation — it evaporates. What makes the water evaporate when there is no fire under it? The warmth and light of the sun; the warmth from above. And now think of all the oceans and seas and lakes all over the world. The sun shines on all of them and from all the waters of the world a huge amount of invisible steam rises. Now imagine that the drops of water could speak and tell their story. They would say:

現在我們必須更多認識地球上的水。我們都見過水沸騰時，從中升起熱騰騰的白色蒸氣。如果一壺水煮得夠久，所有的水都會沸騰蒸發，化為蒸氣消散。如果你把濕衣服晾在繩子上，衣服會乾；裡面的水也會消失，也會升起變成「蒸氣」，只不過是細得看不見的蒸氣。如果我在這裡放一滴水，過一段時間它也會乾掉——消失了。怎麼消失的？它也升起變成了看不見的蒸氣。在拉丁語中，vapor 是蒸氣的意思，水的消失就叫做蒸發（evaporation）。在沒有火燒的情況下，是什麼讓水蒸發的呢？是太陽的溫暖和光芒；是從上方來的熱。現在想想全世界所有的海洋、大海和湖泊。太陽照耀著它們，從世界上所有的水域中，大量的隱形蒸氣升起。現在想像一下，如果水滴能夠說話，述說它們的故事，它們會說：


We were on a big wave in the great ocean and the shining rays of the sun came and with their powers they lifted us up. We rose higher and higher — we became light as air — and more and more of us came up and we all became a beautiful white cloud. Oh, it was lovely to float up high above our father, the ocean. But the wind came and carried our cloud away — we flew over lands, over fields and forests and mountains. Near the mountains it grew cold and our great white cloud turned dark — the cold air made all of us heavy — we got so heavy that we could no longer stay up and we all fell down as rain.

我們在大洋的巨浪上，閃亮的陽光來了，用它的力量把我們舉起。我們越升越高——變得輕如空氣——越來越多的夥伴上來了，我們全都變成一朵美麗的白雲。啊，飄浮在我們的父親——大海的上方，真是美妙。但風來了，帶走了我們的雲——我們飛過大地，飛過田野、森林和山脈。靠近山脈時，天氣變冷了，我們壯麗的白雲變得暗沉——冷空氣使我們每一個都變得沉重——我們沉重得再也待不住，全都落下來變成了雨。


Some of us fell on the fields, some on forests and trees and flowers, but they all were glad to receive us. Many of us fell on mountain rocks where the rays of the sun lifted some of us up, others seeped into the rocks, and others again trickled over the rocks and where a few trickles met, we joined joyfully together and made brooks. The little brooks met — it was lovely to see the other drops again — and came together in a little stream that tumbled downwards over the rocks. Soon the little stream met another little stream, and another one, and we all joined together. Now a strong mountain stream rushed swirling down and met other mountain streams. And now together we became a rushing river. The river flowed on, and joined with another river.

有些夥伴落在田野上，有些落在森林、樹木和花朵上，但它們都歡喜地接住了我們。我們之中許多落在山石上，太陽的光芒把一些夥伴又舉了起來，另一些滲進了岩石裡，還有一些沿著岩石滴流下來，幾股細流匯合的地方，我們歡快地會合，成了小溪。小溪們相遇了——能再見到其他水滴真是太好了——匯成一條小河，翻滾著從岩石上奔流而下。很快，小河遇到了另一條小河，又遇到一條，我們全都匯合在一起。現在一條強勁的山澗旋轉奔湧而下，遇到了其他的山澗。然後我們一起變成了一條奔流的大河。河流繼續流淌，又匯入了另一條河。


Now we were a great wide river that flowed through the plains, through flat land. The river carried many ships with goods and passengers, and ferries going from one bank to another. Great bridges spanned it and great cities stood on the river banks. But on it flowed, and then we reached the sea, the ocean. Joyfully we came back from our long journey to our ocean father. But soon we shall be ready again for the next journey when the sun's rays lift us up to the sky.

現在我們成了一條寬闊的大河，流經平原，流過平坦的大地。河流載著許多裝著貨物和旅客的船隻，還有來回兩岸的渡船。雄偉的橋樑橫跨河面，偉大的城市矗立在河岸上。但河水繼續流淌，然後我們到達了大海，到達了大洋。我們歡欣地從漫長的旅程中回到了大海父親身邊。但很快我們又會準備好再次出發，等太陽的光芒把我們舉上天空。


That is the life-story of a river, the water which flows from the mountains to the sea. It came from the sea, it rose up from the sea as clouds, and came down as rain. It is really the sun which makes our rivers flow. Without the sun there would be no clouds, no rain and no river. The whole path which our drops have travelled from the sea back to the sea is like a circle that comes back to where it started — it is called the circulation of water or the water cycle. The blood in our bodies also circulates — it goes round and round — but the "sun" of our blood is the heart.

這就是一條河流的生命故事——水從山上流到大海。它來自大海，從海面升起化為雲，然後以雨的形式落下。真正讓河流奔流的，其實是太陽。沒有太陽，就沒有雲、沒有雨，也沒有河流。我們的水滴從大海出發又回到大海，走過的整條路徑就像一個圓，回到了起點——這就叫做水的循環（the water cycle）。我們體內的血液也在循環——不停地繞圈流動——但血液的「太陽」是心臟。


We saw that the streams and rivers slowly break down the mountains and grind the rocks into sand and clay, into soil. What really makes the good soil? It is the sun. The sun not only makes the plants grow; it has even made the soil from which they grow!

我們看到，溪流和河川慢慢地磨蝕山脈，把岩石研磨成沙、黏土，研磨成土壤。真正造就好土壤的是什麼？是太陽。太陽不僅讓植物生長，它甚至造就了植物生長的土壤！


# 12. Winds
# 12. 風


We have learned about earth and about water; now we must also learn about the air. We can't see the air; it is colourless. A room is full of air, but we can't see it. Things we can't see are real just the same. If the air in a room gets used up and we feel it's stuffy and want to have some fresh air by opening the window, then we can be sure that this air we can't see is quite real.

我們學習了土地，學習了水；現在我們還必須認識空氣。我們看不見空氣；它是無色的。一個房間裡充滿了空氣，但我們看不到它。看不到的東西同樣是真實的。如果房間裡的空氣用完了，我們覺得悶，想要開窗通風，那我們就能確定這個看不見的空氣確實是真實存在的。


But there are ways of making the air visible. Water is also colourless, but we can colour it with paint. Quite often air can be coloured and become visible because something has been put into it. We all have seen coloured air quite often. I am talking about smoke — the smoke rising from a fire is nothing but air coloured by tiny bits of ash.

但有辦法讓空氣變得看得見。水也是無色的，但我們可以用顏料把它染色。空氣常常也能被染色而變得可見，因為有東西混進了空氣裡。我們其實都常常看到有顏色的空氣。我說的就是煙——從火焰升起的煙，不過就是被細小灰燼染了色的空氣。


These bits of ash do not just rise by themselves. They rise because the air carries them, and the movement you see is nothing else but air rising upwards. We all know why the air from a fire goes up: it is hot. We know that steam rises up from boiling water, and air, when it gets hot, also rises. What will cold air do? It will sink. In a fireplace the hot air goes up through the chimney, and from below colder air comes and takes its place; that is what is called a draught. If there is no draught the fire will not burn. This process — hot air rising, cold air coming in below and taking its place — goes on in nature, and that is how we have winds.

這些灰燼碎屑不是自己升起來的。它們升起是因為空氣帶著它們上升，而你看到的那個運動，不是別的，正是空氣向上升起。我們都知道為什麼火焰旁的空氣往上走：因為它是熱的。我們知道蒸氣從沸騰的水中升起，空氣變熱時也會上升。那冷空氣會怎樣呢？它會下沉。在壁爐裡，熱空氣從煙囪上升，而下方較冷的空氣過來填補它的位置；這就叫做氣流（draught）。如果沒有氣流，火就燒不起來。這個過程——熱空氣上升，冷空氣從下方補上——在大自然中不斷發生著，風就是這樣來的。


Now let us take something a bit more complicated. Imagine it is summer and we are at the seaside on a really nice, sunny day. The sun shines on the land and also on the sea. By about lunch-time you will find that stones and even the top sand have become quite warm — but the water is cool, much cooler than the land. Earth and stones get warm much more quickly than water. But if the earth is warmer, the air above the earth also becomes warmer, and rises. Cool air then comes from the sea. So on a warm, still day, in the afternoon you will get a cool breeze coming from the sea.

現在讓我們來看稍微複雜一點的情況。想像現在是夏天，我們在海邊度過一個陽光明媚的好天氣。太陽照耀著陸地，也照耀著大海。大約午餐時分，你會發現石頭甚至表層的沙子已經變得相當暖和——但海水是涼的，比陸地涼得多。土地和石頭比水升溫快得多。但如果地面較暖，地面上方的空氣也變得較暖，於是上升。涼爽的空氣就從海面過來補上。所以在一個溫暖、無風的日子裡，下午你會感受到從海面吹來的涼風。


At night at the seaside, the earth, stones and sand which became warm so quickly in the sun also lose their warmth quickly; but the water, which warms slowly, also cools down slowly. The water is still warm when the land is already cold. So, in the night, there will also be a breeze, but from land to sea.

到了夜晚，在海邊，白天曬得很快就暖起來的土地、石頭和沙子也很快失去了熱度；但是水——升溫慢的水——也冷卻得慢。陸地已經冷了的時候，海水還是溫暖的。所以到了夜晚，也會有風，但方向反過來，是從陸地吹向大海。


Now think of the whole earth. In the hot tropical countries around the equator, enormous quantities of hot air rise up and spread out to both the north and south, away from the equator. This draws in cooler — but still quite warm — winds. At the icy poles, the air falls and there is a continuous flow of cold air away from the poles. Between the equatorial winds and the polar winds, in temperate zones, the winds blow towards the poles. This circulation of air makes winds blow over the oceans all the year and, because the earth is always rotating, these winds do not just go north and south, they turn east and west too. On both sides of the equator there are the steady, reliable trade winds. Further north (and south) there are colder winds which blow the opposite way, from west to east, the westerlies. In the old days, sailing ships made use of these winds for their journeys. So the air around us is forever moving because warm air goes up, cold air sinks down and the earth turns.

現在想想整個地球。在赤道附近炎熱的熱帶國家，巨量的熱空氣升起，向南、向北兩邊擴散，離開赤道。這就把較涼——但仍然很暖——的風吸引過來。在冰冷的兩極，空氣下沉，冷空氣不斷從兩極向外流動。在赤道風與極地風之間的溫帶地區，風朝著兩極吹去。這種空氣的循環使得風一年到頭在海洋上吹拂。而且因為地球不停地自轉，這些風不只南北移動，還會往東西方偏轉。赤道兩側有穩定可靠的信風（trade winds）。更往北（和往南）則有較冷的風，方向相反，從西吹向東，叫做西風帶（westerlies）。在古代，帆船就利用這些風來航行。所以我們周圍的空氣永遠在運動，因為熱空氣上升，冷空氣下沉，而地球不停地轉。


But sometimes this pattern of hot air and cold air is not just a slow and steady circulation; it becomes instead a madly turning spinning-top. These mad spinning-tops of air happen in warm, tropical regions and are called hurricanes. Sometimes these hurricanes strike the coast. This happens quite often on the southern coast of the United States. Then trees are flattened like matches and houses are broken apart as if a bulldozer had gone through them. Cars and even houses can be blown a distance of half a mile.

但有時候，這種冷熱空氣的模式不只是緩慢而穩定的循環；它會變成一個瘋狂旋轉的陀螺。這些瘋狂旋轉的空氣陀螺發生在溫暖的熱帶地區，叫做颶風（hurricanes）。有時這些颶風會襲擊海岸。這在美國南部海岸經常發生。到那時，樹木像火柴一樣被壓平，房屋像被推土機碾過一樣被撕裂。汽車甚至房屋都能被吹到半英里以外。


Strangely, right in the centre of this spinning-top of air, there is no wind at all. This still centre of the storm is called the eye of the hurricane. Around is a swirling hell of storm and water, but in the centre it is calm. You can even see the blue sky and the sun above.

奇怪的是，在這個旋轉空氣陀螺的正中央，完全沒有風。這個風暴寧靜的中心叫做颶風眼（the eye of the hurricane）。四周是風暴與水的漩渦地獄，但中心卻是平靜的。你甚至能看到頭頂的藍天和太陽。


Like all the winds of the earth the hurricanes too come from the process you see when smoke rises from a fire: hot air goes up, cool air sinks down. And what moves the air in the world? It is the warmth of the sun. Air as well as water, both are moved by the sun.

和地球上所有的風一樣，颶風也來自於你看到煙從火中升起時的那個過程：熱空氣上升，冷空氣下沉。是什麼推動了世界上的空氣運動？是太陽的溫暖。空氣和水一樣，都是被太陽驅動的。


The way the sun warms the earth and warms the water has another effect. Think of summer and winter in Britain. This island is surrounded on all sides by the sea. The sea around our shores may look and feel very cold to you in winter; but because the sea cools down slowly it is still warmer than the land. The warm air rises from the sea and it spreads and comes to us. So we do not usually get very harsh winters with lots of ice and snow. But in summer the sea around us is still cool, compared with the land, and we get a good deal of cool air in summer. So we rarely have a really hot summer, and cool air brings the clouds and rain!

太陽溫暖大地、溫暖水面的方式還有另一個效應。想想英國（Britain）的夏天和冬天。這個島嶼四面環海。冬天時，我們海岸周圍的海水看起來、感覺起來可能很冷；但因為海水冷卻得慢，它其實還是比陸地暖。溫暖的空氣從海面升起，擴散到我們這裡。所以我們通常不會有很嚴酷、滿是冰雪的冬天。但到了夏天，我們周圍的海水與陸地相比仍然涼爽，夏天我們就得到大量涼爽的空氣。所以我們很少有真正炎熱的夏天，而涼爽的空氣帶來了雲和雨！


Now think of a country right in the middle of Europe — so far from the sea that no air can reach it directly from the sea. It will be very hot in the summer, and very cold in winter. So Britain's climate as it is called — the weather over the whole year — is different from the climate of, say, Austria for two reasons: because Britain firstly is further north and secondly is surrounded by sea.

現在想想一個位在歐洲正中央的國家——離海那麼遠，海洋的空氣根本無法直接到達那裡。它的夏天會很熱，冬天會很冷。所以英國的氣候——整年的天氣狀況——和例如奧地利（Austria）的氣候不同，原因有二：第一，英國緯度更北；第二，英國四面環海。


# 13. Glaciers
# 13. 冰川


We have looked at earth, water, air and also at the warmth of the sun; how it moves the winds and the waters of the world. All these things have shaped and formed the world in which we live and they go on shaping and forming it. But there is something else that has played a great part in shaping the world, and that is snow and ice.

我們已經看過了土地、水、空氣，還有太陽的溫暖；看過太陽如何驅動世界的風和水。這一切塑造了我們所生活的世界，而且至今仍在繼續塑造著它。但還有另一樣東西在塑造世界方面扮演了重大角色，那就是雪和冰。


On the peaks of high mountains like the Alps the snow does not melt; it stays from one winter to the next. If winter after winter more and more snow falls, over hundreds or thousands of years, the mountain peaks of the Alps or the Himalayas would by now have a covering of snow higher than the mountains themselves. But why do they not have such high caps of snow?

在像阿爾卑斯山（the Alps）這樣的高山山頂，雪不會融化；它從一個冬天留到下一個冬天。如果一個冬天又一個冬天，越來越多的雪降下來，經過數百年或數千年，阿爾卑斯山或喜馬拉雅山（the Himalayas）的山頂到現在應該覆蓋著比山本身還高的雪了。但為什麼它們沒有那麼高的雪帽呢？


When there is such a thick, deep layer of snow, the snow at the bottom is under great pressure, for all the snow above is pressing down on it. When snow is pressed down hard, it changes first from fluffy snow to hard, compact ice, then it melts. When all the snow and ice lies on a slope and the ice at the bottom turns partly to melt-water, the whole thing very slowly slides over the rocks below. The whole ice-field creeps and slips slowly further and further downhill.
