當雪積得那麼厚、那麼深時，底層的雪承受著巨大的壓力，因為上面所有的雪都壓在它身上。雪被用力壓下去時，先從鬆軟的雪變成堅硬緊實的冰，然後就會融化。當所有的雪和冰堆在一個斜坡上，底部的冰部分融化成水，整個冰體就會非常緩慢地在下方的岩石上滑動。整片冰原慢慢地蠕動、滑行，越來越往山下移去。


Such a moving ice-field is called a glacier. It is really an ice river, but an ice river that flows only very, very slowly downhill. How far can it flow downhill? Until it comes to the level where the air gets warm enough in summer to melt all ice and snow, and there the glacier stops. Streams run from it, but it does not all melt away for there is always more ice coming down from above and more snow falling in the heights. It is a terrific sight, a glacier, a vast field of ice — 40, 50, 100 metres thick in some places — crossed by cracks called crevasses, some quite narrow, but some very wide and deep. It is these cracks in the ice which make crossing a glacier difficult and dangerous. Looking down one of these gaps you see deeper layers of ice, and they appear blue.

這樣移動的冰原就叫做冰川（glacier）。它其實是一條冰河，但是一條流動得非常、非常緩慢的下山冰河。它能往下流多遠？直到它來到夏季空氣溫暖到足以融化所有冰雪的高度，冰川就在那裡停住。溪水從它流出，但冰川不會全部融化消失，因為上方不斷有更多冰塊滑下來，高處不斷有更多雪降落。冰川是一幅壯觀的景象——一片廣袤的冰原，有些地方厚達四十、五十甚至一百公尺——上面橫亙著叫做冰隙（crevasses）的裂縫，有些很窄，但有些非常寬而且深。正是冰上的這些裂縫，使得穿越冰川既困難又危險。往裂隙下方望去，你會看到更深層的冰，它們呈現藍色。


As you look at it, the glacier seems to be as hard and still as rock — it does not seem to move at all — but it only seems so. If a flag is stuck into the ice, you will still be able to find it a few days later, several metres further down, and in time it will come to the end of the glacier. This giant ice field is not quick, it has a slow downward-creeping motion. (Some hardly move at all, but fast ones can move several metres each day).

當你看著冰川時，它似乎像岩石一樣堅硬靜止——看起來完全不動——但那只是看起來如此。如果把一面旗子插在冰上，幾天後你還能找到它，只是它已經往下移了好幾公尺，最終它會到達冰川的末端。這片巨大的冰原不是快速移動的，它有一種緩慢向下蠕動的運動。（有些幾乎不動，但快的一天能移動好幾公尺）。


The glacier is also strewn with boulders, rocks and stones which have been broken from the rocks by the river of ice. All these boulders and stones are slowly moved to the end, where the glacier melts, and then they come to lie on the bare ground. This "depositing," this bringing down of boulders and stones, has been going on for many years and so every glacier has a great fringe, a "hem" of rubble, boulders and stones. This great fringe at the glacier's end is called a moraine.

冰川上還散布著巨石、岩塊和碎石，這些都是冰河從岩壁上剝落下來的。所有這些巨石和碎石都被慢慢搬運到末端——冰川融化的地方，然後它們就停留在裸露的地面上。這種「堆積」，這種把巨石和碎石搬下來的作用，已經持續了許多年，所以每條冰川都有一大圈碎石的「邊緣」——由碎礫、巨石和碎石組成的。冰川末端這一大圈堆積物，叫做冰磧（moraine）。


Now the strange thing is that there are many places in the world where you can find quite enormous moraines, large fields of rubble, boulders and stones; but they are far away down in valleys and in plains, far from any glacier. For a long time no one could think of an explanation of how these moraines came to be there. In the end a Swiss scientist called Louis Agassiz found the explanation. In ancient times the glaciers must have reached much further down than they do now. That was the Ice Age and it ended only about 10,000 years ago. That's how we came to know that there was an ice age.

奇怪的是，世界上很多地方都能找到相當巨大的冰磧——大片的碎礫、巨石和碎石堆；但它們遠在山谷和平原的低處，離任何冰川都很遠。很長一段時間，沒有人能解釋這些冰磧為什麼會出現在那裡。最後，一位叫做路易斯．阿加西（Louis Agassiz）的瑞士科學家找到了答案。在遠古時代，冰川一定曾經延伸到比現在低得多的地方。那就是冰河時期（the Ice Age），它在大約一萬年前才結束。我們就是這樣知道曾經有過冰河時期的。


Now think of the first picture we described: earth and mountain. In that picture the earth as well as the mountain had an ice cap. During the Ice Age both ice caps reached much further. Most of Britain was covered by ice so deep that our mountains were all completely hidden beneath these terrible glaciers. Much of Europe and North America were also covered.

現在回想我們最初描述的那幅圖景：大地和山脈。在那幅圖景中，大地和山脈都有冰帽。在冰河時期，兩個冰帽都延伸得更遠。英國大部分地區被冰覆蓋，冰層之深，以至於所有的山脈都完全隱沒在這些可怕的冰川之下。歐洲和北美洲的大部分地區也被覆蓋了。


The underside of a glacier is just like an enormous rasp (think of woodwork lessons). As it flows downhill it rasps the rock below. This "rasp" is not made of ice alone; it has countless rocks and stones in it. As the glacier flows along these all grind and scrape the bedrock below. Even today there are many places where you can see the parallel scratches left on the surface of a rock by glaciers during the Ice Age. So our mountains have been very much worn down by the Ice Age glaciers. Between the smoothly rounded hills the ice rasp has hollowed furrows and these have become our smooth, U-shaped valleys. Often a stream now flows along the valley floor, but it was not the little stream which cut out such a big valley — it was a mighty glacier during the Ice Age. The rounded, "rolling" landscape of Britain has been shaped by glaciers.

冰川的底面就像一把巨大的銼刀（想想木工課上的銼刀）。當它往山下流動時，就像用銼刀銼磨下方的岩石。這把「銼刀」不只是冰構成的；裡面有無數的岩塊和碎石。冰川流動時，這些石頭全都在研磨、刮擦下方的基岩。即使今天，在很多地方你都能看到冰河時期冰川在岩石表面留下的平行刮痕。所以我們的山脈被冰河時期的冰川大大地磨蝕了。在圓滑的丘陵之間，冰的銼刀刻出了溝槽，這些溝槽就成了我們平滑的 U 形谷。如今常常有溪流沿著谷底流淌，但並不是這條小溪切出了這麼大的山谷——是冰河時期一條巨大的冰川。英國那種圓滾滾、起伏綿延的地貌，就是被冰川塑造出來的。


If you rasp wood you get sawdust from all the wood rasped away; the glaciers, these ice rasps, have also left behind a vast amount of boulders, stones and rock dust. This mixture is called boulder clay. At the end of the Ice Age there were vast piles of boulder clay along with lakes, ponds and rivers left by the melted ice. Quite quickly plants began to grow and animals moved in to live, so that the boulder clay became mixed with plant and animal remains. This all created wonderful rich topsoil. Some of the best farmland in the world, including the fertile land of the Lothians here, is based on the rock and clay left by the glaciers of the Ice Age.

如果你用銼刀銼木頭，被銼掉的木屑就會散落；冰川，這些冰銼刀，也留下了大量的巨石、碎石和岩粉。這種混合物叫做冰磧黏土（boulder clay）。冰河時期結束時，到處是大量的冰磧黏土，以及融冰留下的湖泊、池塘和河流。很快地，植物開始生長，動物搬進來棲息，於是冰磧黏土和植物、動物的殘餘混合在一起。這一切造就了極為豐沃的表土。世界上一些最好的農田，包括這裡洛錫安（the Lothians）的沃土，就是建立在冰河時期冰川遺留的岩石和黏土之上。


Why did the ice spread? And why has it since then melted and retreated to the far north and the great heights? No one knows for certain but there are many possibilities. It may be due to changes in the atmosphere of the earth — more or less carbon dioxide in the air — a kind of "breathing" of the earth. It may be because of small changes in the strength of the sunlight falling on the earth. It may be because so many volcanoes erupted and put great quantities of ash and dust in the air which screened off some of the sunlight. Perhaps all of these played a part.

冰為什麼會擴散？又為什麼後來融化並退縮到遙遠的北方和高處呢？沒有人確切知道，但有很多可能。也許是因為地球大氣的變化——空氣中二氧化碳的增減——一種地球的「呼吸」。也許是因為照射到地球的陽光強度發生了微小的變化。也許是因為那麼多火山噴發，把大量的灰燼和塵埃送進了空氣中，遮蔽了部分陽光。也許這些因素都起了作用。


# 14. The Story of Arthur's Seat in Edinburgh
# 14. 愛丁堡亞瑟王座的故事


We have heard of the ways in which mountains are "born" and how, through water and wind they are worn down again. I now want to describe a hill here in Edinburgh, Arthur's Seat. Every mountain tells its own story; and the people who study the rocks and mountains, the geologists, can read the story of a mountain from the layers and rocks.

我們已經聽過山脈如何「誕生」，以及它們如何通過水和風的作用再被磨蝕。現在我要描述愛丁堡（Edinburgh）這裡的一座山丘——亞瑟王座（Arthur's Seat）。每座山都在訴說自己的故事；而研究岩石和山脈的人——地質學家——能夠從岩層和岩石中讀出一座山的故事。


The story of Arthur's Seat began many millions of years ago, long before Arthur's Seat came into existence. Nearby, to the south of here, there were great volcanic eruptions. In time, the lava and ash from these eruptions formed mountains and we can still see their worn-down remains today: the Pentlands, the Braid Hills and Blackford Hill. But the weather, the climate here, was very different from what it is now. It was hot, so hot that this part of the world was a desert. It is strange to think that this was so, but that is the story that the rocks tell us. There was once a time when the lowlands of Scotland were a desert, a desert deeply covered with sand.

亞瑟王座的故事開始於數百萬年前，遠在亞瑟王座誕生之前。在這附近的南方，發生過巨大的火山噴發。隨著時間推移，這些噴發產生的熔岩和火山灰形成了山脈，而我們今天仍然能看到它們被磨蝕後的殘餘：彭特蘭丘陵（the Pentlands）、布雷德丘陵（the Braid Hills）和布萊克福德山（Blackford Hill）。但那時這裡的天氣、氣候，和現在非常不同。那時很熱，熱到這個地方是一片沙漠。想到這一點令人覺得不可思議，但這就是岩石告訴我們的故事。曾經有一段時期，蘇格蘭（Scotland）低地是一片沙漠，被厚厚的沙覆蓋著。


After many millions of years the land began to sink (or the sea rose) and the desert with its thick layer of sand became a sea-bed. The sand of the desert was pressed down and became sandstone. But then, as more millions of years passed, something else happened. The water above the sandstone became a quiet tropical sea, with tree-lined beaches and lagoons full of life: fish, shrimps, mussels.

又過了數百萬年，陸地開始下沉（或者說海面上升了），沙漠和它厚厚的沙層變成了海床。沙漠的沙被壓實，變成了砂岩。但隨著又一個數百萬年的過去，另外一些事情發生了。砂岩上方的水域變成了一片寧靜的熱帶海洋，有樹木環繞的海灘，有充滿生命的潟湖：魚、蝦、貽貝。


Then, in this tropical sea a terrific volcanic eruption took place. It must have been an enormous eruption for the lava forced its way right through layers of stone and millions of tons of lava came pouring out: lava mixed with the rocks and stones that had been pushed out by the eruption. First a volcano appeared where the Castle Rock now stands and then, through this mighty eruption, the first shape of the volcano we call Arthur's Seat came about.

然後，在這片熱帶海洋中，發生了一場猛烈的火山噴發。那一定是一次巨大的噴發，因為熔岩硬是穿過了層層岩石，數百萬噸的熔岩傾瀉而出：熔岩夾帶著噴發推出的岩石和碎石。首先，一座火山出現在現在城堡岩（Castle Rock）所在的地方，然後，通過這場巨大的噴發，我們稱為亞瑟王座的那座火山最初的形狀形成了。


This was formed by ash and lava together with all the rock and stone that the lava had pushed out in the eruption. But the pipe, the shaft through which the lava had come, was free and more lava came in powerful eruptions. Lava and ash covered everything beneath it.

這是由火山灰和熔岩，連同噴發中被推出的所有岩石和碎石共同形成的。但岩漿管道——熔岩通過的豎管——仍然是通暢的，更多的熔岩在猛烈的噴發中湧出。熔岩和火山灰覆蓋了下方的一切。


In time the volcano of Arthur's Seat which had been smoking for a long time, gave less and less smoke; it became dormant. The lava inside the shaft hardened and cooled and the volcano became extinct; it became a dead volcano. Then the land sank down and Arthur's Seat slowly disappeared beneath the waves and became buried under thick layers of sediment at the bottom of the sea. In this sea there were coral reefs and teeming marine life — beds of shelly limestone formed at the bottom of this sea. At the same time great nearby rivers flowed into the sea, spreading out and depositing huge amounts of sand; in time this formed thick beds of grey sandstone.

隨著時間推移，長期冒煙的亞瑟王座火山漸漸冒出越來越少的煙；它進入了休眠期。岩漿管道內的熔岩硬化冷卻，火山徹底熄滅了；它變成了一座死火山。然後陸地下沉，亞瑟王座慢慢消失在波浪之下，被厚厚的沉積物埋藏在海底。在這片海洋中有珊瑚礁和豐富的海洋生物——海底形成了一層層貝殼石灰岩。同時，附近的大河流入海中，擴散開來，沉積了大量的沙；日久天長，這些沙形成了厚厚的灰色砂岩層。


Then the sea-level went down, the land rose and the land that had been sea-bed became covered by a strange forest in which all kinds of creatures lived. This was the time when many coal-seams were slowly formed, one above the other. Millions of years later these coal seams would be mined and millions of tons of coal dug out for use in homes and industry. But, deep down, there is still a huge amount of this coal left — the last remains of those ancient forests which once grew all around here and over much of the world.

然後海面下降，陸地升起，曾經是海床的大地被一片奇異的森林覆蓋，各種各樣的生物生活在其中。這是許多煤層慢慢形成的時期，一層疊一層。數百萬年後，這些煤層會被開採，數百萬噸的煤被挖出來供家庭和工業使用。但在深處，仍然留有大量的煤——那是曾經生長在這裡四周和世界大部分地方的古老森林最後的遺存。


Then there was more volcanic activity and molten rock forced its way upwards. This time the glowing, fiery magma did not break through to the surface and it hardened, deep underground, into huge slabs of basalt. (Some of these came to the surface — where we can now see them — but only much later, because of deep movements in the earth's crust). Salisbury Crags date from this time. The Crags look reddish, not dark like basalt. But basalt contains iron, and over the years its surface "weathers" to the reddish colour which we see. The hard basalt hills have been quarried and the rock used for building and road making. The quarrymen call this rock whin. But whin is also a name for the tough gorse plant which likes to grow on the stony basalt soil. And every spring the gorse or whin sets these volcanic hills aglow once again with its bright covering of golden flowers.

然後又發生了更多的火山活動，熔融的岩石往上擠。這一次，熾熱的岩漿沒有衝破地表，而是在地底深處硬化成了巨大的玄武岩板塊。（其中一些後來到了地表——也就是我們現在能看到的地方——但那是很久以後的事了，是因為地殼的深層運動。）索爾茲伯里峭壁（Salisbury Crags）就形成於這個時期。峭壁看起來是紅褐色的，不像玄武岩那樣深暗。但玄武岩含有鐵，多年來它的表面「風化」成了我們所見的紅褐色。堅硬的玄武岩山丘曾被開採，岩石用來蓋房子和修路。採石工人把這種石頭叫做 whin。而 whin 也是一種堅韌的荊豆植物的名字，這種植物喜歡生長在佈滿石頭的玄武岩土壤上。每到春天，荊豆——也就是 whin——就用一片燦爛的金色花朵，讓這些火山丘陵再度煥發光芒。


More time passed: the land rose again and the sea receded. The crust of the earth began to fold. This powerful folding of the earth, brought about by the movement of continents, caused earthquakes — the rocks slowly bent, folded and slid into humps and troughs, domes and basins. In this upheaval Arthur's Seat (together with the younger Crags) was lifted again from beneath the sea while the rocks all around were shifted, bent and mixed up. Many of the higher up layers of rocks were worn away, while others — like the Midlothian Coalfield — were preserved. The softer rocks which had covered over Arthur's Seat were worn away, but the hard volcanic rock was not, and so Arthur's Seat stood high above the land once more.

更多時間過去了：陸地再次升起，海水退去。地殼開始褶皺。這種由大陸運動引起的強大地殼褶皺，造成了地震——岩石慢慢彎曲、褶疊、滑動，形成隆起和凹槽、穹隆和盆地。在這場劇變中，亞瑟王座（連同較年輕的峭壁）從海底再次被抬升起來，四周的岩石都被擠壓、彎折、攪亂。許多上層的岩石被磨蝕掉了，但另一些——比如米德洛錫安煤田（the Midlothian Coalfield）——被保存了下來。覆蓋在亞瑟王座上方的較軟岩石被磨蝕掉了，但堅硬的火山岩沒有，於是亞瑟王座再次高聳於大地之上。


Then, in more "recent" times, the Ice Age came and ice covered the whole land. The deep ice-sheet flowed slowly towards the east and ground away at all the rocks, including Arthur's Seat and the Crags, but even the power of the ice could not remove them. Finally the Ice Age went away and by this time, which was "only" about 10,000 years ago, Arthur's Seat looked more or less as it looks today.

然後，在較為「近期」的時代，冰河時期來臨，冰覆蓋了整片大地。厚重的冰層緩慢地向東流動，磨蝕著所有的岩石，包括亞瑟王座和峭壁，但即使冰的力量也無法移除它們。最終冰河時期過去了，到了那時——那「不過」是大約一萬年前——亞瑟王座看起來大致就像今天的模樣了。


So this is the story of Arthur's Seat. And now think of all the stages this mountain has seen. It has seen tropical heat and it has been deep under glaciers in the ice age. It has been dry land, and it has been a sea-bed, deep under the waves — and then dry land again. It has seen the slow process of mountain-folding as well as the sudden terrific bursts of volcanic eruptions. So Arthur's Seat is a mountain that has seen all the things we have talked about.

這就是亞瑟王座的故事。現在想想這座山經歷過的所有階段。它見證過熱帶的酷暑，也曾深埋在冰河時期的冰川之下。它曾是旱地，也曾是海床，沉沒在波浪深處——然後又重新成為旱地。它見證過緩慢的造山褶皺過程，也見證過火山噴發突如其來的猛烈爆發。所以，亞瑟王座是一座見證了我們所談論過的一切的山。
# 15. The Heart and the Sun
# 15. 心臟與太陽

If we think about what the most important thing is that a human being needs, we would probably say food. But if we think it over, we will realize that water is even more important. It is easier to go hungry than to go thirsty, and people lost in the desert can last many days without food, if they have water to drink. But a human being can go perhaps two days without water. But how long could anybody go without air? Not even two minutes. It is fortunate that we don't have to work or to pay for air, that it is always there for us to breathe. We must breathe to live.

如果我們想想人類最重要的需求是什麼，大概會說是食物。但仔細想想就會發現，水其實更重要。忍受飢餓比忍受口渴容易得多，迷失在沙漠中的人只要有水喝，就能撐過許多天沒有食物的日子。然而，人大概只能兩天不喝水。那麼，誰能多久不呼吸呢？連兩分鐘都撐不了。幸運的是，我們不需要工作或付費才能獲得空氣，它總是在那裡讓我們呼吸。我們必須呼吸才能活著。


The rate, or speed of breathing changes. We breathe faster when we run and slower when we sit. If we take our normal breathing and we count breathing in and breathing out as one breath, the average number of breaths per minute is 18. As there are 60 minutes to the hour, we breathe 18 x 60, that is 1,080 times per hour. And in 24 hours that makes 1,080 x 24, or 25,920 breaths every day. That's an average of course, if we swim, run or climb during the day, it will be a good deal more.

呼吸的速率，也就是呼吸的快慢，會隨時改變。跑步時我們呼吸得更快，坐著時則更慢。如果以正常呼吸來計算，把一次吸氣和一次呼氣算作一次呼吸，每分鐘的平均呼吸次數是十八次。一小時有六十分鐘，所以我們每小時呼吸 18 x 60，也就是一千零八十次。一天二十四小時就是 1,080 x 24，即每天兩萬五千九百二十次呼吸。當然這只是平均值，如果白天游泳、跑步或爬山，次數會多出許多。


When we run or climb hard, not only does our breath come faster, but our heart beats much faster. It is really our heart beating faster that makes our lungs need more air. How slow or how fast we breathe depends on our heart. That we breathe normally about 18 times a minute depends on the heart. For every four heartbeats there is one breath, and if the heart beats quickly then the breath has to come quickly. So heartbeat and breath go in a steady rhythm together, day and night.

當我們拼命跑步或用力攀爬時，不只呼吸加速，心跳也快得多。實際上正是心臟跳動加快，才使得肺部需要更多空氣。我們呼吸的快慢取決於心臟。我們正常每分鐘呼吸大約十八次，這就是由心臟決定的。每四次心跳對應一次呼吸，心跳加快，呼吸也就必須跟著加快。就這樣，心跳與呼吸日日夜夜保持著穩定的節奏。


There is another rhythm, also a kind of breathing, but a very slow breathing. It takes much longer, but we need it just as much as we need air. It is the rhythm of sleeping and waking. When we fall asleep it is as if something were going away from us, like slowly breathing something out. And when we awake, it comes back; we are breathing in again. The rhythm of sleeping and waking is also a kind of breathing.

還有另一種節奏，也是一種呼吸，但非常緩慢的呼吸。它需要的時間長得多，但我們對它的需要一如對空氣的需要。那就是睡眠與清醒的節奏。當我們入睡時，彷彿有什麼東西離我們而去，像是緩緩呼出什麼。而當我們醒來，它又回來了；我們再次吸入。睡眠與清醒的節奏也是一種呼吸。


The real breathing, taking in air and letting it out again, is ruled by the heart. Of course, we can breathe quickly or slowly, just for fun; but if we don't interfere, the heart rules and controls the breathing. The heart is the organ which knows how many breaths the body needs. This is because the blood goes through the heart, and the heart knows from the blood how much air the body needs.

真正的呼吸，吸入空氣再呼出，是由心臟主宰的。當然，我們可以刻意加快或放慢呼吸，純粹好玩；但如果我們不去干預，心臟就會掌管並控制呼吸。心臟是那個知道身體需要多少次呼吸的器官。這是因為血液流經心臟，心臟從血液中知道身體需要多少空氣。


The other kind of breathing, the "sleeping and waking," is certainly not ruled by the heart. The heart goes on in its own rhythm, day and night. Sleeping and waking are for us modern people not what they were in ancient times when people went to sleep as darkness fell and woke up at daybreak. They rose with the sun, and they went to sleep when the sun set. Their sleeping and waking was ruled by the sun. Even today, though we stay up long after it gets dark, we feel it is healthier, more wholesome, to sleep at night and be awake in the daytime than the other way round. We still feel it is better to be awake with the sun.

另一種呼吸——「睡眠與清醒」——肯定不是由心臟主宰的。心臟日夜按照自己的節奏跳動。對我們現代人來說，睡眠與清醒已經不同於古代了。古時候，天一黑人們就入睡，天一亮就醒來。他們隨太陽升起而起床，隨太陽落下而入眠。他們的睡眠與清醒是由太陽主宰的。即使在今天，雖然天黑後我們還長時間不睡，我們依然覺得晚上睡覺、白天清醒比反過來更健康、更有益。我們仍然感到，與太陽一起清醒是比較好的。


So the shorter rhythm of breathing in and out is ruled by the heart, and the longer kind of breathing -- sleeping and waking -- is ruled by the sun, that is like a great heart in the world outside. Though the sun is a kind ruler who leaves us modern people a good deal of freedom.

所以，較短的呼吸節奏——吸入與呼出——由心臟主宰，而較長的那種呼吸——睡眠與清醒——由太陽主宰。太陽就像外在世界的一顆偉大心臟。不過，太陽是一位仁慈的統治者，給了我們現代人相當大的自由。


There is a third kind of "breathing." This time it is not a human being who breathes in and out. It is something much larger and so the breathing is very slow. Again it is not a breathing of air, but of something quite different, yet it is still a rhythm.

還有第三種「呼吸」。這一次，呼吸的不是人。它是某種遠為巨大的存在，因此這呼吸極為緩慢。這同樣不是空氣的呼吸，而是某種截然不同的東西，但它仍然是一種節奏。


In spring all the green leaves and flowers appear, then more and more flowers appear towards the summer, and then autumn comes and fields, gardens and trees become bare. This too is a kind of breathing: it is as if the earth breathes out in spring and summer and breathes in again in autumn and winter. Only the earth is so vast that it takes a whole year for such a single breathing in and out. But this long, slow breathing of the earth is ruled by the sun. The rhythm of the seasons is ruled by the sun.

春天裡，所有綠葉和花朵冒出來，然後越來越多的花兒綻放直到夏天，接著秋天來臨，田野、花園和樹木變得光禿。這也是一種呼吸：彷彿大地在春夏時呼出，在秋冬時再吸入。只是大地如此遼闊，一次完整的呼吸就要花上一整年。而大地這漫長、緩慢的呼吸，也是由太陽主宰的。四季的節奏由太陽主宰。


The "breathing" of the earth is not only so much slower than ours, it is altogether different. For when it is winter in Britain and Europe, it is also winter in North America and Russia. But on the other side of the globe -- in Australia, in Southern Africa, in South America -- it is summer, it is the warm season. So while one half of the earth is breathing in the other half is breathing out.

大地的「呼吸」不僅比我們的慢得多，而且完全不同。因為當英國和歐洲是冬天時，北美和俄羅斯也是冬天。但在地球的另一邊——澳洲、南非、南美洲——卻是夏天，是溫暖的季節。所以當地球的一半正在吸氣時，另一半正在呼氣。


Things are even more complicated. For if we went north to the Arctic, to the North Pole we would find it frozen all the time; it is winter during the whole year. And if we went to the equator -- to Africa or Central America -- there are again no seasons; it is summer all year.

事情還更複雜。如果我們往北走到北極圈、到北極，會發現那裡終年冰凍；全年都是冬天。而如果我們去赤道——去非洲或中美洲——同樣沒有四季；全年都是夏天。


# 16. The Sun's Daily Movement
# 16. 太陽的日常運行

Comparing equator and pole, we see that at the equator you can tell the time of the day by looking at the sun, but not the time of the year. It is as if there is no year, only the day. At the pole you cannot tell the time of the day because the sun is always at the same height. But you can easily tell the time of the year. At the poles there is no day, only the year.

比較赤道和極地，我們會發現在赤道上可以透過看太陽來知道一天中的時間，卻無法知道一年中的時節。彷彿沒有年，只有日。在極地，你無法分辨一天中的時間，因為太陽始終在同一高度。但你可以輕易知道一年中的時節。在極地，沒有日，只有年。


While at the equator the sun rises at right angles to the horizon, and at the pole the sun moves in circles parallel to the horizon, in our part of the world the sun rises at an angle to the horizon. We can show this in a diagram of the path of the sun in our part of the world.

在赤道，太陽以直角從地平線升起；在極地，太陽沿著平行於地平線的圓圈移動。而在我們所處的地方，太陽以一個傾斜角度從地平線升起。我們可以用一張圖來展示太陽在我們這個地區的運行路徑。


At the equator at noon the sun appears overhead, in the zenith. In temperate zones (like Britain) it is somewhere between the horizon and overhead at noon. And at the pole it is close to the horizon. But this shows us that it is not really the sun that is higher or lower, it is we, the human beings who look at the sun from different angles. We can see how this comes about from the diagram of the globe of the earth. The person on the equator sees the sun straight overhead, in the zenith, the person in our part of the world sees it lower in the sky, and the person at the pole will see it very low on the horizon.

在赤道，中午時太陽出現在頭頂正上方，也就是天頂。在溫帶地區（如英國），中午的太陽在地平線和天頂之間的某個位置。而在極地，它靠近地平線。但這告訴我們，其實不是太陽真的高了或低了，而是我們人類從不同角度看太陽。從地球的球體圖可以看出這是怎麼回事。赤道上的人看到太陽在正上方的天頂，我們這裡的人看到它在天空較低的位置，而極地的人則看到它很低地貼在地平線上。


The angle at which we see the sun at noon tells us where we are on earth between equator and pole. The nearer we are to the equator, the higher the sun will be at noon, and the closer we are to the pole, the lower the sun will be. So we know that in different parts of the earth, in different latitudes as it is called, the sun appears at different angles at noon.

我們在中午看到太陽的角度，告訴我們身處赤道和極地之間的什麼位置。越靠近赤道，中午的太陽越高；越靠近極地，太陽就越低。所以我們知道，在地球的不同地方——也就是不同的緯度——太陽在中午以不同角度出現。


But this angle at which the light of the sun comes to us makes all the difference to the whole of nature where we live. We can see it from this: If we draw a short line, and then draw as many sun-rays as we can, parallel to each other and falling at right angles on this line. And as we draw them, we count them. Now if we draw a line of the same length, but with parallel sun-rays falling on it from an acute angle, and we count again as we draw as many as we can; we'll find that there are far fewer rays at the acute angle than at the right angle.

而陽光照射到我們這裡的角度，對我們生活所在地的整個大自然造成了巨大差異。我們可以這樣理解：如果畫一條短線，然後盡可能多畫一些彼此平行、以直角落在這條線上的太陽光線，一邊畫一邊數。接著畫一條同樣長度的線，但讓平行的太陽光線以銳角落在上面，再一邊畫一邊數；我們會發現，銳角時的光線數量遠少於直角時。


Now we can understand that at a low angle the sun has less power, gives less light and less warmth than when it shines down at right angles. We can understand now why it is cold at the poles and hot on the equator and temperate, as it is called, in our part of the world. How people dress, what kind of house they build, what kind of plants and animals live around them, all depends on the angle of the sunlight.

現在我們就能理解，當太陽以低角度照射時，它的力量較小，給予的光和熱都比直角照射時少。我們現在能理解為什麼極地寒冷、赤道炎熱，而我們所處的地方則是所謂的溫帶了。人們穿什麼衣服、蓋什麼樣的房子、周圍生長什麼植物和動物，全都取決於陽光的照射角度。


We can also observe the difference which the angles make in a single day. Even on a very hot summer's day, it is cooler in the early morning and towards evening -- because the sun rays come in at a lower (or more acute) angle.

我們也可以在一天之內觀察到角度造成的差異。即使在非常炎熱的夏日，清晨和傍晚仍然比較涼爽——因為太陽光線以較低（或說更銳）的角度射入。


# 17. The Sun During the Year
# 17. 一年中的太陽

We saw how the path of the sun appears differently in different parts of the earth. At the equator, where the path of the sun rises at a right angle to the horizon, there are no seasons of the year. At the poles, where the sun circles in the sky parallel to the horizon, there are no times of the day. And in our part of the world we have both times of the day and the seasons of the year. Now we shall see how these two are connected with the path of the sun.

我們看到了太陽的運行路徑在地球不同地方呈現的不同樣貌。在赤道，太陽以直角從地平線升起的路徑使那裡沒有四季之分。在極地，太陽沿著平行於地平線的圓圈運行，因此沒有一天中的時刻之分。而在我們這個地方，我們既有一天中的時刻，也有一年中的四季。現在我們來看看這兩者如何與太陽的運行路徑相關聯。


In late autumn or early winter we have a chance to get up while it is still dark and see the sun rise (if it is not clouded). If we do this for several days and make a note of a landmark (like a house, tree or hill) where we see the sunrise. After a few days we shall see that the sunrise moves. And if we do the same in the evening we shall see that the sunset also moves. If each time we make a little drawing of what we see, then we would find that during autumn we find that sunrise moves towards the right and sunset moves left.

在深秋或初冬，我們有機會在天還黑的時候起床看日出（如果天氣晴朗的話）。如果我們連續幾天這樣做，並記下看到日出處的某個地標（如一棟房子、一棵樹或一座山丘）。幾天之後，我們會發現日出的位置移動了。如果傍晚也做同樣的觀察，會看到日落的位置也在移動。如果每次都畫一張小圖記錄所見，我們就會發現在秋天，日出向右移，日落向左移。


If you hold your left arm in the direction of sunrise and your right arm in the direction where the sun was setting on one day, and you do the same a few days later, you will see that the angle between your arms becomes smaller, narrower. And if you watch the sun at 12 o'clock (when it is at its highest), you will see that every day it is a little lower in the sky. As your arms between the directions of sunrise and sunset come closer together, and as your gaze towards the midday sun sinks lower, the days get shorter and shorter. From the movement of the arms and head you can see this is a kind of inbreathing.

如果你把左手臂伸向日出的方向，右手臂伸向那天日落的方向，過幾天再做一次，你會發現兩臂之間的角度變小了、變窄了。而如果你在中午十二點觀察太陽（那是太陽最高的時刻），你會看到它每天都稍微低了一些。隨著你的雙臂在日出和日落方向之間越收越攏，隨著你望向正午太陽的目光越降越低，白天變得越來越短。從手臂和頭部的動作，你可以看出這是一種吸入。


So we are losing sunlight in two ways: the days get shorter and the angle of the midday sun also gets less. We receive less light and less warmth.

所以我們在兩方面失去陽光：白天變短了，而正午太陽的角度也變小了。我們接收到的光和熱都減少了。


The shortening of the day and sinking of the midday sun will go on until December 21 or 22, the shortest day of the year. From December 23 onwards the angle of our arms between sunset and sunrise will widen, our eyes have to look higher and higher towards the midday sun. The days get longer. Then on March 20 or 21 day and night are of the same length, twelve hours.

白日的縮短和正午太陽的下沉會持續到十二月二十一日或二十二日，也就是一年中最短的一天。從十二月二十三日起，我們雙臂在日落和日出之間的角度會重新擴大，我們的目光必須越望越高才能追上正午的太陽。白天變長了。到了三月二十日或二十一日，日夜等長，各十二小時。


During the time from December 23 onwards the points of sunset and sunrise move, but not as they did before, now sunrise moves to the left and the sunset to the right. And they continue this journey, the sun being higher at midday and its journey over the sky lasting longer, until June 21, the longest day of the year. The movement of our arms and head following the sunrise, sunset and noon become like an outbreathing.

從十二月二十三日起，日落和日出的位置在移動，但方向與之前相反——現在日出向左移，日落向右移。它們繼續這趟旅程，太陽在正午時越升越高，它穿越天空的旅程也持續得越來越久，直到六月二十一日，一年中最長的一天。我們的手臂和頭部跟隨日出、日落和正午而做的動作，變得像是一種呼出。


From June 21 the days shorten again, the midday sun sinks lower and on September 22 or 23 day and night are of equal length again.

從六月二十一日起，白天又開始縮短，正午的太陽再度下沉，到了九月二十二日或二十三日，日夜再次等長。


So we have one longest and one shortest day in the year, and two days when day and night are equally long, one in spring and one in autumn. These days are called equinoxes (equal night). March 21 is the spring equinox, and September 23 is the autumn equinox. The longest and the shortest day, when the sun turns, are called the solstice. June 22 is the summer solstice, and December 22 the winter solstice.

所以一年中有一個最長和一個最短的白天，還有兩天日夜等長，一天在春天，一天在秋天。這些日子被稱為「分」（equinox，意即等夜）。三月二十一日是春分，九月二十三日是秋分。最長和最短的日子，太陽轉向的時刻，叫做「至」（solstice）。六月二十二日是夏至，十二月二十二日是冬至。


We can now see the height of the midday sun and the length of the day go together. The higher the sun, the more light rays, the more warmth.

我們現在可以看出，正午太陽的高度和白天的長度是一致的。太陽越高，光線越多，溫暖也越多。


Let us look once more at the movements of sunset and sunrise. When we first looked at this we found in late autumn sunrise moves to the right and sunset to left. If we think of the cardinal points of the compass, to the right of east is south, and to the left of west is south. That means both points move south. It seems strange, but in winter both sunset and sunrise move south. At the winter solstice sunrise is in the south-east, sunset is in the south-west. And in the summer sunrise and sunset both move north. On the longest day, at the summer solstice, sunset and sunrise are furthest north, in the north-east and the north-west. Only on the two equinox days, March 21 and September 23, does the sun rise exactly in the east and set exactly in the west.

讓我們再看一次日落和日出的移動。當我們第一次觀察時，發現在深秋日出向右移、日落向左移。如果我們想想羅盤的基本方位：東邊的右方是南，西邊的左方也是南。這意味著兩個點都向南移動。這看起來很奇怪，但在冬天，日出和日落都往南移。在冬至時，日出在東南方，日落在西南方。而在夏天，日出和日落都向北移。在最長的一天，也就是夏至，日落和日出最靠北，分別在東北方和西北方。只有在春分和秋分這兩天，太陽才正好從正東升起、在正西落下。


During the course of one day the sun rises and sets, it goes up and goes down. And during the course of a year the path of the sun goes up and goes down. Additionally, the path of the sun moves northwards for half a year (from the winter to the summer solstice) and then southwards for half a year (from the summer to the winter solstice).

在一天之中，太陽升起又落下，上升又下降。在一年之中，太陽的路徑也上升又下降。此外，太陽的路徑有半年向北移動（從冬至到夏至），然後有半年向南移動（從夏至到冬至）。


This twofold movement of the path of the sun (up-down, north-south) can best be seen in the polar regions. If we were standing at the North Pole any direction in which we look or walk is south. The North Pole is the furthest we can go north on earth, and any step away from the North Pole is a step south.

太陽路徑這種雙重運動（上下、南北）在極地地區最容易看出。如果我們站在北極，任何我們面向或行走的方向都是南方。北極是地球上我們能走到的最北端，離開北極的每一步都是向南的一步。


In summer at the North Pole you see the sun circling in the sky. Towards autumn it sinks lower, and in which direction does the path of the sun go as it sinks? It moves to the south. In the long winter nights when the sun does not rise at all in the Arctic the sun is too far south to be seen.

在夏天的北極，你看到太陽在天空中繞圈。到了秋天它逐漸下沉，而太陽路徑下沉時往哪個方向去呢？它向南移動。在漫長的冬夜裡，北極的太陽根本不會升起——它已經太偏南了，看不見了。


On the equator this twofold movement of the sun's path can also be seen but not as clearly as at the Pole. In December the sun rises and sets a little to the south of east and west, and in June it rises and sets a little to the north. There is no difference in the length of the day and only a little variation of the height of the sun at noon. In December it is a little to the south of the zenith, the point overhead, and in June a little to the north. Only at the equinoxes does the noon sun go exactly overhead through the zenith, at the equator.

在赤道上也能看到太陽路徑的這種雙重運動，但不如在極地那麼明顯。十二月時，太陽稍偏東西之南升起和落下；六月時則稍偏北。白天的長度沒有差異，正午太陽的高度也只有微小的變化。十二月，它稍微在天頂的南邊，六月則稍在北邊。只有在春分和秋分，正午的太陽才恰好通過赤道上方的天頂。


The sun's path is not really a circle but, during the course of the year, it is a spiral. For the sun does not return to the point where it was the day before. At the North Pole we would be able to see the sun's path spiralling up from spring equinox to summer solstice and then spiralling down until the autumn equinox. We would be able to see the entire spiral for half a year.

太陽的路徑其實不是圓，而是在一年當中形成一條螺旋。因為太陽不會回到前一天所在的那個點。在北極，我們能看到太陽的路徑從春分到夏至螺旋上升，然後從夏至到秋分螺旋下降。我們能看到半年裡完整的螺旋。


At the equator we would be able to see half the spiral for the whole year (as the sun is above the horizon for twelve hours every day). In our part of the world we have something in between, for half the year (the summer half) we can see more than half of the spiral, and in the winter half of the year we see less than half of the spiral.

在赤道上，我們全年都能看到螺旋的一半（因為太陽每天都在地平線上方十二個小時）。在我們這裡則介於兩者之間，半年（夏半年）我們能看到螺旋的一半以上，冬半年我們看到的則不到一半。


This spiral movement that goes up and down gives us the seasons of the year which are such a familiar part of our life.

這個上下移動的螺旋運動給了我們四季——它們是我們生活中如此熟悉的一部分。


# 18. The Calendar
# 18. 曆法

As long as people only hunted, as in the early Stone Age, they did not have to watch the seasons very carefully. They could hunt animals in winter as well as in summer. But when agriculture began, in the New Stone Age, in ancient Persian times, people began to sow and harvest crops and the change of seasons became very important.

在人們只靠狩獵維生的時候，如舊石器時代早期，他們不需要特別留意季節。冬天或夏天都可以獵捕動物。但當農業開始以後，在新石器時代，在古波斯時期，人們開始播種和收穫，季節的變化就變得非常重要了。


The first farmers, the first peasants, were also the first people who needed a calendar. Different crops -- grain and vegetables -- have to be sown and harvested at different times of the year, so the farmers had to know what time of the year it was. But there were no calendars (there were no books at all) and the people had to find ways to ensure they knew when to sow their crops.

最早的農人，最早的農民，也是最早需要曆法的人。不同的作物——穀物和蔬菜——必須在一年中不同的時節播種和收穫，所以農人必須知道當時是什麼時節。然而那時沒有曆法（根本沒有書），人們不得不想辦法確定何時該播種。


In Britain, for instance, the wise priests who guided the people built the great stone circle of Stonehenge. It was a holy place, but it was also a kind of enormous calendar. The stones were landmarks for the path of the sun through the year. The priests watched specially the shadows cast by the stones, for the shadows change in the course of the year. The shadows were like the hands of a great clock which showed not hours, but months and from the shadows the priests could tell the people when it was time to sow or to shear the sheep.

例如在英國，引導民眾的智慧祭司們建造了宏偉的巨石陣。那是一個神聖的場所，但同時也是一種巨大的曆法裝置。石頭是太陽全年運行路徑的地標。祭司們特別觀察石頭投下的影子，因為影子在一年之中會變化。這些影子就像一座巨大時鐘的指針，指示的不是小時而是月份，祭司們從影子中可以告訴人們什麼時候該播種，什麼時候該剪羊毛。


Far away in Asia, in Babylonia, the priests also observed the path of the sun. Babylonia was already a great civilization with mighty cities, and the priests built great observatories from where they carefully and patiently watched the path of sun, moon and stars.

遠在亞洲的巴比倫，祭司們也觀察太陽的運行路徑。巴比倫已經是一個擁有偉大城市的強盛文明，祭司們建造了宏偉的天文台，從那裡仔細而耐心地觀測太陽、月亮和星辰的軌跡。


It was not only for agriculture, for the priests of Babylonia said that just as certain plants grow only at a certain time of the year, so a great warrior, for instance, can only be born in a certain time of the year, in the month after the spring equinox. But a boy born, say, in February would make a learned priest. It was like this for every month, even for every day of the year. When a child was born, the priests of Babylonia told the parents what kind of destiny this child would have, according to the time of birth.

但這不僅僅是為了農業。巴比倫的祭司們說，正如某些植物只在一年中的特定時節生長，一位偉大的戰士，例如，也只能在一年中特定的時節出生——在春分之後的那個月。而在二月出生的男孩則會成為一位有學問的祭司。每個月都是如此，甚至一年中的每一天都有說法。當一個孩子出生時，巴比倫的祭司會根據出生時間告訴父母這個孩子將有什麼樣的命運。


That is why the Babylonian priests observed sun, moon and stars so carefully and why they became the people who gave us the division of the year into twelve months and into fifty-two weeks and the week into seven days, and the day into twice twelve hours. All these measurements of time go back to the priests of Babylonia, the land between the Euphrates and the Tigris.

這就是為什麼巴比倫的祭司如此仔細地觀測太陽、月亮和星辰，也是為什麼他們成為給予我們將一年分為十二個月、五十二週、一週七天、一天分為兩個十二小時這些時間劃分的人。所有這些時間的度量都可以追溯到巴比倫的祭司——那片幼發拉底河與底格里斯河之間的土地。


To find how many days were in the year, the priests of Babylonia measured the shadow of a pillar or obelisk very exactly at noon on the longest day of the year, the summer solstice. At that moment the shadow would be shorter than at any other time of the year. And then they counted the days until the shadow was again of the same short length. They counted 365 days. But at noon on the 365th day the shadow was a little longer which meant the sun was not where it had been the last time. So they waited another 365 days, and after that time the shadow was still longer than the first time. And the same thing happened after another 365 days. So they had gone three times through 365 days without getting the same length of shadow on the longest day of the year. The next time, the fourth time, they did get the same shadow lengths as the first time, but after 366 days, not 365 days. The reason was that the real length of the year is not 365 days, but three hundred and sixty-five and a quarter days, or 365 days and 6 hours. And that is why we have one extra day -- February 29 -- every four years, the leap year.

為了找出一年有多少天，巴比倫的祭司在一年中最長的一天——夏至——的正午，非常精確地測量一根柱子或方尖碑的影子。在那個時刻，影子會比一年中任何其他時候都短。然後他們開始數日子，直到影子再次達到同樣的短度。他們數了三百六十五天。但在第三百六十五天的正午，影子稍微長了一些，這意味著太陽還沒有回到上次的位置。所以他們再等三百六十五天，而那時候影子仍然比第一次長。再過三百六十五天，同樣的情況再度發生。所以他們經歷了三個三百六十五天，卻沒能在年中最長日得到相同長度的影子。下一次，第四次，他們終於得到了和第一次相同長度的影子，但花了三百六十六天，而不是三百六十五天。原因是一年的真正長度不是三百六十五天，而是三百六十五又四分之一天，即三百六十五天六小時。這就是為什麼每四年有一個閏年，多出一天——二月二十九日。


The priests of Babylonia discovered by measuring shadows that the true length of the year is 365 1/4 days. The Romans found this out by another way. They at first counted 365 days, year after year. After four years they were only one day ahead of the sun and no one noticed any difference. But after one hundred and twenty years they were one month ahead of the sun -- they called the month April, but the sun was still at the equinox in March. Different things were tried to make things right again, but it became worse until the time of Julius Caesar. Caesar had travelled in Egypt where the priests knew that the year was longer than 365 days. It was Julius Caesar who changed the Roman calendar and introduced the leap year. And the calendar he introduced is called the Julian calendar.

巴比倫的祭司通過測量影子發現一年的真正長度是三百六十五又四分之一天。羅馬人用另一種方式發現了這一點。他們起初年復一年地數三百六十五天。四年之後，他們只比太陽快了一天，沒有人注意到什麼差別。但一百二十年之後，他們比太陽快了一整個月——他們稱那個月為四月，但太陽卻仍在三月的春分。人們嘗試了各種方法來糾正，但情況越來越糟，直到凱撒的時代。凱撒曾到過埃及，那裡的祭司知道一年比三百六十五天更長。正是凱撒改變了羅馬曆法，引入了閏年。他引入的曆法被稱為儒略曆。


But the length of the year is not exactly 365 days and 6 hours, it is 365 days 5 hours 48 minutes and 45 seconds. Julius Caesar did not know this, but this little mistake made his calendar wrong. Every year people were eleven and a quarter minutes behind the sun. That's very little in one year, but after 1600 years this little difference had become ten days. People were ten days behind the sun, or you could say the sun was ten days ahead of the calendar. If this had gone on people would have celebrated Christmas a month after the winter solstice instead of two days after it.

但一年的長度並不精確地是三百六十五天六小時，而是三百六十五天五小時四十八分四十五秒。凱撒不知道這一點，但這個小小的誤差使他的曆法出了錯。每年人們都比太陽慢十一又四分之一分鐘。一年裡這微不足道，但一千六百年之後，這個微小的差異累積成了十天。人們比太陽慢了十天，或者可以說太陽比曆法快了十天。如果繼續下去，人們將在冬至後一個月才慶祝聖誕節，而不是冬至後兩天。


In 1582 the Pope of that time, Gregory XIII, made another change in the calendar. First, to get things back on track, ten days were struck out. Thursday, October 4, was followed not by the 5th, but by Friday, October 15. Many people did not like that at all. In Britain (where this change was made seventy years later because of a quarrel with the Pope) there were riots because people thought the government had robbed them of ten days of their lives.

一五八二年，當時的教宗額我略十三世（Gregory XIII）對曆法做了另一次修改。首先，為了讓一切重新回到正軌，十天被刪去。十月四日星期四之後，接的不是五號，而是十月十五日星期五。很多人非常不滿。在英國（由於與教宗的爭執，這項改變遲了七十年才實施），甚至爆發了暴動，因為人們認為政府偷走了他們生命中的十天。


The ten days struck off the calendar only corrected the past mistake. In future to adjust the year for the eleven and a quarter minutes difference, the rule that is still followed to this day, is that:

刪去的十天只是糾正了過去的錯誤。為了在未來調整每年十一又四分之一分鐘的差異，至今仍在遵循的規則是：


-- every fourth year is a leap year (that is any year that can be divided by four, like 1868, 1992 or 2016)

——每四年是一個閏年（也就是任何能被四整除的年份，如一八六八年、一九九二年或二零一六年）


-- but every century is not a leap year, except those which can be divided by 400 (so 1700, 1800, 1900 were not leap years, but 1600 and 2000 were leap years).

——但每個世紀之交不是閏年，除了能被四百整除的（所以一七零零年、一八零零年、一九零零年不是閏年，但一六零零年和二零零零年是閏年）。


The year seems quite a simple thing, but we now see what a complicated business it is. And even this complicated rule, called the Gregorian calendar after the Pope, is still not quite correct. We are now gaining 11 seconds every year, but as it will take about 4,000 years for this error to grow to a full day, we don't need to worry about it.

「年」看起來是一件很簡單的事，但我們現在看到它是多麼複雜。即使這套以教宗命名的複雜規則——格里曆——仍然不是完全精確的。我們現在每年多出十一秒，但要讓這個誤差累積到整整一天，大約需要四千年，所以我們不必擔心。


At the root of the matter is the problem that the real length of a year cannot be divided by any whole number without a remainder, or if calculated in decimals it would go on endlessly. The length of a year is an irrational number, as such numbers are called. The path of the sun cannot be put into simple numbers.

問題的根源在於，一年的真正長度無法被任何整數整除而沒有餘數，或者用小數來算的話，小數會無限延伸下去。一年的長度是一個所謂的無理數。太陽的軌跡無法用簡單的數字來表達。


# 19. Sundials and Time
# 19. 日晷與時間

We heard how the wise men in Babylonia watched the shadow of a pillar and in ancient Britain watched the shadow of the stones at Stonehenge. From the shadow they could tell the people when it was time to plant grain and when it was time to shear the sheep.

我們聽說了巴比倫的智者如何觀察柱子的影子，古代英國的人如何觀察巨石陣石頭的影子。從影子中他們可以告訴人們什麼時候該種穀物，什麼時候該剪羊毛。


The shadow cast by the sun is altogether very interesting. At the poles -- where the sun stays at the same height all day as it goes round the sky -- what would the shadow of a stick put straight into the snow, show? The shadow would stay the same length all day; it would not get shorter or longer, as the sun remains at the same height. And it would wander around the stick in an exact circle. (To be quite precise it would move in a spiral, getting a little shorter or longer as it went round, depending on whether the sun was climbing up or down.) We know that the higher the sun is in the sky the shorter the shadow will be. At the poles the shadow will be quite long for the sun does not get very high.

太陽投下的影子非常有趣。在極地——太陽整天繞著天空走但保持同一高度——如果把一根棍子直直插在雪裡，影子會是什麼樣子呢？影子整天會保持同一長度；不會變短或變長，因為太陽始終在同一高度。而且它會繞著棍子走出一個精確的圓圈。（嚴格來說，它會走出一個螺旋，繞行時稍微變短或變長，取決於太陽是在爬升還是下降。）我們知道太陽在天空中越高，影子就越短。在極地，影子會相當長，因為太陽升不了太高。


We can also easily imagine the shadow of a stick at the equator. At one of the equinoxes the sun rises exactly in the east, goes right up through the zenith (exactly overhead) and then sets exactly in the west. At sunrise and at sunset the shadow will be very long, and at noon when the sun is in the zenith, there will be no shadow at all. When the sun rises exactly in the east the shadow will point straight west, and at sunset it will point straight east. A line from true east to true west is a straight line, so on that day the shadow of the stick will not move round the stick at all, it will remain a straight line, first pointing west, then getting shorter and shorter until it disappears under the stick, and then pointing east getting longer and longer, but all the time it will keep on the same straight line.

我們也可以輕易想像赤道上一根棍子的影子。在其中一個分日，太陽正好從正東升起，直升到天頂（正頭頂），然後正好從正西落下。日出和日落時影子會很長，而中午太陽在天頂時，完全沒有影子。太陽從正東升起時，影子會直指正西；日落時，影子會直指正東。從正東到正西是一條直線，所以那天棍子的影子根本不會繞著棍子轉，它會保持在一條直線上，先指向西邊，然後越來越短直到消失在棍子底下，接著指向東邊越來越長，但始終保持在同一條直線上。


So even in the shadows the pole and the equator are opposites. In the course of a day at the pole the shadow keeps the same length, and goes round in a circle, while on the equator the shadow changes its length, from long to nothing to long, and moves in a straight line.

所以即使在影子中，極地和赤道也是相反的。在極地，一天之中影子保持同一長度，繞成一個圓圈；而在赤道，影子改變長度，從長到無再到長，沿著一條直線移動。


For us who live in temperate climates the shadow will not move in a straight line or in a circle. It will change its length, longer in the morning and evening and shortest at noon, but what shape will the path of the shadow make if it's neither a circle nor a straight line?

對我們這些住在溫帶的人來說，影子既不會沿直線也不會沿圓圈移動。它的長度會改變，早晚較長，中午最短。但如果既不是圓也不是直線，影子走出的路徑會是什麼形狀呢？


We can find the answer by experiment. Take a sheet of paper and fix it to a board and fix a large needle or nail vertically to the board. Now put the board on a window sill or flat surface outside, making sure it is horizontal, and that it catches the sun for as much of the day as possible. Then every half hour, or as often as possible, mark the point where the shadow ends.

我們可以通過實驗找到答案。拿一張紙固定在板子上，再把一根大針或釘子垂直固定在板子上。然後把板子放在窗台或室外的平面上，確保它是水平的，而且盡可能一整天都能接受陽光。然後每半小時，或盡可能頻繁地，標記影子末端的位置。


If all is set up well, and we have good weather, we shall have a complete set of points. When we connect these points we find they make a curve. If we have done this in winter when the sun rises in the south-east there will be a long shadow pointing north-west, at noon when the sun is in the south there will be a shorter shadow to the north, and at sunset (in the south-west) there will be a long shadow pointing to the north-east.

如果一切都設置好了，天氣也好，我們就會得到一整組完整的點。當我們連接這些點時，會發現它們構成一條曲線。如果我們在冬天做這個實驗，太陽從東南升起時會有一條長影子指向西北，中午太陽在正南時會有一條較短的影子指向北方，日落時（太陽在西南方）會有一條長影子指向東北方。


If we did this every month for a year we would find a set of curves as shown overleaf. Among these curves is a straight line, which is the shadow cast by the sun at the equinox when it rises exactly in the east, and sets exactly in the west. But as we are not on the equator the top of the shadow does not disappear exactly under the stick, but still has a length, and so is north of the stick.

如果我們全年每個月都做一次，會發現一組曲線。在這些曲線中有一條直線，那就是太陽在春秋分時投下的影子——這天太陽正好從正東升起、在正西落下。但由於我們不在赤道上，影子的頂端不會恰好消失在棍子底下，仍然有一段長度，所以位於棍子的北邊。


A vertical stick at the North Pole would be a perfect sundial. Draw a circle round the stick and mark twenty-four hours around it. The shadow would then show the time. But in our part of the world we would have to put the stick parallel to that stick at the Pole -- for Edinburgh that would be at an angle of 56 degrees to the horizontal (the latitude of Edinburgh). The gnomon, as the stick of a sundial is called, is always at an angle. If you measured the angle you would find it is always the same as the latitude of the place where the sundial stands.

在北極豎直插一根棍子就是一個完美的日晷。在棍子周圍畫一個圓，標上二十四個小時。影子就會顯示時間。但在我們這個地方，我們必須讓棍子與極地的那根棍子平行——對愛丁堡來說，那就是與水平面成五十六度角（愛丁堡的緯度）。日晷上的指針叫做「晷針」（gnomon），它總是傾斜的。如果你測量這個角度，會發現它永遠等於日晷所在地的緯度。


When the shadow is shortest it is noon. Our watch will not show exactly twelve o'clock, because our clocks do not go by the true time shown by the sun. During the course of the year, the sun sometimes moves a little faster, sometimes a little slower, while our clocks rigidly keep to the same speed. So there can be differences of up to 15 minutes between the sun's noon and clock noon.

當影子最短時就是正午。我們的手錶不會正好顯示十二點，因為我們的鐘表並不按照太陽顯示的真正時間走。在一年之中，太陽有時走得稍快，有時稍慢，而我們的鐘表嚴格保持同一速度。所以太陽的正午和鐘錶的正午之間可能有多達十五分鐘的差異。


Another thing which can make an even bigger difference is the following. The further west you go, the later the sun rises and sets, and the later it will be at its highest at noon. At the latitude of London (51 1/2 degrees) for every 17 km (11 miles) you go west, the sun rises one minute later. So Bristol's real or local time is ten minutes behind London's. Before the days of railways each town and village kept its own local time, and that worked fine for everyday life. But when the railways were built and trains ran to timetables, a standard time was introduced across the whole country. In Britain we keep to Greenwich Mean Time, the time of London's observatory in Greenwich.

另一件能造成更大差異的事是這樣的。你越往西走，太陽升起和落下就越遲，中午太陽到達最高點也越遲。在倫敦的緯度（五十一度半），每往西走十七公里（十一英里），太陽就晚一分鐘升起。所以布里斯托的真正或地方時間比倫敦慢十分鐘。在鐵路時代之前，每個城鎮和村莊都使用自己的地方時間，這對日常生活來說完全夠用。但鐵路建成後，火車按時刻表運行，全國就引入了統一的標準時間。在英國，我們使用格林威治標準時間——倫敦格林威治天文台的時間。


Going further west, in New York it is noon five hours after it is noon in London. So it is still seven in the morning when it's noon in Britain. And going east, Beijing is eight hours ahead of Britain. While each country could have its own time, most countries in the world now keep to a time that is a whole number of hours different from Greenwich Mean Time. So travelling between Britain and Germany, for instance, there is exactly one hour time difference, or travelling between Sydney in Australia and Britain there is exactly 10 hours difference. Some countries stretch so far east and west that they have several time zones in the same country: the United States (including Alaska and Hawaii) has 6 time zones, each an hour apart, and Russia has 10!

再往西走，紐約的正午比倫敦的正午晚五個小時。所以英國正午時，紐約還是早上七點。往東走，北京比英國快八個小時。雖然每個國家可以有自己的時間，但世界上大多數國家現在都使用與格林威治標準時間相差整數小時的時間。所以在英國和德國之間旅行，時差正好是一個小時；在澳洲雪梨和英國之間旅行，時差正好是十個小時。有些國家東西跨度太大，在同一國家內就有好幾個時區：美國（包括阿拉斯加和夏威夷）有六個時區，每個相差一小時，而俄羅斯有十個！


# 20. The Circling Stars and the Pole Star
# 20. 旋轉的星辰與北極星

We have looked at the sun in connection with time: the time of day by the rising and setting of the sun itself, and the time of the year by the change in the whole path of the sun. And we have looked at the first clocks, the sundials, that tell the time of day, and the stones of Stonehenge which were a kind of clock for the year. Now we shall look at the directions of space, something that is also connected to the sun.

我們已經從時間的角度看過太陽：通過太陽的升落來看一天的時間，通過太陽整條路徑的變化來看一年的時間。我們也看過了最早的時鐘——日晷，它們標示一天中的時刻，以及巨石陣的石頭，那是一種年度時鐘。現在我們來看看空間的方向——這也和太陽有關。


If, for instance on our holidays, we come to a town or village where we have never been before it takes some time until we know the layout of the streets. But a bee flying from its hive in search of nectar has no streets to go through, nor can bees see very far. Yet they often collect their nectar far out of sight of their hive, and always find their way back. They can even tell other bees where they have found a rich supply of nectar. Scientists who study bees discovered that the bees find their way by knowing at any time at which angle to the sun they have been flying. Strangely the movement of the sun over the sky does not matter to the bees, nor does it matter if the sky is overcast. They do not find their way by looking for landmarks on the ground (as we would do), they are guided by the position of the sun, and that it moves does not matter to them.

譬如在假期裡，我們來到一個從未去過的城鎮或村莊，需要一些時間才能弄清街道的佈局。但一隻從蜂巢飛出去尋找花蜜的蜜蜂既沒有街道可循，視力也看不了多遠。然而牠們常常在蜂巢視線之外很遠的地方採蜜，卻總能找到回去的路。牠們甚至能告訴其他蜜蜂在哪裡找到了豐富的花蜜。研究蜜蜂的科學家發現，蜜蜂靠著隨時知道自己飛行方向與太陽的角度來辨路。奇妙的是，太陽在天空中的移動對蜜蜂沒有影響，天空是否多雲也無所謂。牠們不像我們那樣通過尋找地面上的地標來辨路，而是以太陽的位置為指引，太陽會移動這件事對牠們毫無影響。


And scientists now believe that not only bees but also birds which fly south in winter (like swallows which fly all the way to Africa) use the sun to guide them in the right direction.

科學家現在相信，不僅蜜蜂，冬天南飛的鳥類（如燕子一路飛到非洲）也利用太陽來引導正確的方向。


Birds and bees are born with this wisdom -- or instinct as it is called -- which tells them how to guide themselves with the help of the sun. We human beings have not such instincts; we look for landmarks -- the streets of a city, roads and paths in the countryside, or hills, trees and rivers when there are no roads.

鳥和蜜蜂天生就有這種智慧——或者稱之為本能——它告訴牠們如何借助太陽為自己導航。我們人類沒有這種本能；我們尋找地標——城市的街道、鄉間的道路與小徑，或者在沒有路的地方找山丘、樹木和河流。


But there are no landmarks on the sea. And when the first people took to boats they also had to look up to the sky, to the sun, to give them the direction in which they were going.

但海上沒有地標。當最早的人們開始乘船時，他們也不得不仰望天空、仰望太陽，來確認航行的方向。


When in Greek or Roman times a ship sailed from Italy to Phoenicia -- that is to Asia -- they sailed in the direction of the rising sun. And that is why they called these lands of Asia the Orient. The word "Orient" means "rising." The Orient is the land which lies where we see the sun rising. And we have the verb "orientate," which means to find one's way about. "I have to orientate myself," means "I have to find out if I am going in the right direction." The phrase "to orientate oneself" goes right back to the times when sailors sailed by the sun.

在希臘或羅馬時代，一艘船從義大利駛向腓尼基——也就是亞洲——他們朝著太陽升起的方向航行。這就是為什麼他們把亞洲的土地稱為「東方」（Orient）。「Orient」這個詞意思是「升起」。東方就是我們看到太陽升起之處的土地。而我們有一個動詞「orientate」（辨別方向），意思是找到自己的路。「我得辨別一下方向」意思是「我得弄清楚自己走的方向對不對」。「辨別方向」這個說法一路追溯到水手們靠太陽航行的年代。


When the same ship sailed back to Italy, to Europe, it sailed in the direction of the setting sun. And Europe became the Occident, meaning "setting," the land of the setting sun. Even in our time, in geography, we still speak of the countries of the Near East and the Far East; and the civilization of Europe and America is called "western" civilization. So we still use the sun to orientate ourselves in geography.

當同一艘船返航回義大利、回歐洲時，它朝著太陽落下的方向航行。於是歐洲成了「西方」（Occident），意思是「落下」，太陽西沉之地。即使在我們的時代，在地理學中，我們仍然說近東和遠東的國家；歐美文明被稱為「西方」文明。所以我們仍然用太陽來為自己在地理上定位。


Most of our maps are made so that north is up, and south down, east on the right and west on the left. These four directions (the cardinal points) are taken from the sun's path over the sky.

我們大多數地圖的繪製方式是北在上、南在下、東在右、西在左。這四個方向（基本方位）就是取自太陽在天空中的路徑。


All this goes back to the first sailors who had no landmarks and had to guide themselves by the sun. It is wonderful, when you come to think of it, that in order to find their way here on earth, the sailors of ancient times had to look up to the sun.

這一切都追溯到最早那些沒有地標、必須靠太陽導航的水手。仔細想想，這真是奇妙——為了在地球上找到自己的路，古代水手們必須仰望太陽。


But none of the sailors of ancient times were ever far from land. Their journeys were short hops from one island to the next, and the Mediterranean Sea has so many islands that it was fairly easy to get across in any direction. Only when a storm blew a ship off course did the captain no longer know where he was with his boat, and had to trust his luck to find some land, a landmark, soon. None of these sailors of ancient times would have ventured out into seas that were unknown. If a ship did make a long journey, say from Gibraltar to Constantinople the sailors kept close to the African coast. And if they sailed from Gibraltar to Britain, they were never far from the coast of Portugal or France. Being close to the coast was the only way to know where they were. In winter when storms were more likely, ships did not sail at all.

但古代的水手從來不會遠離陸地。他們的航程只是從一個島跳到下一個島，而地中海有那麼多島嶼，要往任何方向橫渡都相當容易。只有當風暴把船吹離航線時，船長才不再知道自己在哪裡，只能靠運氣盡快找到陸地、找到地標。古代的水手沒有人會冒險駛入未知的海域。如果一艘船真要走長途，比如從直布羅陀到君士坦丁堡，水手們會沿著非洲海岸走。如果從直布羅陀駛向英國，他們也從不遠離葡萄牙或法國的海岸。靠近海岸是知道自己在哪裡的唯一方法。冬天風暴更多，船根本不會出海。


The first European sailors who dared to venture out into unknown seas were the Vikings who sailed to Iceland, Greenland and Vinland (Flaki used ravens to give him the direction to the nearest land). They did this all without maps or compass, and they could never know exactly where they were on the sea; they could only say, "It took two days rowing north-west," or "three days rowing east." They did not have watches or clocks to tell them the exact time it had taken.

最早敢於冒險駛入未知海域的歐洲水手是維京人，他們航行到了冰島、格陵蘭和文蘭（弗洛基用渡鴉來指引他最近陸地的方向）。這一切都是在沒有地圖和羅盤的情況下完成的，他們永遠無法確切知道自己在海上的位置；他們只能說，「往西北划了兩天」，或「往東划了三天」。他們沒有鐘表來告訴他們確切花了多長時間。


But the Greeks, the Romans and the Vikings all had to sail at night as well as by day, for they could not always find a convenient island or a harbour when darkness fell. When they looked up to the countless stars in the sky they saw that the whole sky with all the stars moved. Like the sun, the starry sky moved from east to west. The stars moved in circles, but all the circles of the stars had the same centre: the stars moved in concentric circles. In the centre of all the stars' circles there was one star that never moved at all, it always stayed in the same place. They called this star the Pole Star, or Polaris.

但希臘人、羅馬人和維京人都必須在夜間也航行，因為天黑時不見得總能找到方便的島嶼或港口。當他們仰望天空中無數的星辰，看到整片星空都在移動。就像太陽一樣，星空從東向西運轉。星星沿著圓圈運動，但所有星星的圓圈有著同一個圓心：星星們在同心圓上運動。在所有星星圓圈的中心，有一顆星完全不動，它始終待在同一個位置。他們稱這顆星為北極星（Pole Star），或 Polaris。


It can easily be found by looking at a group of bright stars called the Plough or the Great Bear. If you follow a line from the last two stars of the Plough you come to the Pole Star. If you watch it for a time you can see the whole Plough slowly swinging round the Pole Star, but the last two stars always point to it.

可以很容易地通過觀察一組明亮的星星找到它——那組星叫做犁（北斗七星）或大熊座。如果你沿著北斗七星最後兩顆星的連線延伸，就會找到北極星。如果你觀察一段時間，可以看到整個北斗七星緩慢地繞著北極星旋轉，但最後兩顆星總是指向它。


Not only is the Pole Star the only star that stands still, but it also stands exactly in the north. If you look in the direction of the Pole Star you are looking exactly north. We can see why the Pole Star was so important to sailors; they could always find it on a cloudless night and it showed them exactly where north was. No matter whether they sailed east, south or north-west, they could get their bearings by saying: if the Pole Star is there in the north, then east is at a right angle, and so on.

北極星不僅是唯一靜止不動的星，而且正好位於北方。如果你朝北極星的方向看，你就是在看正北方。我們可以理解為什麼北極星對水手如此重要；在晴朗的夜晚他們總能找到它，它精確地指出北方在哪裡。不管他們往東、往南還是往西北航行，都可以靠著北極星來確定方位：如果北極星在北邊的那裡，那麼東邊就與它成直角，依此類推。


Sailors in ancient times could orientate themselves in the day time by the sun which is in the south at midday, and at night time by the Pole Star which is always in the north.

古代水手白天靠正午在南方的太陽辨別方向，夜晚則靠始終在北方的北極星。


# 21. The Curvature of the Earth
# 21. 地球的弧度

These were the two things which puzzled the Greek sailors: approaching an island over a flat sea the island appeared as if they were walking up a hill; and that the Pole Star stood higher in the north than in the south.

有兩件事讓希臘水手感到困惑：在平坦的海面上駛近一座島嶼時，那座島看起來好像他們在爬一座山丘；還有北極星在北方比在南方高。


In Alexandria, the great city of learning and knowledge that Alexander the Great had founded in Egypt, there were wise and learned men who found the answer to the sailors' puzzles. These wise men said that the earth is round, it is a globe.

在亞歷山卓——亞歷山大大帝在埃及建立的那座偉大的學術和知識之城——有智慧淵博的學者找到了水手們困惑的答案。這些智者說：地球是圓的，它是一個球體。


It was rather like when we walk up a hill and on the other side is a village with a high church tower. At first we will only see the top of the tower over the hilltop, then we will see more of the tower, and only when we get to the top will we see the whole village. And the sailors of ancient times, looking at the flat expanse of sea before them, wondered why it was that this flat, calm sea (on a calm day) was like a hill when they approached an island. Yet they knew they were not sailing uphill!

這很像我們爬上一座山丘，山的另一邊有個村莊，有座高高的教堂塔樓。起初我們只看到塔尖露在山頂上方，然後看到塔的更多部分，只有當我們走到山頂才能看見整個村莊。古代水手們望著眼前平坦的海面，想不明白為什麼這片平靜的海（在風平浪靜的日子裡）在他們駛近一座島嶼時彷彿是一座山丘。然而他們知道自己並沒有在往上坡航行！


The other puzzling thing was the Pole Star itself. In the Mediterranean, where most of the sailing was done, the Pole Star is not very high over the horizon. If you held one arm horizontally and lifted the other to point at the Pole Star, the angle between your arms would be no more than 35 degrees. But when these sailors from the Mediterranean sailed north, say to the coast of Britain, the Pole Star stood higher in the sky; the angle was 50 degrees or more above the horizon. They knew the Pole Star does not move, but the further north they went the higher the Pole Star stood, and further south it stood lower.

另一件令人困惑的事是北極星本身。在地中海——大多數航行發生的地方——北極星並不很高。如果你一隻手臂平舉，另一隻手臂抬起指向北極星，兩臂之間的角度不超過三十五度。但當這些地中海的水手向北航行，比方說到英國海岸時，北極星在天空中就高了許多；角度在地平線上方五十度甚至更高。他們知道北極星是不動的，但越往北走北極星就越高，越往南走它就越低。


If the earth is round the look-out on a ship will see first the peaks of a mountain -- it will be like going up a hill. And if the earth is round and the Pole Star stands in the zenith over the North Pole, then it will appear lower and lower the further you go south. And if you went as far as the equator, the Pole Star would be on the horizon. In the southern half of the world, for instance in Australia, you can't see the Pole Star at all. The stars there also go in a circle, but there is no visible star at the centre of the circles.

如果地球是圓的，船上的瞭望員就會先看到山峰——就像在爬山一樣。如果地球是圓的，而北極星就在北極正上方的天頂，那麼越往南走它就會顯得越來越低。如果你走到赤道，北極星就會落在地平線上。在南半球，比如在澳洲，根本看不到北極星。那裡的星辰也繞圓圈運轉，但圓圈的中心沒有可見的星星。


It is through these two observations made by sailors that the wise Greeks of Alexandria worked out that the earth is not flat but a round globe.

正是通過水手們的這兩個觀察，亞歷山卓的希臘智者們推斷出地球不是平的，而是一個圓圓的球體。


So why don't we normally notice that the earth is round? The larger a circle is, the less it curves or the flatter it is. The radius of the earth is nearly 4000 miles, and therefore the curve is so slight that we don't notice it.

那為什麼我們平常感覺不到地球是圓的呢？圓越大，彎曲就越小，也就越平坦。地球的半徑將近四千英里，因此弧度如此微小，我們察覺不到。


Let us compare the Pole Star with the sun. At the North Pole the Pole Star stands highest, in the zenith right above us. But the sun is very low and in winter disappears below the horizon. On the equator the sun stands highest at noon in the zenith, but the Pole Star is on the horizon, and you cannot see it as the air on the horizon is never clear enough. The Pole Star is highest at the North Pole and lowest on the equator; the sun is highest on the equator and lowest at the North Pole. The Pole Star stands still; the sun moves in a circle over the sky.

讓我們把北極星和太陽做個比較。在北極，北極星最高，就在我們正上方的天頂。但太陽非常低，冬天甚至落到地平線以下。在赤道，太陽在正午時最高，在天頂；但北極星卻在地平線上，而且由於地平線的空氣永遠不夠清澈，你看不到它。北極星在北極最高，在赤道最低；太陽在赤道最高，在北極最低。北極星靜止不動；太陽在天空中繞圈運行。


So the wise Greeks of Alexandria who never went very far north or very far south, just by thinking about the observations of sailors, found that the earth was round. It was by observing the sky -- the sun and the stars -- that they discovered something important about the earth. It was the sun and the stars, the Pole Star especially, which revealed the shape of the earth.

因此亞歷山卓的希臘智者們——他們自己從未到過很北或很南的地方——僅僅通過思考水手們的觀察，就發現了地球是圓的。正是通過觀察天空——太陽和星辰——他們發現了關於地球的重要事實。是太陽和星辰，尤其是北極星，揭示了地球的形狀。
# 22. Longitude and Latitude
# 22. 經度與緯度

The wise Greeks of Alexandria came to the conclusion that the earth was not flat, but a globe. When the Roman Empire fell to the Barbarians, like so much other knowledge, this knowledge of the shape of the earth was forgotten and lost. It took a thousand years until people in Europe discovered anew what the Greeks had already known, that the earth is a globe.

智慧的亞歷山大城希臘人得出了一個結論：地球不是平坦的，而是一個球體。當羅馬帝國被蠻族攻陷之後，與許多其他知識一樣，這項關於地球形狀的知識也被遺忘了。整整過了一千年，歐洲人才重新發現希臘人早已知道的事實——地球是一個球體。


If we take a ball and let light fall on it from one side, we see the shadow line: one half is in darkness, the other half is in the light, and the shadow line (which is not very sharp) divides the light part from the dark part. If this ball were the earth, the shadow line would go from the North Pole to the South Pole. And on one side would be night and on the other it would be day. All people along this shadow line would say, "It is dawn, the sun is rising."

如果我們拿一顆球，讓光從一側照射過來，我們會看見一條陰影線：一半在黑暗中，另一半在光明中，而這條陰影線（並不是非常銳利的）將明亮的部分與黑暗的部分隔開。如果這顆球就是地球，那麼陰影線就會從北極延伸到南極。一側是黑夜，另一側則是白晝。所有站在這條陰影線上的人都會說：「天亮了，太陽正在升起。」


The shadow line goes from the North Pole to the South Pole, and for all the people on that line — say, from Norway to South Africa — it is the same time, daybreak. And it will be the same all through the day: all the people along this line where the shadow line was, will continue to have the same time right through the day and night.

這條陰影線從北極延伸到南極，而在這條線上的所有人——比如說從挪威到南非——都處於同一個時刻，也就是黎明。而且一整天都是如此：這條陰影線上的所有人，在整個白天和夜晚都會擁有相同的時間。


At noon all the people along the line where the shadow was will see the sun at its highest point. People further west will see it lower but rising, and people further east see it lower but going down. But all the people on that shadow line have the same time of day.

在正午時分，這條線上的所有人都會看見太陽在天空的最高點。更西邊的人會看到太陽較低但正在上升，更東邊的人會看到太陽較低但正在西沉。然而，這條陰影線上的所有人擁有的是同一個日間時刻。


But one thing is different. We know that the sun is not very high in the north in winter, even at its highest point at noon. But someone living on the same shadow line, say in Africa, would see the sun much higher at noon. So people on this shadow line all have the same time of day, but they see the sun at noon at different heights.

但有一件事是不同的。我們知道在冬天，太陽在北方地區即使在正午最高點時也不會太高。但是住在同一條陰影線上的人，比如在非洲，正午時會看到太陽高得多。所以這條陰影線上的人雖然都有相同的日間時刻，但他們在正午看到太陽的高度卻不一樣。


We can find these shadow lines drawn on every map. They go from the North to the South Pole, and they are called meridians (midday line), for all the people along it have midday at the same time. And the meridians on the maps have numbers. While you could start counting meridians anywhere on the globe, by common agreement the meridian going through Greenwich is the start on every map in the world, and it is numbered 0 (not 1). Meridians are numbered like the degrees on a circle (or on a protractor) going from 0° to 180° east of Greenwich, and from 0° to 180° west of Greenwich. The meridian is called the longitude of that place. The longitude of Edinburgh is 3°12' west of Greenwich, or simply 3°12' W. New York is 74° W, and Tokyo is 139°40' E.

我們可以在每一張地圖上找到這些陰影線。它們從北極延伸到南極，被稱為子午線（也就是正午線），因為沿著它的所有人都在同一時刻迎來正午。地圖上的子午線都有編號。雖然你可以從地球上任何地方開始計算子午線，但根據全世界共同的約定，經過 Greenwich（格林威治）的子午線是每張地圖的起點，編號為 0（而不是 1）。子午線的編號就像圓上的度數（或量角器上的度數），從格林威治向東 0° 到 180°，向西 0° 到 180°。子午線代表的就是那個地方的經度。Edinburgh（愛丁堡）的經度是格林威治以西 3°12'，簡寫為 3°12' W。New York（紐約）是 74° W，Tokyo（東京）是 139°40' E。


But to say exactly where a place is it is not enough to write how many degrees east or west of Greenwich it is. We also need to know how far north or south it is.

但是要精確地說明一個地方在哪裡，光寫它在格林威治以東或以西多少度是不夠的。我們還需要知道它在多北或多南的位置。


The meridian lines all go through the poles like the slices of an orange, they are related to the poles. The other kind of lines must have something to do with the equator. They are lines parallel to the equator and are therefore called parallels. The equator itself is starting parallel, 0°, and the other parallels go then to 90° south and to 90° north of the equator. These parallels tell us the latitude of a place (which means your distance between equator and pole.)

子午線都像柳橙的切片一樣穿過兩極，它們與兩極有關。另一種線則與赤道有關。它們是平行於赤道的線條，因此被稱為緯線。赤道本身就是起始緯線，編號 0°，其他緯線則從赤道向南延伸到 90°、向北延伸到 90°。這些緯線告訴我們一個地方的緯度（也就是你離赤道和極點之間的距離）。


How will the sun appear to people living on the same parallel, on the same latitude? They will not have the same time of the day; they will all have noon at different times. But when they have noon, the people on the same latitude will see the sun at the same height.

太陽對住在同一條緯線、同一緯度上的人來說會是什麼樣子呢？他們不會有相同的日間時刻；他們都在不同的時間迎來正午。但當他們各自迎來正午的時候，同一緯度上的人會看到太陽在相同的高度。


We can now give the exact location of any place on the earth by stating the latitude and longitude. This is particularly useful for ships at sea where there are no landmarks to tell where they are. So, for instance, New Orleans lies at 30° N, 90° W; or Sydney is at 33°52' S, 151°12' E.

我們現在可以透過說明緯度和經度來精確標出地球上任何地方的位置。這對於海上的船隻特別有用，因為在海上沒有地標可以告訴他們身在何處。例如，New Orleans（紐奧良）位於 30° N, 90° W；Sydney（雪梨）位於 33°52' S, 151°12' E。


In summary, the meridian, or longitude east or west of Greenwich, has the same time of day, but the midday sun is at different heights. The parallel, latitude north or south of the equator, has different times, but the midday sun will be at the same height.

總結而言，子午線，也就是格林威治以東或以西的經度，擁有相同的日間時刻，但正午太陽的高度不同。緯線，也就是赤道以北或以南的緯度，有著不同的時刻，但正午太陽的高度相同。


---

# 23. The Circle
# 23. 圓

We have looked at the movements of the sun in the sky. Though we see only a part of the path of the sun, we know that this path is a circle. And we have seen that the stars — all the stars in the sky — also move in circles. They move in concentric circles round the Pole Star.

我們已經觀察了太陽在天空中的運動。雖然我們只看到太陽路徑的一部分，但我們知道這條路徑是一個圓。我們也看到了星星——天空中所有的星星——也在做圓周運動。它們以同心圓的方式繞著北極星運行。


But the sun itself is a circle as we can see it at sunrise and at sunset; the full moon is a circle (even the stars are very small circles). The sun and the moon are themselves circles, and their paths are circles. A rainbow is a part of a great circle: it is as if the sun would paint a picture of itself on rain and clouds.

但太陽本身就是一個圓，我們在日出和日落時可以看到；滿月也是一個圓（甚至星星也是非常小的圓）。太陽和月亮本身是圓的，它們的軌跡也是圓的。彩虹是一個大圓的一部分：彷彿太陽在雨滴和雲朵上畫了一幅自己的肖像。


The ancient Greeks called the great world of sun and moon and stars, "that which makes beautiful," the cosmos. And it is still so called today. Cosmos means "adornment," or "beautiful." Out there in the cosmos the lights you see — sun, moon, stars, and their paths — are all what the Greeks called the "perfect form," the circle.

古希臘人稱太陽、月亮和星辰的廣大世界為「美的締造者」——cosmos（宇宙）。時至今日仍然這樣稱呼。Cosmos 的意思是「裝飾」或「美麗」。在那遙遠的宇宙中，你所看見的光——太陽、月亮、星辰及它們的軌跡——都是希臘人所說的「完美形式」，也就是圓。


The heavenly circle of the sun also works on earth. If we look at the blossoms of many flowers, we can see that the petals stand in a circle. But in the sunlight the blossoms become fruits and now think how many kinds of fruit are rounded globes — cherries, oranges, grapefruit, coconuts, peas and poppy seeds. If we cut through the stem of most plants we can again see a little circle. Even if we cut through a tree trunk, the rings are not perfect circles, but they are trying to be concentric circles.

太陽的天體之圓也在地球上發揮著作用。如果我們觀察許多花朵的花瓣，可以看到花瓣排列成一個圓。而在陽光下，花朵變成了果實——現在想想有多少種水果是圓球狀的：櫻桃、柳橙、葡萄柚、椰子、豌豆和罌粟籽。如果我們橫切大多數植物的莖，又能看到一個小圓。即使我們橫切一段樹幹，那些年輪也許不是完美的圓，但它們努力想成為同心圓。


If we watch a cat trying to be really comfortable, we can see it rolling itself into a little ball. It tries to make itself into a ball or globe. Snakes, too, roll themselves up into tight, round coils, and birds, when they go to sleep, often tuck their heads in and become round little balls of feathers.

如果我們觀察一隻貓想要真正舒適地休息，可以看到牠把自己蜷成一個小球。牠試圖把自己變成一個球體。蛇也會把自己捲成緊緻的圓圈，而鳥兒在入睡時，常常把頭縮進去，變成一個圓滾滾的小羽毛球。


The human head that we carry proudly on our shoulders — upright towards the cosmos, the world of stars and sun — the head too is rounded and, especially the skull protecting the brain, is a globe.

我們驕傲地承載在肩膀上的人類頭顱——挺立朝向宇宙、朝向星辰和太陽的世界——頭顱也是圓的，尤其是保護大腦的頭骨，就是一個球體。


All these living things have rounded shapes, and want to form a ball, a globe. But crystals, for instance, are not alive, and their shape is not at all rounded. They have straight edges and sharp corners. Crystals are not alive, and there is no such thing as a round crystal.

所有這些有生命的事物都有圓潤的形狀，都想要形成球或球體。但晶體，例如，並不是活的，它們的形狀一點也不圓潤。晶體有直線的邊和尖銳的角。晶體沒有生命，世上也沒有圓形的晶體。


Or the peaks of the Himalayas — these mighty rocks are certainly not alive — have sharp ridges and pointed peaks. Only over thousands of years will wind and weather gradually round them.

又比如喜馬拉雅山的山峰——這些巨大的岩石當然不是活的——有著尖銳的稜線和尖聳的山頂。只有經過數千年的風吹日曬，才能逐漸將它們磨圓。


Things which are dead and without life tend to be made of straight lines and sharp edges, while what is alive tends to have rounded forms, like circles, and globes. And the rounded shape reflects the cosmos, the world of sun, moon and stars. We can understand that life itself comes from the cosmos. With the light of sun, moon and stars, life also flows from the cosmos.

死去的、沒有生命的事物往往由直線和銳角構成，而有生命的事物則傾向擁有圓潤的形態，像圓和球體。而圓潤的形狀反映著宇宙，反映著太陽、月亮和星辰的世界。我們可以理解，生命本身就來自宇宙。隨著太陽、月亮和星辰的光芒，生命也從宇宙流淌而來。


The round forms, the circles, the globes, are the handwriting of the cosmos which we can recognize just as we recognize someone's handwriting. If we find a round shell that is dead the round form tells us that this was once part of a living creature and its life came from the cosmos.

圓形、圓圈、球體，就是宇宙的筆跡，我們可以辨認它，就像我們辨認某個人的字跡一樣。如果我們發現一個已經死去的圓形貝殼，那圓潤的形狀告訴我們，它曾經是一個有生命的生物的一部分，而它的生命來自宇宙。


We can now begin to understand why the Greeks called the circle the perfect form. It is the form of life.

我們現在可以開始理解為什麼希臘人稱圓為完美的形式了。它是生命的形式。


---

# 24. The Stars and Sirius
# 24. 星辰與天狼星

The sun is like a trumpet that calls us to work, to be active; the stars are more like an orchestra that invites us to sit quietly and listen. And people have always felt that in some way they are related to the sun which calls us to our tasks, but there is also something in us that feels a kinship with the stars.

太陽就像一把小號，召喚我們工作、行動；而星辰更像一支管弦樂團，邀請我們靜靜地坐下來聆聽。人們一直感覺到，在某種意義上，我們與那召喚我們去工作的太陽有著連結，但我們內在也有某些東西感受到與星辰的親緣。


Nowadays, in the age of space exploration, people do not feel this connection with the stars as it was felt in ancient times. If you had told a man from ancient Babylonia or Egypt that we can send a spaceship up to Mars or Venus he would have said, "That's a quite useless exercise because if you patiently watch the movements of these planets, how they grow brighter or dimmer, the stars themselves will tell you all you need to know about them. And it is far more fruitful for the human spirit to reach up to the stars than to send up human bodies, which are not really made for space travel, and have to be put into a strange armour to survive."

在今天這個太空探索的時代，人們已經不像古代那樣感受到與星辰的聯繫了。如果你告訴一個古代 Babylonia（巴比倫）或 Egypt（埃及）的人，說我們能把太空船送上 Mars（火星）或 Venus（金星），他會說：「那是毫無用處的事，因為如果你耐心地觀察這些行星的運動，觀察它們如何變亮或變暗，星辰本身就會告訴你所有需要知道的事。讓人類的精神去觸及星辰，遠比把人類的身體送上去更有成效——人的身體本來就不是為太空旅行而造的，還得穿上奇怪的盔甲才能存活。」


Of course we can't go back to the ways of ancient Babylonia, but it is still true that the movements which can be observed are quite mysterious and wonderful, and we shall consider them first.

當然我們無法回到古代巴比倫的方式，但那些可以觀察到的運動確實神秘而奇妙，這一點至今仍然成立，我們先來思考這些運動。


If we look up to the night sky when it is not cloudy, the stars all look the same, except that some are brighter than the others. But if we patiently watch several nights in a row, we may discover a star which changes its position in relation to the others. That star which has not stayed in its place is actually not a star, but a planet. The real stars are all fixed stars, but the ones that move in relation to the others are planets.

如果在沒有雲的夜晚仰望星空，所有的星星看起來都一樣，只是有些比較亮。但如果我們連續幾個晚上耐心觀察，可能會發現有一顆星星改變了它相對於其他星星的位置。那顆沒有待在原位的星星實際上不是恆星，而是一顆行星。真正的恆星都是固定的——恆星，而那些相對於其他星星移動的則是行星。


There is another difference between the planets and the fixed stars. The fixed stars shine with their own light but the planets have no light of their own, they only reflect the sunlight which falls on them.

行星和恆星之間還有另一個區別。恆星以自己的光芒閃耀，但行星沒有自己的光，它們只是反射照射在它們身上的陽光。


We will first consider the fixed stars, of which there are millions, while there are only nine or ten planets that can be observed from earth. With the naked eye only about six or seven thousand stars can be seen. With a telescope, the more powerful it is, the more stars can be seen.

我們先來看恆星，恆星有數百萬顆，而從地球上能觀察到的行星只有九或十顆。用肉眼只能看到大約六七千顆星星。用望遠鏡的話，望遠鏡越強大，能看到的星星就越多。


From ancient times the fixed stars which are close together have been grouped together and are known by one name, usually taken from mythology. Modern astronomy has kept these old names (as well as adding some new ones), so on a star map we will find a group of stars called Perseus and another called Andromeda. These are taken from the Greek myth. Such a group of fixed stars is called a constellation.

從古代開始，彼此靠近的恆星就被歸為一組，以一個名字來稱呼，通常取自神話。現代天文學保留了這些古老的名字（也添加了一些新的），所以在星圖上我們會找到一組叫做 Perseus（英仙座）的星群，還有一組叫做 Andromeda（仙女座）。這些名字來自希臘神話。這樣一組恆星就叫做一個星座。


One of the constellations which can easily be found in the southern part of the sky in winter is Orion. It can be recognized by three stars in a straight line, the "belt" of Orion. Orion was a great hunter, and below this constellation there are two other constellations, his two dogs, the Little Dog and the Great Dog. The brightest star in the Great Dog is also the brightest fixed star in the sky. It is called Sirius.

冬天在天空南方很容易找到的星座之一是 Orion（獵戶座）。它可以透過三顆排成一直線的星星辨認出來，那就是獵戶座的「腰帶」。Orion 是一位偉大的獵人，在這個星座下方還有兩個星座，就是他的兩隻狗——小犬座和大犬座。大犬座中最亮的星星也是全天空最亮的恆星，它叫做 Sirius（天狼星）。


This bright star, Sirius, has always been of great interest to astronomers. In the nineteenth century there was a German astronomer, Friedrich Bessel, who made a special study of Sirius. We said the fixed stars do not move. But they do move very, very slightly, but this movement can only be detected with a very big telescope. So Bessel was not surprised that the star Sirius showed a slight movement. But what he observed was not what he had expected. Sirius did not move in a straight line, but in a curve. And Bessel wondered why this was so.

這顆明亮的星——天狼星，一直以來都非常受天文學家關注。十九世紀有一位德國天文學家 Friedrich Bessel（貝塞爾），他對天狼星做了專門的研究。我們說過恆星不會移動。但它們確實會非常、非常微小地移動，不過這種移動只有用非常大的望遠鏡才能探測到。所以貝塞爾對天狼星顯示出微小移動並不感到驚訝。但他觀察到的並不是他所預期的。天狼星不是沿直線移動，而是沿著一條曲線移動。貝塞爾很想知道為什麼會這樣。


It occurred to him one day that there might be another star so close to Sirius that it had an effect on its movement. Bessel, who looked at Sirius through a powerful telescope which showed many more stars that you can see with the naked eye, could not find any star close enough to Sirius to influence its movement. But almost twenty years later, in 1862, an American, Alvon Clark, made a bigger and more powerful telescope than any that had existed before. He had a son, a boy of 14, and showed him how to look at the stars through it. The boy turned the big telescope to Sirius and suddenly he shouted, "Father, look Sirius has a little companion."

有一天他想到，也許有另一顆星離天狼星非常近，以至於影響了它的運動。貝塞爾透過一架強大的望遠鏡觀察天狼星，這架望遠鏡能看到比肉眼多得多的星星，但他找不到任何離天狼星足夠近、能影響其運動的星星。然而將近二十年後，在 1862 年，一位美國人 Alvon Clark（阿爾凡·克拉克）製造了一架比以往任何望遠鏡都更大、更強力的望遠鏡。他有一個十四歲的兒子，他教兒子如何透過望遠鏡觀星。男孩把大望遠鏡轉向天狼星，突然喊道：「父親，快看，天狼星有一個小伴侶！」


Through the new telescope they could see the star which Bessel had not been able to find. But Bessel through his thinking had deduced that there must be such a companion for Sirius. The human mind, the human spirit can reach out to the stars.

透過新的望遠鏡，他們看到了貝塞爾未能找到的那顆星。但貝塞爾早已透過思考推斷出天狼星一定有這樣一個伴星。人類的心智、人類的精神，能夠觸及星辰。


*Pluto, the tenth planet, discovered in 1930, has since 2006 been classified as a dwarf planet, of which currently five are known.*

*Pluto（冥王星），第十顆行星，於 1930 年被發現，自 2006 年起被歸類為矮行星，目前已知有五顆矮行星。*


---

# 25. The Daily Movement of Stars and Sun
# 25. 星辰與太陽的日常運動

Of the many constellations in the sky — there are now 88 such groups covering the whole sky — some are more important than others. We mentioned one constellation which was very useful in ancient times, the Plough or Great Bear. From the Plough, which can be easily found in the northern sky, one can find the Pole Star. The Pole Star is the only star in the sky which does not move. All the other stars move in concentric circles around it, or rather, the whole starry sky rotates around the Pole Star. We can observe this if we carefully watch the night sky for a few hours. The constellation Plough swings around the Pole Star, always pointing at it. The constellations further away from the Pole Star describe big circles, so big that only a part of the circle is above the horizon, and the rest is below where we cannot see it. In one day the Plough makes a complete circle round the Pole Star and, in our northern latitudes, is never below the horizon.

在天空中的眾多星座——現在共有 88 個這樣的星群覆蓋整個天空——有些比其他的更重要。我們曾提到一個在古代非常有用的星座，就是北斗七星，也稱大熊座。從北方天空中容易找到的北斗七星出發，人們可以找到北極星。北極星是天空中唯一不動的星星。所有其他星星都以同心圓的方式圍繞它運動，或者更確切地說，整個星空都繞著北極星旋轉。如果我們仔細觀察夜空幾個小時，就能觀察到這一現象。北斗七星圍繞北極星擺動，始終指向它。離北極星較遠的星座劃出巨大的圓圈，大到只有圓的一部分在地平線以上，其餘在地平線以下我們看不到的地方。一天之內，北斗七星繞北極星完成一整圈，在我們北半球的緯度，它從不落到地平線以下。


In ancient times people had no watches or clocks; there were hour-glasses, but few people had those. During the day they could estimate what the time was from the position of the sun or, more exactly, from a sundial. And during the night they looked at the position of the constellation of the Plough. The Plough rotates around the Pole Star in approximately 24 hours and, with some practice, it is possible to guess fairly accurately what the time is. Of course, it is not quite exact but most people had no need to know the time exactly to the minute or second.

在古代，人們沒有手錶或時鐘；有沙漏，但很少人擁有。白天他們可以根據太陽的位置來估計時間，或者更精確地說，用日晷。而在夜晚，他們觀察北斗七星的位置。北斗七星大約每 24 小時繞北極星旋轉一圈，經過一些練習，可以相當準確地猜出現在是什麼時間。當然不是非常精確，但大多數人並不需要精確到分鐘或秒鐘。


However, the astronomers of Babylonia, of Greece and Rome, who wanted to be very accurate in their time measurements, discovered something one can also observe today by using a watch. The Plough describes a full circle and comes back to the same position in less than 24 hours. It is only a difference of a few minutes per day but after a week or so the difference is quite noticeable. Our watches and clocks — just like the hour-glasses and sundials of ancient times — take their time from the sun. We divide the time from one sunrise to the next into 24 parts which we call hours. The sun takes 24 hours to come back to the same position. But the fixed stars come back to the same position in less time, in about 23 hours and 56 minutes.

然而，巴比倫、希臘和羅馬的天文學家，他們想要非常精確地測量時間，發現了一件今天用手錶也能觀察到的事。北斗七星劃完一整圈回到同一位置所花的時間不到 24 小時。每天只差幾分鐘，但一個星期左右之後，差異就相當明顯了。我們的手錶和時鐘——就像古代的沙漏和日晷一樣——是以太陽為基準計時的。我們把從一次日出到下一次日出的時間分成 24 份，稱之為小時。太陽需要 24 小時回到同一位置。但恆星回到同一位置所需的時間較短，大約是 23 小時 56 分鐘。
