We can see the whole starry night-sky rotating. But this rotation does not stop during the day and when the sun rises and then sets. The sun is really part of the same rotation. But — and this is the difference — when one rotation of the stars is complete, the sun is lagging a little behind and comes back to the same position about 4 minutes later. And, of course, we take our time from the sun and not from the stars.

我們可以看到整個星夜天空在旋轉。但這個旋轉在白天、在太陽升起又落下的時候並沒有停止。太陽實際上也是同一個旋轉的一部分。但——這就是區別——當星辰完成一圈旋轉時，太陽稍微落後了一點，大約晚 4 分鐘才回到同一位置。而我們計時當然是以太陽為準，而不是以星辰為準。


This time-lag between the stars and the sun means that the sun changes its position in relation to the fixed stars. There are always stars in the sky, even in the daytime, but the stars of the day-sky are invisible because the sunlight is too strong. We can see the stars becoming paler and paler every day at dawn, but they are still there even though we cannot see them. You might think it is a pity that we can never see the stars which are in the day-sky, but we will see them again in six months time.

星辰和太陽之間的這種時間差意味著太陽相對於恆星改變了位置。天空中總是有星星的，即使在白天，但白天的星星因為陽光太強而看不見。我們每天黎明時可以看到星星越來越淡，但即使我們看不見它們，它們仍然在那裡。你可能覺得遺憾，我們永遠看不到白天天空中的星星，但六個月後我們就會再次看到它們。


This is how the people of ancient times discovered that the sun moves, changes its position in relation to the stars: some constellations which are in the night-sky in winter, in summer are in the day-sky and cannot be seen.

古代的人們就是這樣發現太陽在移動、在改變相對於星辰的位置的：有些在冬天夜空中可見的星座，到了夏天就轉到了白天的天空中而看不見了。


If we imagine for a moment that we could see the stars and the sun at the same time — the sun in the foreground and the stars in the background — we would then see the sun standing before a particular constellation of stars. Owing to the time-lag of 4 minutes per day the sun would slowly move through this constellation and after about 30 days the sun would stand in front of another constellation. Wherever the sun is, that constellation as well as the ones next to it are outshone by the sunlight, but the others are in the night sky and can be seen. The constellations through which the sun passes form a circle, and when the sun has passed the last of these constellations it comes back to the first one, just as the hand on our watch comes back to the 12 o'clock and then starts again. Just as there are 12 hours on our watch so there are, for the sun, twelve constellations. The hour hand on our watch makes a full circle in 12 hours, and the sun makes its full circle in 12 months, that is of course, a year.

如果我們想像一下，我們能同時看到星星和太陽——太陽在前景，星星在背景——我們就會看到太陽站在某個特定星座的前面。由於每天 4 分鐘的時間差，太陽會緩慢地穿越這個星座，大約 30 天後，太陽就會站在另一個星座前面。不管太陽在哪裡，那個星座以及旁邊的星座都被陽光蓋過了，但其他的星座則在夜空中可以看到。太陽經過的星座構成一個圓，當太陽經過最後一個星座後，它又回到第一個，就像我們手錶上的指針回到 12 點然後重新開始。正如我們的錶上有 12 個小時，對太陽來說也有十二個星座。我們手錶的時針在 12 小時內繞一整圈，而太陽在 12 個月內繞一整圈，那當然就是一年。


There are twelve constellations through which the sun goes in one year and that's why we have twelve months in a year. Once, in the past, the months coincided with the passage of the sun through each constellation, but in the course of time people changed the calendar to suit their own purposes.

太陽一年之中穿越十二個星座，這就是為什麼一年有十二個月。曾經在過去，月份與太陽穿越每個星座的時間是吻合的，但隨著時間推移，人們為了自己的需要而更改了曆法。


---

# 26. The Zodiac and Precession of the Equinox
# 26. 黃道十二宮與歲差

The circle of twelve constellations through which the sun goes in one year is called the zodiac, a Greek word meaning the "circle of animals." However, not all the twelve are named after animals. There is a little rhyme which might help to remember them:

太陽一年中穿越的十二個星座所形成的圓圈叫做 zodiac（黃道帶），這是一個希臘詞，意思是「動物之環」。不過，十二個星座並非全都以動物命名。有一首小詩可以幫助記住它們：


The Ram, the Bull, the heavenly Twins,
Beside the Crab the Lion stands,
The Virgin and the Scales;
The Scorpion, Archer and the Goat,
The Man who pours the water out,
And Fish with glittering tails.

白羊、金牛、天上的雙子，
巨蟹身旁獅子站，
還有處女和天秤；
天蠍、射手與山羊，
倒水的寶瓶人，
尾鰭閃閃的雙魚。


They are usually called by their Latin names: Aries, Taurus, Gemini, Cancer, Leo, Virgo, Libra, Scorpio, Sagittarius, Capricorn, Aquarius, and Pisces.

它們通常以拉丁名稱呼：Aries（白羊座）、Taurus（金牛座）、Gemini（雙子座）、Cancer（巨蟹座）、Leo（獅子座）、Virgo（處女座）、Libra（天秤座）、Scorpio（天蠍座）、Sagittarius（射手座）、Capricorn（摩羯座）、Aquarius（水瓶座）和 Pisces（雙魚座）。


This "circle of animals" or zodiac is not merely a circle but a circular belt. The reason it is important in astronomy is that not only the sun, but also the planets all move along this belt. There are many constellations in the sky, but sun, moon and planets move only within the narrow belt of these 12 constellations of the zodiac.

這個「動物之環」或黃道帶不僅僅是一個圓，而是一條環狀帶。它在天文學中重要的原因是，不只太陽，所有行星也都沿著這條帶運行。天空中有許多星座，但太陽、月亮和行星只在黃道十二宮這條狹窄的帶狀區域內移動。


As well as sun, moon and planets moving through the zodiac, something else also moves through the zodiac, though we cannot see it at all because it is only a mathematical point. It moves so slowly that it takes hundreds of years to notice that it has moved at all. Yet, this movement is very important for the whole of humanity. What is this strange mathematical point?

除了太陽、月亮和行星穿越黃道帶之外，還有另一樣東西也在黃道帶中移動，儘管我們完全看不到它，因為它只是一個數學上的點。它移動得如此緩慢，以至於要幾百年才能察覺它移動了。然而，這個運動對全人類都非常重要。這個奇怪的數學點是什麼？


There are two days of the year when day and night are equal, when there are 12 hours of daylight and 12 hours of darkness: one in the spring and one in the autumn. They are called equinox (from the Latin, equi, equal and nox, night). The equator of the earth has its name because it is the circle where day and night are always equal.

一年中有兩天日夜等長，各有 12 小時的白晝和 12 小時的黑夜：一個在春天，一個在秋天。它們叫做 equinox（二分點），源自拉丁文 equi（相等）和 nox（夜晚）。地球的赤道之所以得名，就是因為在赤道上日夜總是等長的。


The spring equinox is the one which in ancient times (when most people were working on the land as farmers) was regarded as a very special date in the year. From that day onwards daytime was longer than night, the sunlight grew in strength and warmth, and the seeds the farmers had planted sent out little sprouts. It was the beginning of spring. And in Egypt a sacred white bull, the Apis-Bull, was led through the streets to celebrate this occasion. Why a bull? Because at the time of ancient Egypt on the day of the spring equinox, March 20, the sun stood in the constellation of Taurus, the Bull.

春分是古代（當大多數人都在土地上務農時）被視為一年中非常特別的日子。從那天起，白晝比黑夜長，陽光越來越強、越來越溫暖，農夫種下的種子冒出了小嫩芽。那是春天的開始。在埃及，人們會牽著一頭神聖的白色公牛——Apis（阿匹斯）牛——走過街道來慶祝這個日子。為什麼是公牛？因為在古埃及時代，春分那天——三月二十日——太陽正好在 Taurus（金牛座）的位置。


About two thousand years later, in the time of ancient Greece and Rome, people no longer celebrated March 20, the spring equinox. But if they had, it would not have been a bull that was led through the streets, it would have been a ram, because at that time the sun shone from the constellation Aries, the Ram, on March 20. And if we had such a custom today, we would have to carry two fishes through the streets, because now the sun stands in the constellation of Pisces, the Fishes, on March 20.

大約兩千年後，在古希臘和羅馬時代，人們已不再慶祝三月二十日的春分。但如果他們慶祝的話，被牽過街道的就不會是公牛，而會是公羊，因為那時在三月二十日太陽照耀在 Aries（白羊座）的位置。而如果今天我們有這樣的習俗，我們就得抬著兩條魚走過街道，因為現在在三月二十日太陽位於 Pisces（雙魚座）的位置。


The position of the sun at the spring equinox, or the vernal point has moved through three constellations since the time of ancient Egypt: Taurus, Aries, Pisces. This movement is called the precession of the equinox.

自古埃及時代以來，太陽在春分時的位置，也就是春分點，已經穿越了三個星座：金牛座、白羊座、雙魚座。這種運動就叫做歲差（precession of the equinox）。


But why should it matter to us where the sun stands on March 20? Around AD 1400 a number of great things began to be discovered or invented. About this time the European voyages of discovery began; these led to the discovery of America and culminated in the circumnavigation of the world. New inventions were made, such as book printing, which made it possible for many people to have books and learn about the world. There was also the invention of gun-powder which made knights' armour useless. From that time onwards the flow of discoveries and inventions never stopped. In the 600 years since 1400 more things have been discovered and invented than in all the thousands of years of human history before 1400.

但太陽在三月二十日站在哪個位置，跟我們有什麼關係呢？大約在西元 1400 年前後，許多偉大的事物開始被發現或發明。大約在這個時候，歐洲的地理大發現開始了；這些航行導致了美洲的發現，最終實現了環球航行。新的發明出現了，例如印刷術，使許多人能夠擁有書籍、認識世界。還有火藥的發明，使騎士的盔甲變得毫無用處。從那時起，發現和發明的潮流就再也沒有停止過。自 1400 年以來的六百年間，被發現和發明的事物比 1400 年之前數千年人類歷史中的總和還要多。


This is not, as one might think, because the Greeks or Romans were not clever enough. For instance, Heron, a clever Greek in Alexandria made a little contraption which used the steam of boiling water to turn a wheel, but this was only a toy to amuse and no one thought that there could be a practical use for this idea. The Greeks and Romans were as clever as we are, but they were not interested in technical inventions. What has changed is human interest.

這並不像人們可能以為的那樣，是因為希臘人或羅馬人不夠聰明。例如，亞歷山大城一位聰明的希臘人 Heron（希羅）做了一個小裝置，利用沸水的蒸汽來轉動輪子，但這只是一個供人消遣的玩具，沒有人想到這個點子可以有實際用途。希臘人和羅馬人跟我們一樣聰明，但他們對技術發明不感興趣。改變的是人類的興趣。


The interests of the Egyptians and Babylonians were different from those of the Greeks, just as the interests of the Greeks were not the same as ours. Whenever the spring equinox passes from one constellation to another there is such a change of human interest. There are people who say that when the next change comes, when the spring equinox will pass from the constellation Pisces, the Fishes, into the constellation Aquarius, the Water-Carrier, then humanity will become more interested in spiritual matters than in material things, and will have a much stronger feeling that all people are brothers and sisters, and must help each other. So the movement of this mathematical point of the vernal equinox means something for humanity.

埃及人和巴比倫人的興趣與希臘人不同，正如希臘人的興趣也與我們不同。每當春分點從一個星座移到另一個星座時，人類的興趣就會發生這樣的變化。有人說，當下一次轉變到來——當春分點從雙魚座移入 Aquarius（水瓶座）時——人類將會對精神事物比對物質事物更感興趣，而且會更強烈地感覺到所有人都是兄弟姊妹，必須互相幫助。所以這個數學上的春分點的移動，對人類是有意義的。


---

# 27. The Cosmic or Platonic Year
# 27. 宇宙年（柏拉圖年）

The spring equinox, the point where the sun stands on March 20, moves through the zodiac. While the sun moves round the whole zodiac in 12 months, astronomers have calculated that it takes about 25,920 years for the spring equinox to move around the zodiac. That is a long time, but it is a figure which is interesting for another reason. We breathe at an average about 18 times a minute, and that makes 25,920 times in a day.

春分點——太陽在三月二十日所處的位置——在黃道帶中移動。太陽在 12 個月內繞完整個黃道帶，而天文學家計算出，春分點繞黃道帶一圈大約需要 25,920 年。那是很長的時間，但這個數字因為另一個原因而很有趣。我們平均每分鐘呼吸約 18 次，一天下來就是 25,920 次。


The Greek astronomers, who worked out this figure of 25,920 years, called this movement of the spring equinox around the zodiac a Cosmic Year, or a Platonic Year, after the great Greek philosopher Plato. So, the Cosmic Year has a length of 25,920 ordinary years. So how long is a cosmic month? Dividing 25,920 years by 12, it is 2,160 years. This is the time it takes for the spring equinox to pass through one whole constellation of the zodiac. For 2,160 years the spring equinox is in the same constellation, slowly moving through it. And then it passes on to the next constellation.

計算出 25,920 這個數字的希臘天文學家，將春分點繞黃道帶一圈的運動稱為宇宙年，或柏拉圖年（Platonic Year），以偉大的希臘哲學家 Plato（柏拉圖）命名。所以，一個宇宙年的長度是 25,920 個普通年。那麼一個宇宙月有多長呢？用 25,920 年除以 12，是 2,160 年。這就是春分點穿越黃道帶中一整個星座所需的時間。在 2,160 年中，春分點都在同一個星座裡，緩慢地穿越它。然後才移入下一個星座。


In this time human interests change. The Egyptian civilization was in the "cosmic month" of the Bull, the Greeks lived in the cosmic month of the Ram and we are now in the cosmic month of the Fishes.

在這段時間裡，人類的興趣會改變。埃及文明處於金牛的「宇宙月」，希臘人生活在白羊的宇宙月，而我們現在處於雙魚的宇宙月。


An ordinary month has 30 days. Dividing the cosmic month of 2,160 years by 30 we get a "cosmic day" of 72 years. A cosmic day is 72 years long which consists of 25,920 ordinary days, which means one ordinary day is one "cosmic breath." Or, in other words, one cosmic breath takes as long as 25,920 human breaths.

一個普通的月有 30 天。把 2,160 年的宇宙月除以 30，我們得到 72 年的「宇宙日」。一個宇宙日長 72 年，包含 25,920 個普通日，這意味著一個普通日就是一次「宇宙呼吸」。換句話說，一次宇宙呼吸的時間等於 25,920 次人的呼吸。


Our own breathing and even our life is "tuned in" to the great rhythm of the cosmos. But our breathing is not something separate from our whole organization: our heartbeat is "tuned in" to our breathing. There are four heartbeats to one breath. And as our heart beats, so the blood flows through our body. The most important rhythms of our life are in tune or in harmony with the rhythms of the cosmos. And it is therefore not so strange that a change in the cosmos, for instance, when the spring equinox passes over from the constellation Ram to the constellation Fishes is accompanied by a change in the way human beings feel and where their interests lie.

我們自己的呼吸，甚至我們的生命，都「調頻」在宇宙的偉大節奏上。而我們的呼吸與整個身體組織並非各自分開：我們的心跳也「調頻」在呼吸上。每一次呼吸對應四次心跳。而隨著心臟跳動，血液在我們體內流淌。我們生命中最重要的節奏與宇宙的節奏和諧一致。因此，當宇宙中發生變化時——例如當春分點從白羊座過渡到雙魚座——伴隨而來的是人類感受方式和興趣方向的轉變，這並不那麼奇怪。


Another thing which changes with the movement of the spring equinox is the Pole Star, the star which stays in the same place while the whole sky with all the stars in it is turning around it. But the star we call the Pole Star in our time is not the same star as the one which the Egyptians and Babylonians saw as their Pole Star.

隨著春分點的移動而改變的另一件事是北極星——那顆在整個天空連同所有星星都圍繞著它旋轉時，自己待在同一個位置的星星。但我們這個時代稱為北極星的星星，與埃及人和巴比倫人所見的北極星並不是同一顆。


In the long course of time different stars become the Pole Star, and all the stars which, one after another, become Pole Stars, lie in a little circle. The time it takes until all the stars in that little circle have had their turn at being Pole Stars is 25,920 years.

在漫長的歲月中，不同的星星會成為北極星，而所有先後成為北極星的星星都排列在一個小圓上。等到這個小圓上所有的星星都輪流當過北極星，所需的時間就是 25,920 年。


Why is the Pole Star not always the same star? We said the whole starry sky is rotating — that this is how it appears to us — but that it is really the earth which is rotating on its axis; the earth is spinning round. The earth turns round its axis, and this axis points in a certain direction — to the Pole Star. When we see the Pole Star we see the direction in which the axis of the earth points.

為什麼北極星不總是同一顆星呢？我們說過整個星空在旋轉——這是我們看到的樣子——但其實是地球在繞著自己的軸旋轉；地球在自轉。地球繞著自己的軸轉動，而這根軸指向一個特定方向——指向北極星。當我們看到北極星時，我們看到的就是地球軸線所指的方向。


If we take an old-fashioned wooden spinning top, and make it spin, it will not remain exactly upright, but will wobble (especially as it slows down). The axis of the earth has a slight wobble, and this means that it points in different directions, but always describing a circle. It is a very slow wobble, but owing to this wobble the axis points to different stars which in turn become the Pole Star.

如果我們拿一個老式的木製陀螺讓它旋轉，它不會完全保持直立，而會搖擺（尤其當它減速時）。地球的軸也有輕微的搖擺，這意味著它指向不同的方向，但始終在畫一個圓。這是非常緩慢的搖擺，但正因為這個搖擺，地軸指向了不同的星星，它們就依次成為北極星。


So the whole earth is involved in this great cosmic rhythm of 25,920 years.

所以整個地球都參與在 25,920 年這個偉大的宇宙節奏之中。


---

# 28. The Seven Classical Planets
# 28. 七顆古典行星

Where do the names of the days of the week come from? Few people still know that they come from astronomy. Saturday gets its name from the planet Saturn. Sunday of course, is called after the sun, just as Monday is called after the moon. Tuesday is named after the Norse god of war, Tiu (or Tyr); the Romans called the same god Mars, and in French the day is called mardi, the day of Mars. Mars is a planet. Wednesday is named after the Norse god of the winds and the air, Wodan (or Odin) whom the Romans called Mercury, and in French this day is mercredi. It is the day of the planet Mercury. Thursday is named after the god of thunder and lightning, Thor, whom the Romans called Jupiter, in French the day is jeudi. It is the day of the planet Jupiter. And Friday is the day of the Norse goddess of beauty, Freia, whose Latin or Roman name was Venus, and the French call this day vendredi. It is the day named after the planet Venus.

一週各天的名字從何而來？如今很少有人知道它們來自天文學。Saturday（星期六）的名字來自行星 Saturn（土星）。Sunday（星期日）當然是以太陽命名的，就像 Monday（星期一）是以月亮命名的一樣。Tuesday（星期二）以北歐戰神 Tiu（或 Tyr）命名；羅馬人稱同一位神為 Mars（瑪爾斯），法文把這一天叫做 mardi，即火星日。Mars 是一顆行星。Wednesday（星期三）以北歐風與空氣之神 Wodan（或 Odin）命名，羅馬人稱他為 Mercury（墨丘利），法文把這一天叫做 mercredi，是水星日。Thursday（星期四）以雷電之神 Thor（索爾）命名，羅馬人稱他為 Jupiter（朱庇特），法文叫做 jeudi，是木星日。Friday（星期五）是北歐美之女神 Freia（弗蕾亞）的日子，她的拉丁或羅馬名字是 Venus（維納斯），法文把這一天叫做 vendredi，是以金星命名的日子。


Saturn, sun, moon, Mars, Mercury, Jupiter, Venus — these are the seven heavenly bodies which can be seen by the naked eye that change their position in relation to the fixed stars of the zodiac. They are the "wandering stars," or planetei in Greek from which we have our word planet. And these wandering heavenly bodies are always in the constellations of the zodiac.

土星、太陽、月亮、火星、水星、木星、金星——這是肉眼可見的、會改變自己相對於黃道恆星位置的七個天體。它們就是「漫遊的星星」，希臘文叫 planetei，我們的 planet（行星）一詞就由此而來。而這些漫遊的天體總是出現在黃道星座中。


These seven heavenly bodies, however, move at quite different speeds through the zodiac. The ancient astronomers concluded that the longer a planet takes to make one round of the zodiac, the further away it is from the earth. They thought of the paths of the seven heavenly bodies as concentric circles, which, as we shall find out, is not quite true.

然而，這七個天體穿越黃道帶的速度大不相同。古代天文學家得出結論：一顆行星繞黃道帶一圈所花的時間越長，它離地球就越遠。他們認為七個天體的軌道是同心圓，正如我們後來會發現的，這並不完全正確。


As the seven wandering stars have different speeds the astronomers speak of faster or slower planets, but we must keep in mind that we only notice that a planet is moving by observing it over a longer period. The movements of the planets are like the growing of a plant. It takes some time before you can see that the plant has grown, yet the plant is steadily growing and the planets are steadily moving.

由於七顆漫遊之星的速度各不相同，天文學家會說行星較快或較慢，但我們必須記住，我們只有經過較長時間的觀察才能察覺行星在移動。行星的運動就像植物的生長。你需要過一段時間才能看到植物長大了，但植物一直在穩定地生長，行星也一直在穩定地移動。


Let us look at how long they take to go round the zodiac. The times given here are approximate, but for just now we are only comparing their speeds.

讓我們看看它們繞黃道帶一圈各需要多長時間。這裡給出的時間是近似值，但現在我們只是比較它們的速度。


Moon — 1 month
Mercury — 12 months
Venus — 12 months
Sun — 12 months
Mars — 2 years
Jupiter — 12 years
Saturn — 30 years

月亮 —— 1 個月
水星 —— 12 個月
金星 —— 12 個月
太陽 —— 12 個月
火星 —— 2 年
木星 —— 12 年
土星 —— 30 年


Mercury, Venus and the sun each take a year to move round the zodiac. While the sun moves slowly and steadily, Mercury sometimes dashes ahead, and sometimes lingers behind — three times a year dashing ahead, and three times a year lingering behind, so you could say Mercury has a kind of movement of about 4 months. Venus does something similar but more slowly. For this reason the Greek astronomers called Mercury and Venus the faster planets, and placed them between moon and sun.

水星、金星和太陽各需要一年的時間繞黃道帶一圈。太陽緩慢而穩定地移動，水星則時而衝到前面，時而落在後面——一年中三次衝到前面，三次落在後面，所以可以說水星有一種大約 4 個月的運動週期。金星的運動類似但更慢。因此，希臘天文學家稱水星和金星為較快的行星，並把它們排在月亮和太陽之間。


If we look at these times we can see that the moon is 24 times faster than Mars, moon and Mars are like an hour is to a day. Jupiter takes 12 years, in one year it goes only as far as the sun in one month. So Jupiter is to the sun like a year to a month. This is the opposite of the sun-moon relation, where the moon is to the sun like a month is to a year. Saturn needs a long time, 30 years, to complete its round of the zodiac, that is 360 months or almost as many months as the sun takes days. So Saturn is to the sun like a month to a day. One could also say that Saturn takes as many years as the moon takes days to complete a round. So Saturn is to the moon like a year to a day.

如果我們看看這些時間，就能發現月亮比火星快 24 倍，月亮和火星的關係就像一小時之於一天。木星需要 12 年，一年中它走過的距離只相當於太陽一個月走的。所以木星之於太陽就像一年之於一個月。這與太陽和月亮的關係正好相反——月亮之於太陽就像一個月之於一年。土星需要很長的時間，30 年，才能完成黃道帶的一圈，也就是 360 個月，幾乎等於太陽繞一圈所需的天數。所以土星之於太陽就像一個月之於一天。也可以說，土星繞一圈所需的年數，恰好等於月亮繞一圈所需的天數。所以土星之於月亮就像一年之於一天。


So we can see the paths of the seven heavenly bodies and the pace at which they move are interrelated in a marvellous pattern. Sun, moon and planets are "tuned" to each other, and move in harmony. And as we saw with the movement of the spring equinox, we ourselves with our breathing and our heartbeat are also connected with the rhythms of the cosmos. So the human being and the sun, moon, planets, are all part of the great pattern written in the sky as the constellations of the zodiac.

由此我們可以看到，七個天體的軌道和它們運行的速度以一種奇妙的模式相互關聯。太陽、月亮和行星彼此「調頻」，和諧地運行。正如我們在春分點運動中所看到的，我們自己的呼吸和心跳也與宇宙的節奏相連。因此，人類與太陽、月亮、行星，都是寫在天空中的偉大圖案——黃道星座——的一部分。
# 29. The Moon
# 29. 月亮

The heavenly body which is nearest to our earth, that is the one whose path forms the smallest circle and so completes a full round of the zodiac in the shortest time, is the moon. Now the moon has one thing in common with the planets Saturn, Jupiter, Mars, Venus and Mercury. It is that they all reflect the light of the sun. They have no light of their own and we can only see them because the sun shines on them and we see the reflected light.

離我們地球最近的天體，也就是軌道構成最小圓圈、因此在最短時間內完成一趟黃道之旅的天體，就是月亮。月亮和 Saturn（土星）、Jupiter（木星）、Mars（火星）、Venus（金星）、Mercury（水星）這些行星有一個共同點：它們都反射太陽的光。它們本身不會發光，我們之所以能看見它們，是因為太陽照在它們身上，而我們看到的是反射的光。


With the planets this is not so easy to see but the moon shows it very clearly with its phases: waxing, waning, full and new moon. The bright, lit side of the moon always faces the sun, and during the month as the moon moves around the zodiac, we see the phases changing.

行星的這個特性不太容易看出來，但月亮透過它的盈虧變化清楚地展現了這一點：漸盈、漸虧、滿月和新月。月亮明亮的那一面總是朝向太陽，而在一個月當中，隨著月亮沿黃道移動，我們就看到了月相的變化。


During the course of a month, we first see the fine crescent of the moon in the evening just after sunset. Over the next days it grows — it is waxing — until about a week later it is half moon. The moon continues to grow, to wax, for about another week until it is full. At this phase, at full moon, it is always in the constellation of the zodiac opposite the constellation where the sun is. When the sun is in Aries the full moon is in Libra, and a month later when the sun is in Taurus the full moon is in Scorpio, and so on.

在一個月的過程中，我們先在傍晚日落之後看到一彎纖細的月牙。接下來幾天它逐漸長大——這就是漸盈——大約一週後成為半月。月亮繼續增長、漸盈，再過大約一週就成為滿月。在滿月這個階段，月亮總是位在黃道上與太陽所在星座相對的星座裡。當太陽在 Aries（牡羊座）時，滿月在 Libra（天秤座）；一個月後太陽到了 Taurus（金牛座），滿月就在 Scorpio（天蠍座），依此類推。


After full moon it begins to get smaller, to wane. The lop-sided shape between half moon and full moon is called gibbous. And it continues to wane past half moon, to a waning crescent moon which can be seen in the early morning before sunrise. Then the moon is not visible for two or three days while it passes the sun. While we like to call the thin evening crescent of the moon the new moon, astronomers call new moon the moment the moon passes the sun, just the time when we cannot see anything at all.

滿月之後，月亮開始變小，也就是漸虧。半月和滿月之間那個不對稱的形狀叫做凸月（gibbous）。月亮繼續虧損，過了半月之後，變成清晨日出前可見的殘月。然後在月亮經過太陽的那兩三天裡，我們完全看不見它。雖然我們喜歡把傍晚那一彎纖細的月牙稱為新月，但天文學家所說的新月，是月亮通過太陽的那個瞬間——恰恰是我們什麼都看不見的時候。


Usually the new moon is a little above or below the sun, but once or twice (rarely three times) a year the new moon stands in front of the sun and then the black disc of the moon darkens the bright sun disc either wholly or partially, depending where the moon happens to be. This is an eclipse of the sun.

通常新月會略高於或略低於太陽，但一年中有一兩次（很少三次），新月正好擋在太陽前面，於是月亮的黑色圓盤將明亮的太陽圓盤遮暗——完全遮住或部分遮住，取決於月亮當時的位置。這就是日食。


The diagram shows a fine point of total shadow, the umbra, reaching the earth. If we happen to be standing just in that part of the earth during the eclipse we would be in total shadow: the sun will be completely darkened or eclipsed. Around the dark shadow is another part where there is a partial shadow, the penumbra. If we were standing in this penumbra, we would be able to see part of the sun, but part would be blocked: we would see a partial eclipse.

圖示顯示了一個細小的全影區（umbra，本影）觸及地球。如果日食發生時我們恰好站在地球上那個區域，我們就處於全影之中：太陽將被完全遮暗，也就是全食。在黑暗的影子周圍還有一片半影區（penumbra，半影）。如果我們站在半影中，就能看到太陽的一部分，但另一部分會被遮住：我們看到的就是日偏食。


As the moon is passing across the disc of the sun, the shadow moves, and for each total eclipse the shadow moves across the earth from west to east, making a line. So if we want to see an eclipse of the sun, we have to be in the right part of the earth to see it. Astronomers will travel for thousands of miles to observe this.

當月亮掠過太陽的圓面時，影子在移動，每次日全食的影子都從西向東橫掃地球，畫出一條線。所以如果我們想看日食，就必須站在地球上正確的位置。天文學家會為此旅行數千英里。


At full moon, it can also happen that sun, earth and moon stand exactly in line. Then the earth casts its shadow onto the full moon, and there is an eclipse of the moon. There usually are two moon eclipses in a year, and provided the moon is above the horizon (and at full moon that is any time between sunset and sunrise), we will be able to see the eclipse.

在滿月時，也可能發生太陽、地球和月亮恰好排成一線的情況。這時地球的影子投射到滿月上，就產生了月食。一年中通常有兩次月食，只要月亮在地平線以上（在滿月時，從日落到日出之間的任何時候都是），我們就能看到月食。


Of course, the earth is always casting a shadow but if there is nothing for it to fall on, we cannot see it. But when the full moon is in line with earth and sun, then the earth shadow does fall on it. At an eclipse of the sun the shadow of the moon falls on the earth. At an eclipse of the moon the earth shadow falls on the moon.

當然，地球一直都在投射影子，但如果沒有東西讓影子落在上面，我們就看不到它。但當滿月與地球和太陽排成一線時，地球的影子就落在了月亮上。日食時，是月亮的影子落在地球上；月食時，是地球的影子落在月亮上。


Just as the earth casts a shadow from its dark side, so its light side, the day side, reflects the light of the sun. Again this reflection goes out into space and we do not notice it. But there are occasions when one can notice it. If there is a clear sky when the slender crescent moon appears, we can see the old moon in the new moon's arms. The dark part of the moon is still visible, gently illuminated by the bluish reflected light that comes from the earth, the earth-shine. Springtime is the best season to see it. This is because the new moon in spring stands higher above the horizon than it does at other times.

正如地球從它黑暗的一面投射出影子，它明亮的一面——白天的那一面——也反射太陽的光。這反射的光同樣射入太空，我們通常不會注意到。但有些時候是可以察覺的。當天空晴朗、纖細的新月出現時，我們可以看到「新月懷抱著舊月」。月亮暗淡的部分仍然隱約可見，被從地球反射來的藍色微光溫柔地照亮——這就是地球反照光（earth-shine）。春天是觀看它的最佳季節，因為春天的新月比其他時候高懸在地平線之上。


Both earth and moon receive their light from the sun but, when the moon is new, it is not only that the light crescent of the moon sends a little light to the dark side of earth, the earth also sends its light to the dark side of the moon. It is a time when earth and moon greet each other with light; that's different from the times of eclipses, when they cast shadows on one other. At new moon the dark side of the moon is made a little brighter by the light which our earth sends out into the cosmos.

地球和月亮都從太陽那裡接收光芒，但在新月的時候，不僅月亮的光亮月牙向地球的黑暗面送去一點光，地球也把自己的光送到月亮的暗面。這是地球和月亮以光相互問候的時刻——這和日食、月食時它們彼此投射陰影的時刻截然不同。在新月時，月亮的暗面因為我們地球向宇宙射出的光而變得稍微明亮了一些。


# 30. Tides and Other Lunar Influences
# 30. 潮汐與其他月球影響

The moon moves faster through the zodiac than the sun and its movement is also easier to observe. If we look out of the window at 8 pm and see the moon standing just above the top of a tree, we will not see it there the next evening at the same time. It will arrive there 50 minutes later, at 8.50. And the reason for this is that the moon has changed its position, it has moved in relation to the sun.

月亮在黃道上移動得比太陽快，它的運動也更容易觀察。如果我們晚上八點從窗口望出去，看到月亮正好在一棵樹的頂端上方，第二天同一時間我們不會在同一位置看到它。它會晚五十分鐘才到達那裡，也就是八點五十分。原因是月亮改變了它的位置——它相對於太陽移動了。


There are a great many people who know these 50 minutes by which the moon gets later to the same place without ever looking up to the moon. People who live by the sea know the tides. In most of the seas and oceans there are two high tides every 24 hours. If there is a high tide at 8 in the morning, there is a second high tide at 8.25 in the evening. And the next tide is at 8.50 on the following morning. So between one morning high tide and the next, there are 24 hours 50 minutes. High tide comes 50 minutes later every day: the tides follow the rhythm of the moon.

有很多人知道月亮每天遲到五十分鐘這件事，卻從不抬頭看月亮。住在海邊的人都知道潮汐。在大多數海洋中，每二十四小時有兩次漲潮。如果早上八點漲潮，晚上八點二十五分就會有第二次漲潮。下一次漲潮則在隔天早上八點五十分。所以從一個早上的漲潮到下一個早上的漲潮，間隔是二十四小時五十分鐘。每天漲潮都晚五十分鐘：潮汐跟隨著月亮的節奏。


But the high tides are not always of the same height. The highest high tides and lowest low tide (called spring tides, from Old English springere, meaning to rise or spring up, not from the season called spring) are always around the time of full moon or new moon. The tides with the least change (around the time of the waxing or waning half moon) are called neap tides. So the moon has certain effects on things that happen here on earth.

但漲潮並不總是一樣高。最高的漲潮和最低的退潮（稱為大潮 spring tides，來自古英語 springere，意思是湧起或跳起，不是來自春天這個季節）總是出現在滿月或新月前後。變化最小的潮汐（出現在上弦月或下弦月前後）稱為小潮（neap tides）。所以月亮對地球上發生的事情確實有一定的影響。


There are also other and more subtle effects of the moon. Around 1920 a German scientist, Lily Kolisko, planted the seeds of carrots, radishes and other vegetables three days before the full moon, that is at the waxing phase. And she also planted the same kind of seeds three days before the new moon, at the waning phase. The plants of the waxing phase did much better, grew faster and were stronger than the plants of the waning phase. Since then many gardeners and farmers all over the world have followed the advice of this scientist and have profited from it.

月亮還有其他更細微的影響。大約在一九二零年，一位德國科學家 Lily Kolisko（莉莉·科利斯科）在滿月前三天——也就是漸盈的階段——播下胡蘿蔔、蘿蔔和其他蔬菜的種子。她也在新月前三天——漸虧的階段——播下同樣的種子。漸盈階段播種的植物長得好得多，生長更快、也更強壯。從那以後，世界各地許多園丁和農夫都遵循了這位科學家的建議，並從中獲益。


There are other and even more subtle effects of the moon. Nurses who work in hospitals for people who are mentally ill know that at the time of the full moon many of their patients become much worse and are more difficult to handle. This was so well known in ancient times that madmen were simply called "lunatics" which comes from the Latin word luna, the moon. A "lunatic" meant someone who reacts too strongly to the influence of the full moon. But there is also a good side to the mental influence of the full moon. Writers, poets, composers of music, people who need a great deal of imagination for their work have more ideas at the time of the full moon than at other times.

月亮還有更加細微的影響。在精神病院工作的護士都知道，滿月時許多病人的狀況會明顯惡化，更加難以照顧。這在古代就已經廣為人知，以至於瘋子被直接稱為 "lunatics"（瘋子），這個詞來自拉丁文 luna，也就是月亮。"lunatic" 的意思是對滿月的影響反應過於強烈的人。但滿月對精神的影響也有好的一面。作家、詩人、音樂作曲家——這些工作需要大量想像力的人——在滿月時比其他時候有更多的靈感。


The peasants in the Middle Ages always reckoned that rain was more likely at the time of the full moon or the new moon. Then came the scientists and said it is all superstition. But some years ago an Australian meteorologist, Bowen, collected the frequency of rainfall from places all over the world and over long periods and found that the stupid peasants had not been so stupid and that rain is indeed more frequent at the times of the full or the new moon.

中世紀的農民一向認為滿月或新月時更容易下雨。後來科學家出來說這全是迷信。但幾年前，一位澳洲氣象學家 Bowen（鮑恩）收集了世界各地長時期的降雨頻率資料，發現那些「愚蠢的農民」其實並不愚蠢——在滿月或新月時，降雨確實更為頻繁。


There are many examples of the influence of the moon in the animal world. One of the strangest instances is the palolo worm, a sea-worm that lives in the Pacific Ocean. This worm is regarded as a delicacy by the natives of Samoa, but they can enjoy eating their fried palolo worms only once a year. Just at dawn one week after the full moon following the equinox, the worms come out of the deep sea where they live, to spawn their eggs. They come up in their millions and are caught by the Samoans. No one knows how the worms know the phase of the moon, for the full moon does not occur on the same date every year. But whatever the actual date is, on that day the worms come up from the depth. They cannot see the moon in the dark depth of the sea where they live, so it is a mystery how they time their spawning so exactly.

在動物世界中，月亮的影響有許多例子。最奇特的例子之一是磯沙蠶（palolo worm），一種生活在太平洋裡的海蟲。這種蟲被 Samoa（薩摩亞）的原住民視為美味佳餚，但他們一年只能享用一次炸磯沙蠶。就在春分之後滿月再過一週的黎明時分，這些蟲從牠們居住的深海中浮出水面產卵。牠們成千上萬地湧出，被薩摩亞人捕撈。沒有人知道這些蟲是怎麼知道月相的，因為滿月每年不會落在同一個日期。但不管實際日期是哪一天，牠們就在那一天從深處浮上來。在牠們棲息的漆黑海底，牠們看不到月亮，所以牠們是如何如此精確地掌握產卵時機，至今仍是一個謎。


As there are so many strange influences connected with the moon it is not surprising that there are many fables and legends about it. There is a very beautiful one which comes from Africa.

既然月亮有這麼多奇妙的影響，有許多關於月亮的寓言和傳說也就不足為奇了。有一個非常美麗的傳說來自非洲。


When we in Europe look up at the full moon we see the dark patches as a kind of face and we call it the "man in the moon." But to the Africans these patches looked like an animal, like a hare, and they tell a story how the hare got up there. They say that in very ancient times human beings could see that when a person died the soul went up to God in the light of the sun and the moon and the stars, they could see it as we see clouds or the rainbow in the sky. And because they could see what happened after death they were not afraid of dying. Death was for them no more than a journey to another land. But as time passed men lost the ability to see where the souls of the dead went and so they began to be afraid of death, they feared death.

我們在歐洲仰望滿月時，看到那些暗斑像一張臉，我們稱之為「月亮上的人」。但對非洲人來說，那些暗斑看起來像一隻動物，像一隻兔子，他們講述了兔子是怎麼到月亮上去的故事。他們說，在非常古老的年代，人類能夠看見一個人死去時，靈魂在太陽、月亮和星星的光芒中升向上帝，就像我們看見天空中的雲朵或彩虹一樣。因為他們能看見死後發生的事，所以他們不害怕死亡。死亡對他們而言不過是前往另一片土地的旅程。但隨著時間推移，人們失去了看見亡者靈魂去向的能力，於是他們開始害怕死亡，恐懼死亡。


And the moon-spirit took pity on these poor people on earth. He said to the hare, "You shall be my messenger. Go to the men on earth and tell them to look at the moon. Just as the moon gets less and less after it has been full and disappears at the new moon, but then appears again as a thin crescent which grows and grows, just like that the souls of the people who have died and disappeared will come and live again. The new moon is not the end of the moon-existence and death is not the end of human existence."

月亮之靈對地球上這些可憐的人心生憐憫。他對兔子說：「你來當我的使者吧。去告訴地球上的人們，讓他們看看月亮。正如月亮在滿月之後越來越小，在新月時消失，但接著又以一彎纖細的月牙重新出現，然後越長越大——人們死去消失之後，靈魂也會同樣地回來再次活過。新月不是月亮存在的終結，死亡也不是人類存在的終結。」


The hare obeyed and went to the men on earth to bring them the message of the moon. But the men did not listen: they hunted the hare, shooting arrows at it, and chased it with their dogs, so the hare ran away without delivering the message. And the moon spirit was angry with the hare and threw it onto the moon where the Africans can still see it today.

兔子遵命前往人間，為人們帶去月亮的訊息。但人們不願傾聽：他們追獵兔子，向牠射箭，放狗追趕牠，於是兔子沒有傳達訊息就逃走了。月亮之靈對兔子很生氣，把牠扔到了月亮上——非洲人至今仍然可以在月亮上看到牠。


But how did people then know what the moon spirit had said to the hare? The African tribes say that the moon whispered its message to good and wise men in their dreams. As there are not so many good and wise men about, there have always been only a few to whom the moon could speak in their dreams, and they told the others.

但人們後來又是怎麼知道月亮之靈對兔子說了什麼呢？非洲部落說，月亮在善良而智慧的人的夢中低語了牠的訊息。因為世上善良而智慧的人並不多，所以月亮總是只能在少數人的夢中訴說，再由他們轉告其他人。


# 31. Easter
# 31. 復活節

Spring is the time of the vernal equinox, the time when neither day nor night are stronger, each lasting exactly twelve hours. At the time of the spring equinox the sun shines down from the direction of the constellation of the zodiac which is as important for our time as the constellation of the Bull was for ancient Egypt, or the Ram was for Greece and Rome. In our time the constellation where the sun stands at the time of the spring equinox is the Fishes. Fish move freely in the oceans, they range far and wide, (think of the salmon which swim thousands of miles from the Atlantic Ocean and up our rivers). Our time is a time when people should range far and wide and explore the world, also with their mind and spirit. That is the message which the sunlight brings to us at the spring equinox, March 20, when the sun stands before the constellation of the Fishes.

春天是春分的時節，是白天和黑夜勢均力敵的時候，各自恰好十二個小時。在春分時，太陽從一個對我們這個時代特別重要的黃道星座方向照耀下來——就像金牛座對古埃及、白羊座對希臘和羅馬那樣重要。在我們的時代，太陽在春分時所處的星座是雙魚座（Pisces）。魚在大海中自由遊動，四處遨遊（想想鮭魚，牠們從大西洋游上數千英里再溯河而上）。我們的時代是人們應該四處遨遊、探索世界的時代——不僅是身體上的，也包括心靈和精神上的。這就是太陽在三月二十日春分時、站在雙魚座前方帶給我們的訊息。


March 20 is also called the beginning of spring in our calendars (of course, it is different in the southern hemisphere). It is the time when nature all around us is growing and budding, when the cold days of winter are past and there is new life everywhere. In the African story we heard how people on earth were told to look up and to learn from the waning moon that the new moon is not an end, but will be followed by the waxing moon, the sign of new life. Before Easter not only is this waxing half moon highest in the sky, but here on earth too all things are waxing, that is, growing. Life here on earth also tells us: in winter trees may look dead and barren, the fields may look dead and bare, but it only seems so, for now there is new life everywhere.

三月二十日在我們的日曆上也被稱為春天的開始（當然，在南半球是不同的）。這是周圍大自然萌芽生長的時節，寒冷的冬日已過，到處都是新的生命。在非洲的故事裡，我們聽到地上的人們被告知要仰望天空，從漸虧的月亮中學到一個道理：新月不是終點，接下來會是漸盈的月亮——新生命的標誌。在復活節之前，不僅天空中漸盈的半月高懸，地球上的萬物也都在漸盈、在生長。大地上的生命也在告訴我們：冬天裡，樹木可能看起來枯死荒蕪，田野可能看起來死寂蕭條，但那只是表象，因為現在到處都有新的生命。


So at Easter nature around us, and the moon in the sky, the sun and the stars, they all have a special message for us at this special time of the year.

因此在復活節，我們周圍的大自然、天空中的月亮、太陽和星星，都在這一年中特別的時刻向我們傳遞著特別的訊息。


In the African story, in a time long past people had no fear of death for they could see the souls of those who died rise up in the light of sun, moon, stars. But later they lost this ability, and could no longer see what happened after death; they lived in fear of death. In the times of ancient India, as we heard in the story of the Pandu brothers, people even looked forward to death, they were glad to leave earth. Gilgamesh, who lived four thousand years later, was already afraid of death.

在非洲的故事裡，在遙遠的過去，人們不害怕死亡，因為他們能看見亡者的靈魂在太陽、月亮和星星的光芒中升起。但後來他們失去了這個能力，再也看不到死後發生的事情，於是活在對死亡的恐懼中。在古印度時代，正如我們在 Pandu（般度）兄弟的故事中聽到的，人們甚至期盼死亡，他們樂於離開塵世。而四千年後的 Gilgamesh（吉爾伽美什）已經開始害怕死亡了。


It was to show us that death is not an end but the beginning of a new life, that Christ went through death and rose from the grave. That is what happened at the first Easter.

為了向我們展示死亡不是終點，而是新生命的開端，基督（Christ）經歷了死亡，又從墳墓中復活。這就是第一個復活節所發生的事。


So why is Easter not on the same date every year? The early Christians said, "The death and resurrection of Christ is not only something that concerns people on earth, it is a great event for the cosmos, and when we celebrate Easter we want to take account of the cosmos, of sun and moon and stars."

那麼，為什麼復活節每年不在同一個日期呢？早期的基督徒說：「基督的死亡與復活不僅僅關乎地上的人，它是宇宙的大事件。當我們慶祝復活節時，我們要把宇宙——太陽、月亮和星星——都考慮進來。」


So they made the following rule: Easter Sunday is the first Sunday after the full moon following the spring equinox. Sunday means the day of the sun, so that takes account of the sun. After the full moon, that takes account of the moon. And after the spring equinox, takes account of the stars where the sun is at the equinox.

因此他們制定了以下規則：復活節星期日是春分之後第一個滿月之後的第一個星期天。星期天（Sunday）意味著太陽之日，這考慮到了太陽。在滿月之後，這考慮到了月亮。在春分之後，這考慮到了春分時太陽所在的星座。


That is why Easter is not always on the same date; Christmas is always on December 25, but the date of Easter changes from year to year. It can be as early as March 22 or as late as April 25. Easter is the festival of life, the triumph of life over death, it is a celebration of all the new life that comes with the spring, and all life is connected with the rhythms of the cosmos.

這就是為什麼復活節不總在同一天。聖誕節固定在十二月二十五日，但復活節的日期每年都在變。最早可以在三月二十二日，最晚可以到四月二十五日。復活節是生命的節日，是生命戰勝死亡的慶典，是慶祝隨春天而來的一切新生命——而一切生命都與宇宙的節奏相連。


# 32. The Planets
# 32. 行星

We now come to the other heavenly bodies that move through the zodiac, the planets Mercury, Venus, Mars, Jupiter and Saturn. The most brilliant of these planets is Venus. Venus is a planet which is never very far from the sun; it either appears before sunrise in the morning, then we call it the morning star, or it follows the sun and shines after sunset in the evening sky and we call it the evening star. Both the morning star and the evening star are the same planet, Venus. Of course Venus is a planet, not a star, it has no light of its own and, like the moon, only reflects the sunlight. (The planets Mercury and Venus, like the moon, show phases, but they take much longer than the moon, and we need binoculars or a telescope to observe them.)

我們現在來談在黃道上移動的其他天體——行星 Mercury（水星）、Venus（金星）、Mars（火星）、Jupiter（木星）和 Saturn（土星）。這些行星中最明亮的是金星。金星是一顆從不遠離太陽的行星：它要麼在早晨日出前出現，我們稱它為晨星；要麼跟在太陽後面，在日落後的夜空中閃耀，我們稱它為昏星。晨星和昏星其實是同一顆行星——金星。當然，金星是行星而不是恆星，它本身不發光，和月亮一樣只是反射太陽光。（水星和金星跟月亮一樣也有盈虧變化，但週期比月亮長得多，而且需要用雙筒望遠鏡或望遠鏡才能觀察到。）


There are also times when Venus is not visible because it is then so near to the sun that its light cannot be seen in the daytime sky. There is a certain rhythm in this. You see Venus for a time as morning star; it gets nearer and nearer to the sun and becomes invisible in the sun's bright light. And then it reappears as evening star. Then the evening star gets nearer and nearer to the sun and disappears, and then reappears as the morning star. When one heavenly body passes another, it is called a conjunction. So Venus has a conjunction with the sun after being the evening star and another one after being the morning star.

也有些時候金星是看不見的，因為它離太陽太近，在白天的天空中無法看到它的光。這有一定的節奏。你會看到金星作為晨星出現一段時間；它越來越靠近太陽，消失在太陽的強光中。然後它又作為昏星重新出現。接著昏星越來越靠近太陽，再次消失，然後又作為晨星重新出現。當一個天體經過另一個天體時，稱為合（conjunction）。所以金星在作為昏星之後與太陽有一次合，在作為晨星之後又有一次合。


If we make a drawing of the zodiac as a circle and connect the points where Venus has a conjunction after being the morning star, we find it makes a regular five-pointed star. And it is the same with the conjunctions which come after Venus has been the evening star. Venus draws five-pointed stars, but you have to be an astronomer to become aware of it.

如果我們把黃道畫成一個圓，然後連接金星作為晨星之後與太陽合的各個位置，我們會發現它構成了一個規則的五角星。金星作為昏星之後的合也是如此。金星在天空中畫出五角星，但你必須是天文學家才能意識到這一點。


The planets Mars, Jupiter and Saturn take longer than the sun to travel through the zodiac. Their movement is not tied to the sun's and so they can be high in the midnight sky (which never happens with Venus or Mercury). They are in the night sky when the sun is on the opposite side of the zodiac to where they are. They can also be in the day sky, invisible, which happens when the sun overtakes them, when they have a conjunction with the sun. We can mark these conjunction-points as we did with Venus or Mercury, and we find that they also make interesting patterns. Mars takes about two years between conjunction, and has seven irregularly spaced conjunction points in 15 years. Jupiter makes eleven neat, evenly-spaced conjunctions in 12 years, and Saturn takes 30 years to make 29 conjunctions.

火星、木星和土星穿越黃道的時間比太陽長。它們的運動不受太陽束縛，因此可以在午夜的天空中高懸（金星和水星則永遠不會如此）。當太陽在黃道上它們的對面時，它們就出現在夜空中。當太陽追上它們時——也就是它們與太陽合的時候——它們也可以在白天的天空中，但不可見。我們可以像標記金星或水星那樣標記這些合的位置，就會發現它們也構成有趣的圖案。火星大約每兩年一次合，在十五年中有七個不規則分布的合點。木星在十二年中形成十一個整齊、均勻分布的合。土星則花三十年形成二十九次合。


In ancient times astronomers noticed another thing with these slow planets. Carefully observing the position of one of these planets night after night, they discovered that these planets move not only in one direction as the sun and the moon do, they sometimes slow down, stop and go backwards, and then after a time stop again and move forwards. You have to observe them for weeks and months and mark their positions against the background of stars to see how these slow planets make U-turns and loops. We shall hear later how the astronomers tried to explain this movement of Mars, Jupiter and Saturn.

古代天文學家還注意到這些緩慢行星的另一個現象。夜復一夜仔細觀察其中一顆行星的位置後，他們發現這些行星不像太陽和月亮那樣只朝一個方向移動，它們有時會慢下來、停止、然後倒退，過一段時間再次停下然後向前移動。你必須觀察數週數月，把它們的位置標記在背景恆星上，才能看出這些緩慢的行星如何做出掉頭和循環的動作。我們後面會聽到天文學家如何嘗試解釋火星、木星和土星的這種運動。


Of these three, Jupiter is the brightest, but not as bright as Venus. Mars is also quite bright and shines with a reddish light. Saturn has the weakest light of them, but can still shine more brightly than most of the surrounding stars.

在這三顆行星中，木星最明亮，但不如金星亮。火星也相當明亮，發出紅色的光芒。土星的光最弱，但仍然可以比周圍大多數恆星更明亮。


Sun, moon, Mercury, Venus, Mars, Jupiter, Saturn were known to the astronomers of ancient times in Babylonia and Egypt as the seven wanderers, or seven planets. Of course these astronomers had no telescopes. Since the invention of telescopes two more great planets have been discovered: Uranus and Neptune. These "new" planets are very far away, as we can see from how long they take to go round the zodiac. Uranus takes almost 85 years and Neptune takes 165 years. They are planets which, even if you observe them the whole year, hardly seem to move at all. Pluto, the tenth planet, was discovered in 1930, but in 2006 astronomers decided it was too small to be a real planet, and it was reclassified as a dwarf planet, of which currently five are known.

太陽、月亮、水星、金星、火星、木星、土星——古代 Babylonia（巴比倫）和 Egypt（埃及）的天文學家把它們稱為七顆漫遊者，或七大行星。當然，那些天文學家沒有望遠鏡。自從望遠鏡發明以來，又發現了兩顆大行星：Uranus（天王星）和 Neptune（海王星）。這些「新」行星非常遙遠，從它們繞黃道一圈所需的時間就可以看出來。天王星需要將近八十五年，海王星需要一百六十五年。即使你觀察它們一整年，它們似乎幾乎都沒有移動。Pluto（冥王星），第十顆行星，於一九三零年被發現，但在二零零六年天文學家認定它太小，不算真正的行星，將它重新歸類為矮行星——目前已知的矮行星有五顆。


# 33. Pythagoras
# 33. 畢達哥拉斯

Before going on to what is known about the stars, let us look at the great men who have built up astronomy as it is today. The story of astronomy began in Egypt and Babylonia and the names of the priests and wise men who studied the skies patiently over long periods have not been recorded. The first known astronomers lived in ancient Greece.

在繼續介紹關於恆星的知識之前，讓我們先來看看那些締造了今日天文學的偉人們。天文學的故事始於 Egypt（埃及）和 Babylonia（巴比倫），那些耐心地長期觀察天空的祭司和智者的名字並沒有被記錄下來。最早的已知天文學家生活在古希臘。


One of the earliest great men who helped to build up that wonderful treasure of knowledge which we have today was Pythagoras. He was born on a little island called Samos in the Aegean Sea around 500 BC (at the same time as Buddha lived in India). His father was a merchant and when the son was born, the father, as was usual in those days, sent messengers to the famous temple of Delphi to ask the oracle what future his newborn son would have. And the priests of the temple answered, "As long as men live on earth the name of this child will be remembered."

幫助建立起我們今天所擁有的這份美好知識寶藏的最早偉人之一，就是 Pythagoras（畢達哥拉斯）。他大約在西元前五百年出生在愛琴海上一個叫 Samos（薩摩斯）的小島上（與 Buddha（佛陀）在印度的時代相同）。他的父親是一位商人，兒子出生時，父親按照當時的慣例，派使者去著名的 Delphi（德爾菲）神廟詢問神諭，想知道這個新生兒的未來將會如何。神廟的祭司回答說：「只要人類還生活在地球上，這個孩子的名字就會被記住。」


As this boy grew up he showed a great love for doing geometrical drawings, and doing sums of any kind was not "work," but a joy and pleasure for him. By the time he was twenty-one he had learned as much of arithmetic and geometry as anybody in the whole of Greece could teach him. But Pythagoras wanted to know more. It was not just ordinary curiosity, there was something more. He had often watched when one of the beautiful Greek temples was built and he had seen how carefully and accurately each pillar, each step, each part of the temple had to be measured and made to just the right size. He had seen the architects working with compasses and rulers and making long calculations, so that all parts of the temple would fit together perfectly. And Pythagoras said to himself, "Without using numbers no temple could be built, nor even the houses people live in. But is not the whole world the temple of God? Surely, the whole world is created and built in accordance with numbers and the more I can understand about numbers and figures, the more I can understand of the world."

當這個男孩長大時，他展現了對幾何繪圖的極大熱愛，做任何種類的算術對他來說都不是「工作」，而是一種喜悅和樂趣。到二十一歲時，他已經學會了全希臘任何人所能教他的算術和幾何。但畢達哥拉斯想知道更多。這不僅僅是普通的好奇心，還有更深的東西。他經常觀看美麗的希臘神廟如何建造，看到每根柱子、每個台階、神廟的每個部分都必須多麼仔細、精確地測量，做到恰好的尺寸。他看到建築師們用圓規和尺子工作，進行長長的計算，讓神廟的所有部分完美地結合在一起。畢達哥拉斯對自己說：「不用數字，就建不成神廟，連人住的房子都蓋不成。但整個世界不就是上帝的神廟嗎？整個世界一定是按照數字來創造和建造的，而我越能理解數字和圖形，就越能理解這個世界。」


Numbers, arithmetic, algebra, geometry, all this is called "mathematics," and mathematics is a way to understand the divine wisdom in all creation, that is why Pythagoras was so anxious to learn more about it.

數字、算術、代數、幾何——所有這些都叫做「數學」，而數學是理解萬物創造中的神聖智慧的途徑。這就是畢達哥拉斯如此渴望學習更多數學的原因。


There was no one in Greece who could have taught him anything he did not know already, but he heard that there were priests in Egypt who knew much more than the Greeks. So Pythagoras left the Greek island of Samos where he was born and sailed to the land of Egypt.

在希臘已經沒有人能教他不知道的東西了，但他聽說埃及的祭司們知道的比希臘人多得多。於是畢達哥拉斯離開了他出生的希臘小島薩摩斯，航向埃及。


When he came to the wise priests of Egypt and told them he had come to learn from them, they answered: "It is not our custom to share our knowledge with any person who comes along. We regard knowledge as something holy, something sacred, and only people who are worthy should have knowledge. If you want to learn from us you must first prove to us that you are the right person to share our secrets."

當他來到埃及的智慧祭司面前，告訴他們他是來學習的，他們回答說：「我們的慣例不是把知識隨便分享給任何前來的人。我們視知識為神聖之物，只有配得上的人才應該擁有知識。如果你想向我們學習，你必須先向我們證明你是分享我們秘密的合適人選。」


In our time we teach science, maths, all subjects, to anybody and everybody. But in ancient Egypt all knowledge was holy and was given only to special people. To prove that he was worthy Pythagoras had to pass certain tests. They were not at all like the tests we know, tests with pencil and paper; they were quite different. For instance, he was given a task that was very dangerous; to show that he had courage. At other times he had to go a long time without food or drink, to show that he was master of his body, not the body master of him. At other times he was not allowed to speak for many months, no matter what happened or what he wanted, to show that he was master of his tongue. And there were other tests. Only when Pythagoras had passed these tests was he accepted as a pupil by the priests of Egypt. He spent many years with them, learning the great wisdom and knowledge they had.

在我們的時代，科學、數學，所有學科都教給任何人。但在古埃及，所有知識都是神聖的，只傳授給特定的人。為了證明自己配得上，畢達哥拉斯必須通過某些考驗。這些考驗完全不像我們所知道的那種用紙筆的測試；它們截然不同。比如，他被交付一項非常危險的任務，以展示他的勇氣。有時他必須長時間不吃不喝，以證明他是身體的主人，而不是身體控制他。有時他被要求好幾個月不能說話，無論發生什麼事或他想要什麼，以證明他是自己舌頭的主人。還有其他考驗。只有當畢達哥拉斯通過了這些考驗，他才被埃及的祭司們接受為學生。他在他們那裡度過了許多年，學習他們所擁有的偉大智慧和知識。


While Pythagoras was in Egypt, the land was invaded and conquered by the Persians. The Persians took many of the Egyptian priests as prisoners and sent them to Persia. For them Pythagoras was also an Egyptian priest, and so he too came as a prisoner to Persia. But the King of Persia had a Greek physician, a doctor, and when this doctor saw a fellow Greek amongst the prisoners, he pleaded with the King, and Pythagoras was set free but had to stay in Persia. Now at this time Babylonia was also under Persian rule and Pythagoras went to Babylonia to learn about the stars and sun and moon — for at that time the priests of Babylonia knew more about the stars than anybody else in the world. Just as Pythagoras had passed the tests of the priests in Egypt, so now again he had to pass hard and dangerous tests until the Babylonian priests took him as a pupil to learn their secrets.

畢達哥拉斯在埃及期間，這片土地被波斯人入侵和征服了。波斯人把許多埃及祭司擄為囚犯送往波斯。在他們眼中畢達哥拉斯也是一位埃及祭司，所以他也以囚犯身分來到了波斯。但波斯國王有一位希臘醫生，當這位醫生看到囚犯中有一位希臘同胞時，他向國王求情，畢達哥拉斯被釋放了，但必須留在波斯。當時巴比倫也在波斯統治之下，畢達哥拉斯便前往巴比倫學習關於星星、太陽和月亮的知識——因為那時巴比倫的祭司比世界上任何人都更了解星星。正如畢達哥拉斯曾通過埃及祭司的考驗，他現在又必須通過艱難而危險的考驗，直到巴比倫的祭司接受他為學生，教導他們的秘密。


Just as in the Old Testament, the Children of Israel were first in Egypt and then, centuries later, were captives in Babylonia, so it was with Pythagoras. He also met some of the holy men and prophets of the Israelites there and learned from them. After many years Pythagoras was allowed to return to Greece.

正如《舊約》中以色列的子民先在埃及，然後幾個世紀後又在巴比倫被俘——畢達哥拉斯的經歷也是如此。他還在那裡遇到了一些以色列的聖人和先知，並向他們學習。多年之後，畢達哥拉斯終於被允許返回希臘。


But where should he go? In all these long years of his absence his parents had died, he had no relatives and the island where he was born had been conquered by the Persians. But he now possessed more knowledge, secret knowledge, than anybody of his time. Where would he find pupils worthy of sharing his knowledge?

但他該去哪裡呢？在他漫長的離鄉歲月裡，父母已經去世，他沒有親戚，而他出生的島嶼也已被波斯人征服。但他現在擁有比任何同時代的人都更多的知識——秘密的知識。他到哪裡才能找到配得上分享他知識的學生呢？


At that time there were Greek cities not only in Greece but also in the south of Italy. For instance, Naples is a Greek name Neopolis, meaning "new city." And Pythagoras went to one of these Greek cities in Italy, called Croton.

那個時代，希臘城市不僅在希臘，也在義大利南部。例如 Naples（那不勒斯）就是希臘語名字 Neopolis，意思是「新城」。畢達哥拉斯去了義大利的一個希臘城市，叫做 Croton（克羅頓）。


Pythagoras did not look like an ordinary man. It was not only that he was tall and dressed in the pure white linen of the Egyptian priests, it was not only that his long hair and beard had turned white in these years in foreign lands and by the hardships he had gone through, but in his dark eyes one could see the power of knowledge.

畢達哥拉斯看起來不像一個普通人。不僅因為他身材高大、穿著埃及祭司的純白亞麻衣袍，不僅因為他在異鄉的歲月和經歷的艱辛使他的長髮和鬍鬚變白了，而是在他深色的眼睛裡，人們能看到知識的力量。


He started a school or college at the Greek town of Croton in southern Italy. What was taught at the college was kept strictly secret and it was only after Pythagoras had died that the secret knowledge — or some parts of it — became known in the world. It was in this way that the Greeks heard for the first time something which other nations had known for a long time. The Greeks at that time had only a very sad idea of what happened to a human soul after death; they thought the souls of the dead lived in a dark world of shadows, the realm of Hades. But Pythagoras told his pupils what he had learned from the wise priests of Egypt: that the souls come back to earth again and are born again. In the Orient, in India, in Egypt, this was nothing new, but in Europe it was Pythagoras who was the first to tell his pupils about reincarnation, as it is called.

他在義大利南部的希臘城鎮克羅頓開辦了一所學校或學院。學院裡教的東西被嚴格保密，只有在畢達哥拉斯去世之後，這些秘密知識——或其中的一部分——才為世人所知。正是透過這種方式，希臘人第一次聽到了其他民族早已知曉的事情。那時的希臘人對人死後靈魂的命運只有非常悲觀的想像；他們認為亡者的靈魂生活在一個陰暗的影子世界裡——Hades（冥府）的領域。但畢達哥拉斯把他從埃及智慧祭司那裡學到的告訴了他的學生：靈魂會再次回到地球，再次出生。在東方，在印度，在埃及，這並不是什麼新鮮事，但在歐洲，畢達哥拉斯是第一個向他的學生講述「輪迴轉世」（reincarnation）的人。


That was one kind of knowledge Pythagoras brought from the East. Another kind of knowledge was about numbers, but it was quite different from the way we usually think about numbers. When Pythagoras had passed his tests and trials in Egypt, the priests of Egypt told him that the great pyramid, if you approach it from afar, you see first the peak, the point in which all sides come together. This point stands for one. If you come nearer and see the pyramid from a corner, you see two sides, and one is always darker than the other (because of the sunlight), this view shows the two-ness. But if you see the pyramid from the side, you see the triangle that stands for three. And if you could see the pyramid from above you would see the square base which stands for four-ness in the world.

這是畢達哥拉斯從東方帶回的一種知識。另一種知識是關於數字的，但和我們通常理解數字的方式截然不同。當畢達哥拉斯通過了在埃及的考驗之後，埃及的祭司告訴他：如果你從遠處接近大金字塔，首先看到的是塔尖——所有面匯聚的那個點。這個點代表「一」。走近一些從一個角落看金字塔，你會看到兩個面，其中一個總是比另一個暗（因為陽光的關係），這個視角展現了「二」的本質。但如果你從側面看金字塔，你看到的是三角形，代表「三」。而如果你能從上方看金字塔，你會看到正方形的底座，代表世界中「四」的本質。


And then the priests told him that the triangle stands for all threefoldness in the world and the square for all fourfoldness. And there are different kinds of triangles: there are as many kinds of triangles as there are "elements" in the world — four. There is one kind of triangle where all sides are of different lengths, it is called the scalene triangle and it is the triangle of air. There are triangles which have two sides equal, they are called isosceles triangles and these are the triangles of fire. There are triangles where all three sides have the same length, equilateral triangles, they belong to earth. And there is still one more kind of triangle, its sides are of different length but it has one right angle: it is the right-angled triangle, the triangle of water.

祭司們接著告訴他，三角形代表世間一切三重性，正方形代表一切四重性。三角形有不同的種類：三角形的種類和世界中「元素」的種類一樣多——四種。有一種三角形三邊長度各不相同，叫做不等邊三角形（scalene triangle），它是「風」的三角形。有一種三角形有兩邊相等，叫做等腰三角形（isosceles triangle），這是「火」的三角形。有一種三角形三邊都等長，叫做等邊三角形（equilateral triangle），它屬於「土」。還有一種三角形，三邊長度不同但有一個直角：這就是直角三角形（right-angled triangle），「水」的三角形。


# 34. Ptolemy
# 34. 托勒密

Pythagoras had learned geometry from the priests of Egypt. He had gone further than the Egyptians and had discovered the "theorem" about right-angled triangles which made him famous for all times. It was a simple construction — but because of it, the prophecy of the Oracle in Delphi came true and his name is still remembered today.

畢達哥拉斯從埃及的祭司那裡學到了幾何學。他比埃及人走得更遠，發現了關於直角三角形的「定理」，使他永世留名。那是一個簡單的構造——但正因如此，德爾菲神諭的預言成真了，他的名字至今仍被人們記住。


When Pythagoras was in Babylonia (then part of Persia), he came to the priests of Babylonia. These great astronomers had gathered more knowledge about sun, moon, planets and stars than any other people of the world.

當畢達哥拉斯在巴比倫（當時是波斯的一部分）時，他來到了巴比倫的祭司那裡。這些偉大的天文學家所積累的關於太陽、月亮、行星和恆星的知識，比世界上任何其他民族都多。


Many years later Pythagoras spoke to his pupils in Croton about his stay in Babylonia and what he had learned there. He told them how, by some means which remained secret, he was put into a kind of sleep that was not like ordinary sleep and not like an ordinary dream, because his mind was wide awake, but his body was lying almost as if it were dead. His mind was not in the body at all; he felt that he was soaring higher and higher. He was a spirit, free of the body, and rising from the earth into the cosmos. And, rising as a free spirit into the height, he heard the cosmos. The sun was a mighty voice, yet more beautiful than any human voice. The moon was a gentle, sweet voice, and the planets had each their own sound. And from the fixed stars far away there came a sound like a great choir; no music on earth can compare with the mighty, ever-changing music of the cosmos. It was not only the planet that we see that sounded, but the path of every planet is part of a great sphere, and the whole sphere of every planet sounded and sang and sent forth music. That was the great "music of the spheres" that can only be heard by souls free of their bodies. But then as he felt himself drawn back to earth, the music of the spheres became fainter; silence and darkness was around him, and then his strange sleep came to an end. He could feel his body again, and awoke.

多年後，畢達哥拉斯在克羅頓向他的學生們講述了他在巴比倫的經歷和所學。他告訴他們，透過某種始終保密的方式，他被帶入一種不同於普通睡眠、也不同於普通夢境的狀態——因為他的心智完全清醒，但他的身體幾乎像死了一樣躺著。他的心智完全不在身體裡；他感覺自己越飛越高。他是一個靈魂，脫離了肉體，從地球升入宇宙。當他作為自由的靈魂升入高處時，他聽見了宇宙。太陽是一個雄渾的聲音，卻比任何人類的聲音都更美。月亮是一個溫柔甜美的聲音，每顆行星都有自己的聲音。從遙遠的恆星那裡傳來像大合唱一般的聲音；地球上沒有任何音樂可以與宇宙那雄偉而不斷變化的音樂相比。發出聲音的不僅是我們看見的行星，每顆行星的軌道都是一個巨大天球的一部分，每顆行星的整個天球都在鳴響、歌唱、奏出音樂。這就是偉大的「天球之樂」（music of the spheres），只有脫離肉體的靈魂才能聽到。但當他感到自己被拉回地球時，天球之樂越來越微弱；寂靜與黑暗包圍了他，然後他奇異的沉睡結束了。他又能感覺到自己的身體，醒了過來。


Pythagoras told his pupils about the "music of the spheres," the music of the cosmos. He also told them that human souls have a very faint memory of this great music they heard before they were born. That is why on earth they make music and enjoy it; they are trying to remember the music of the spheres. And, of course, some people remember this music of the cosmos better than others.

畢達哥拉斯向他的學生講述了「天球之樂」——宇宙的音樂。他還告訴他們，人類的靈魂對出生前聽到的這偉大音樂有著非常微弱的記憶。這就是為什麼人們在地球上要創造音樂、享受音樂——他們在試圖回憶天球之樂。當然，有些人比其他人更能記住宇宙的音樂。


It was a great secret which Pythagoras told his pupils, but this secret was betrayed, and ever since people used to speak of the "harmonies" of the spheres. Even centuries later, Shakespeare, for instance, spoke of it in his play, The Merchant of Venice, and there is a poem by Goethe that also speaks of the "music of the spheres."

這是畢達哥拉斯告訴學生們的一個重大秘密，但這個秘密被洩露了，從此人們便開始談論天球的「和聲」。甚至幾個世紀後，Shakespeare（莎士比亞）在他的戲劇《威尼斯商人》（The Merchant of Venice）中提到了它，Goethe（歌德）也有一首詩談到了「天球之樂」。


Pythagoras also told his pupils something they could hardly believe. He said, "You think the stars, the whole sky with stars and sun and moon are turning around you. But you are mistaken. It is the earth which turns round, the earth is a globe which turns round its axis. The axis of the earth points to the Pole Star. That is why it does not appear to move. But the stars, the fixed stars do not move at all, it is the earth which turns round. And the earth does not just turn round on one spot in the cosmos, it moves on a path around the sun."

畢達哥拉斯還告訴他的學生一些他們幾乎不敢相信的事。他說：「你們以為星星、整個帶著星星和太陽和月亮的天空都在繞著你們轉。但你們錯了。轉動的是地球，地球是一個繞著自己的軸旋轉的球體。地球的軸指向北極星。這就是為什麼北極星看起來不動。但那些恆星、那些固定的星星根本不動，轉動的是地球。而且地球不只是在宇宙中原地轉動，它還沿著一條軌道繞太陽運行。」


That was a difficult thing to understand for Pythagoras' pupils. They found it hard to imagine that the solid earth on which they walked was not only spinning round, but moving on a path, on a circle, in the cosmos. Later, when the secrets of Pythagoras were made known, that was one thing few people in Greece or, later in Rome believed. There were a few who thought Pythagoras was right, but most people would not believe it. And so, the name of Pythagoras was praised for his geometry, for his theorem, and the "music of the spheres" was also accepted, but what he had said about earth and its movement was not taken seriously for two thousand years.

對畢達哥拉斯的學生來說，這是很難理解的事。他們很難想像他們腳下堅實的大地不僅在旋轉，而且還在宇宙中沿著一條軌道、一個圓圈移動。後來，當畢達哥拉斯的秘密被公開時，這是希臘——以及後來的羅馬——很少有人相信的一件事。有少數人認為畢達哥拉斯是對的，但大多數人不願相信。因此，畢達哥拉斯的名字因他的幾何學和定理而受到讚頌，「天球之樂」也被接受了，但他關於地球及其運動的說法在兩千年裡都沒有被認真對待。


About six hundred years after Pythagoras, in Alexandria in Egypt a Greek called Ptolemy wrote a book about astronomy. Ptolemy had heard about Pythagoras and of the spheres and their music. In his book he described that the earth was in the centre of seven spheres which carried the sun, moon and planets, and an eighth sphere which held all the fixed stars. The moon, being the fastest, had the smallest sphere. Then came the spheres — ever larger — of Mercury, Venus, the sun, Mars, Jupiter, Saturn, and finally the greatest sphere was the sphere of the fixed stars.

畢達哥拉斯之後大約六百年，在埃及的 Alexandria（亞歷山大城），一位名叫 Ptolemy（托勒密）的希臘人寫了一本關於天文學的書。托勒密聽說過畢達哥拉斯以及天球和天球之樂。在他的書中，他描述地球位於七個天球的中心，這些天球承載著太陽、月亮和行星，還有第八個天球承載著所有的恆星。月亮移動最快，所以有最小的天球。然後是越來越大的天球——依次是水星、金星、太陽、火星、木星、土星，最後最大的天球是恆星天球。


Pythagoras had also said that the earth moved, but Ptolemy had either not heard that or did not believe it. In any case, he did not mention it in his book. People thought Ptolemy was a very clever man. He was greatly respected in his own time, and for many centuries later.

畢達哥拉斯還說過地球會動，但托勒密要麼沒聽說，要麼不相信。無論如何，他在書中沒有提到這一點。人們認為托勒密是一個非常聰明的人。他在自己的時代和此後的許多個世紀裡都備受尊崇。


In time, people no longer understood that these spheres were not something hard and solid; they thought that spheres were like transparent solid globes around the earth and that the planets, sun, moon, rolled around these globes. They imagined the spheres were really something solid which one could touch if one could fly high enough. But Pythagoras had spoken of something he had only known and heard when his soul was out of his body, as long as we are in the body these spheres cannot be seen or touched.

隨著時間推移，人們不再理解這些天球並非堅硬實體的東西；他們以為天球就像圍繞地球的透明固體球，行星、太陽、月亮在這些球上滾動。他們想像天球真的是實心的東西，如果能飛得夠高就能觸摸到。但畢達哥拉斯所說的是他的靈魂離開身體時才能認識和聽到的東西——只要我們還在肉體之中，這些天球就無法被看到或觸碰。


For fifteen hundred years the system of Ptolemy was looked upon as something one could not doubt at all. Only when the spring equinox entered a new constellation, the Fishes, did human minds change and people began to question whether Ptolemy had been right.

一千五百年來，托勒密的體系被視為不容置疑的真理。只有當春分點進入一個新的星座——雙魚座時，人類的思維才開始改變，人們開始質疑托勒密是否正確。


# 35. Copernicus
# 35. 哥白尼

We have heard about the threefoldness in human life: we think, we feel and we do things. But we are different from one other. Some people are very good at thinking, but when it comes to making anything with their hands they are clumsy. Some people have very warm, kind feelings for others, they will do anything to help others, but they are not very clever when it comes to thinking. And some people are born to do great deeds, like Alexander the Great or Julius Caesar, but they are neither great thinkers nor specially kind hearted.

我們已經聽說過人類生命的三重性：我們思考、我們感受、我們行動。但我們彼此不同。有些人非常善於思考，但一到動手做東西就笨手笨腳。有些人對他人有非常溫暖善良的情感，願意為幫助他人做任何事，但在思考方面卻不太靈光。還有些人天生就是做大事的料，像 Alexander the Great（亞歷山大大帝）或 Julius Caesar（凱撒），但他們既不是偉大的思想家，也不是特別心地善良的人。


Alexander or Caesar, Richard the Lionheart or the Vikings who sailed to Vinland were heroes of deeds, not of thinking or feeling. St Francis of Assisi was a hero of feeling, as was Dr Barnardo who had this great love for the poor children without proper homes. There are also heroes of thinking. And Pythagoras was such a hero of thought. The theorem which is named after him is a thought; so was the idea of reincarnation and what he said about the harmony of the spheres or the movement of the earth. These were also great thoughts.

亞歷山大或凱撒、Richard the Lionheart（獅心王理查）或航行到 Vinland（文蘭）的維京人，都是行動的英雄，不是思考或感受的英雄。Assisi（亞西西）的 St Francis（聖方濟各）是感受的英雄，Dr Barnardo（巴納多博士）也是，他對那些沒有適當家園的貧困兒童有著偉大的愛。也有思考的英雄。而畢達哥拉斯就是這樣一位思想的英雄。以他命名的定理是一個思想；輪迴轉世的觀念，以及他關於天球和聲與地球運動的學說，也都是偉大的思想。


However, the astronomer of Alexandria, Ptolemy, was not a great hero of thought. He only repeated something Pythagoras had said. But for nearly two thousand years Ptolemy's ideas were believed by everybody. Soon after the year 1400 the spring equinox came into the constellation of Pisces, the Fishes, and the human mind began to change. After a hundred years, by about 1500, people began to ask questions they had never asked before.

然而，亞歷山大城的天文學家托勒密並不是一位偉大的思想英雄。他只是重複了畢達哥拉斯說過的東西。但近兩千年來，托勒密的觀點被所有人相信。在一四零零年之後不久，春分點進入了雙魚座，人類的思維開始改變。再過一百年，到大約一五零零年，人們開始提出以前從未問過的問題。


In Poland there lived a canon of the Church, a kind of priest, whose hobby was astronomy. The name of this priest was Nicolaus Copernicus. Being an educated man, Copernicus read Latin and Greek, and in some books of ancient times which had survived he read about Pythagoras. Pythagoras had not only spoken of the harmonies of the spheres, but had also spoken of the movement of the earth. Now one thing was very complicated in Ptolemy's world picture, and that was the "dance" of the planets. If you observe the planet Jupiter or Mars, for instance, you can see over weeks and months that the planet moves for a time in one direction, but then it moves in the opposite direction making a loop.

在波蘭，有一位教會的參事——一種神職人員——他的愛好是天文學。這位神父的名字叫 Nicolaus Copernicus（尼古拉·哥白尼）。哥白尼是個受過教育的人，能讀拉丁文和希臘文。在一些保存下來的古代書籍中，他讀到了畢達哥拉斯的事蹟。畢達哥拉斯不僅談到了天球的和聲，也談到了地球的運動。在托勒密的世界圖景中有一件事非常複雜，那就是行星的「舞蹈」。如果你觀察木星或火星，經過數週數月，你會看到行星先朝一個方向移動一段時間，然後又反方向移動，畫出一個迴圈。


The Greek astronomers and Ptolemy explained this by saying the planets moved on a little circle or sphere, the epicycle, which moved around the great circle or sphere. Each planet (though not sun and moon) had its great circle as well as its smaller epicycle.

希臘天文學家和托勒密對此的解釋是：行星在一個小圓或小天球上運動——叫做本輪（epicycle），而這個本輪又繞著大圓或大天球運動。每顆行星（太陽和月亮除外）都有它的大圓和較小的本輪。


Now Copernicus thought, if I ride on a horse and I overtake another rider on the road, it may seem to me that this other rider is going backwards, but he is not, it is only my own movement, my own speed, which leaves him further and further behind. Of course, because we see the ground we know the other rider is not really going backwards; but what if we could not see the ground? Perhaps the planets did not really travel backwards, but earth moved on and this made the planets look as if they were going backwards. Copernicus found that if he let the earth move around the sun, and the planets too, move around the sun, then because of these two movements the planets appear to make loops and go backwards.

哥白尼想到，如果我騎馬超過路上另一個騎者，在我看來那個騎者好像在後退，但他並沒有，那只是我自己的移動、我自己的速度，把他越甩越遠。當然，因為我們能看到地面，所以知道那個騎者並不是真的在後退；但如果我們看不到地面呢？也許行星並不是真的在倒退，而是地球在向前移動，這使得行星看起來好像在後退。哥白尼發現，如果讓地球繞太陽運行，行星也繞太陽運行，那麼由於這兩種運動，行星就會看起來在畫迴圈、在倒退。


So Copernicus said that the sun does not move in a circle round the earth, but that it is the earth which goes in a circle round the sun; the sun must be fixed. And as the earth goes round the sun in one year, we see the sun against a different background of stars, the constellations of the zodiac.

所以哥白尼說，不是太陽繞地球做圓周運動，而是地球繞太陽做圓周運動；太陽必定是固定的。由於地球一年繞太陽一圈，我們看到太陽的背景是不同的恆星——也就是黃道的各個星座。


What about the moon? The moon does not make loops, but we see the moon in different constellations of the zodiac during the course of a month. The moon is the only thing moving in a circle round the earth. So the world-picture Copernicus worked out had all planets going round the sun, and the earth also going round the sun, making the earth a planet. But the moon goes round the earth, and so is not a planet, but a satellite.

那月亮呢？月亮不會畫迴圈，但在一個月的過程中，我們看到月亮出現在黃道的不同星座中。月亮是唯一繞地球做圓周運動的天體。所以哥白尼推演出的世界圖景是：所有行星都繞太陽運行，地球也繞太陽運行，使地球成為一顆行星。但月亮繞地球運行，因此不是行星，而是衛星。


All this was thought out by this man Copernicus, and it gave a much simpler explanation of all the movements we can see in the sky. But there was nothing to prove that it was true, it was all just an idea, a theory, and you can work out the movements of the sun, moon and planets with either system. So for a long time he did not even write a book about his idea. Only when Copernicus was an old man did his friends, whom he had told about his idea, press him to write it all down. In 1543 he finally did, calling his book, On the Revolutions of the Celestial Spheres. He saw the first copy of the book on the day he died.

這一切都是哥白尼這個人想出來的，它對我們在天空中看到的所有運動給出了簡單得多的解釋。但沒有任何東西能證明它是正確的，一切只是一個想法、一個理論，用兩種體系都可以計算出太陽、月亮和行星的運動。所以很長一段時間他甚至沒有寫書來闡述他的想法。直到哥白尼年老時，他那些聽他談過這個想法的朋友們才催促他把一切寫下來。一五四三年他終於完成了，書名為《天體運行論》（On the Revolutions of the Celestial Spheres）。他在去世的那一天見到了這本書的第一份印刷本。
# 36. Tycho Brahe
# 36. 第谷·布拉赫

Three years after Copernicus died, Tycho Brahe was born. He came from a noble family, his father and uncle were at the court of the King of Denmark. For most of his childhood he lived with his uncle. When Tycho was thirteen years old he was studying at the University of Copenhagen. In those days boys often went to university at the age of 13 or 14. There he heard that there would be an eclipse of the sun the following day. Tycho eagerly watched the next day, and the sun really did turn dark. Young Tycho cried out, "A man who can predict such a thing must be like God." From that day onwards he was determined to become an astronomer.

Copernicus（哥白尼）過世三年後，Tycho Brahe（第谷·布拉赫）出生了。他出身貴族世家，父親和叔父都在丹麥國王的宮廷任職。童年大部分時間他與叔父同住。第谷十三歲時便在哥本哈根大學求學——在那個年代，男孩十三、四歲上大學是常有的事。在那裡，他聽說隔天將會發生日食。第谷滿懷期待地觀看，太陽果然暗了下來。年輕的第谷驚呼：「能預測這種事的人，簡直像上帝一樣。」從那天起，他立志要成為一名天文學家。


His uncle wanted Tycho to study law, but he was much more interested in astronomy. At night when he was supposed to sleep he stole out into the garden to watch the stars. He soon knew every star one can see with the naked eye. He studied every available map of the stars. At the age of sixteen he was sent with a tutor to finish his studies of law at universities in Germany. His tutor, however, soon found he had undertaken a hopeless task. However hard he tried, he could not succeed in interesting Tycho in anything but astronomy. Any money Tycho managed to get was immediately secretly spent on astronomical books and instruments. He wrote, "None of the charts match the others. There are as many measurements as there are astronomers and all of them disagree."

叔父希望第谷學法律，但他對天文學的興趣大得多。夜裡本該就寢時，他偷偷溜到花園觀星。不久，他便認識了肉眼所能見到的每一顆星。他研讀了所有能找到的星圖。十六歲時，他被派去德國的大學，帶著一位家庭教師完成法律學業。然而家庭教師很快發現這是一項無望的任務——不管怎麼努力，都無法讓第谷對天文學以外的事產生興趣。第谷一拿到錢，就立刻偷偷花在天文書籍和儀器上。他寫道：「沒有兩張星圖是一致的。有多少天文學家，就有多少種測量結果，而且彼此矛盾。」


He resolved to systematically observe the skies and make the most accurate map of the stars. He made himself special instruments to measure the angles between stars. To the disappointment of his uncle he refused to go riding and hunting as all other young noblemen did. He said, "I prefer to look at God's beautiful work, I am not going to waste any time riding or hunting." When he was nineteen Tycho's uncle died, and he was no longer forced to study law and expect to do things he did not want.

他下定決心要有系統地觀測天空，繪製最精確的星圖。他自製了特殊儀器來測量星與星之間的角度。令叔父失望的是，他拒絕像其他年輕貴族那樣去騎馬和打獵。他說：「我寧願欣賞上帝美麗的造物，不想把時間浪費在騎馬打獵上。」十九歲時叔父去世，他不再被迫學法律，也不必做自己不想做的事了。


At that time all people — and all astronomers — believed that the stars ruled human life on earth. If you knew the position of the planets on the day a person was born, you could foretell what was going to happen to that person. Now young Tycho wrote a poem in which he predicted that, according to his calculations of the stars, the Sultan of Turkey would die in October 1566 during an eclipse of the moon. And, strangely enough, the Sultan did die around that time. This made Tycho's name known.

在那個時代，所有人——包括所有天文學家——都相信星辰主宰著地上人類的命運。如果你知道一個人出生那天行星的位置，就能預言他將來會遇到什麼事。年輕的第谷寫了一首詩，預言根據他的星象計算，土耳其蘇丹會在一五六六年十月的月食期間去世。說也奇怪，蘇丹真的在那前後死了。這使第谷的名字傳開了。


However, what made Tycho really famous in the whole of Europe was something that occurred a few years later. One evening in early winter, as he was walking home, he looked up at the sky and saw a brilliant star high in the constellation of Cassiopeia. He immediately knew there was no star there, and he also knew that no planet could ever stray that far from the zodiac. To make sure he called his servants to ask whether they could see this star. They certainly could, and so Tycho knew it was not a creation of his mind, or something he had eaten or drunk.

然而，真正讓第谷聞名全歐洲的，是幾年後發生的一件事。初冬的一個傍晚，他走在回家的路上，抬頭望向天空，在仙后座（Cassiopeia）高處看到一顆明亮的星。他立刻知道那裡本來沒有星，也知道任何行星都不可能偏離黃道那麼遠。為了確認，他叫來僕人，問他們能不能看到這顆星。他們當然看得到，於是第谷明白這不是他的幻覺，也不是吃了什麼喝了什麼造成的。


Tycho immediately when he got home pulled out his great instruments to measure the exact position of the new star. He soon calculated it was not some bright light in the clouds, but a real star, as distant as sun, planets and stars. Having observed the new star for some weeks, Tycho wrote up his observations. His friends tried to dissuade him from writing, pointing out it was beneath the dignity of a nobleman to write a book.

第谷一回到家，立刻拿出他的大型儀器來測量這顆新星的精確位置。他很快計算出這不是雲中的某種亮光，而是一顆真正的恆星，和太陽、行星、群星一樣遙遠。觀測了新星數週之後，第谷寫下了他的觀測紀錄。朋友們試圖勸阻他，指出寫書有損貴族的尊嚴。


But Tycho was undeterred, and published his book, De Nova Stella. Like all learned books of that time it was written in Latin. Astronomers still call a new star a "nova" from the Latin.

但第谷毫不退縮，出版了他的著作《De Nova Stella》（新星論）。和當時所有學術著作一樣，這本書用拉丁文寫成。天文學家至今仍用拉丁文的「nova」來稱呼新星。


Following this, the King of Denmark made Tycho Brahe his court astronomer. He gave him a whole island on which Tycho built the greatest observatory that had ever been built for watching the stars. He had many servants and assistants — instrument-makers, mathematicians, builders. He not only had farms and bakers to supply all the people with food, he even built a paper mill on the island to ensure there was enough paper to write down all his observations. Here on this island Tycho made finer, more exact instruments for mapping the course of the planets than anybody had ever had before, and produced more accurate charts of the stars than ever before.

此後，丹麥國王任命第谷·布拉赫為宮廷天文學家，並將整座島嶼賜給他。第谷在島上建造了有史以來最宏偉的天文觀測台。他擁有許多僕人和助手——儀器製造師、數學家、建築師。他不僅有農場和麵包師傅供應所有人的食物，甚至在島上建了一座造紙廠，確保有足夠的紙張記錄所有觀測資料。在這座島上，第谷製作了前所未有的精密儀器來繪製行星軌跡，產出了有史以來最精確的星圖。


Tycho, like all astronomers of that time, had been taught the system of Ptolemy with the earth in the centre and the sun, moon and planets going round the earth. But he had also read the book by Copernicus with the new idea that the sun stood still and the earth and other planets moved round it.

第谷和當時所有天文學家一樣，學的是 Ptolemy（托勒密）的體系——地球在中心，太陽、月亮和行星繞著地球運行。但他也讀過哥白尼的書，那個全新的想法：太陽靜止不動，地球和其他行星繞太陽運行。


The system of Ptolemy had one great advantage. It was what we really see: sun, moon and planets going round the earth. The Copernican system, with earth and the planets going round the sun and the moon going round the earth, was simpler, but it was not what we see.

托勒密體系有一個很大的優點：它符合我們實際所見——太陽、月亮和行星繞著地球運行。哥白尼體系——地球和行星繞太陽運行、月亮繞地球運行——雖然更簡潔，但並不是我們所看到的。


Tycho of course knew both systems, but he did not like to give up the world-picture of Ptolemy altogether. After all, we do see the stars and sun and moon going round the earth. And so he thought out a different system. He said the planets — Venus, Mercury, Mars, Jupiter, Saturn — go round the sun (so Copernicus is quite right), but the sun goes round the earth, and so the planets, following the sun, go round the earth too (and so Ptolemy is also right). And the movements of the planets can just as well be explained with this system as with that of Copernicus.

第谷當然了解兩套體系，但他不願完全放棄托勒密的宇宙圖像。畢竟，我們確實看到星辰、太陽和月亮繞著地球運行。於是他構想出一套不同的體系。他說，行星——金星、水星、火星、木星、土星——繞太陽運行（所以哥白尼是對的），但太陽繞地球運行，因此行星跟隨太陽，也繞地球運行（所以托勒密也是對的）。用這套體系來解釋行星運動，和用哥白尼體系一樣可行。


# 37. Johannes Kepler
# 37. 約翰尼斯·克卜勒

When the King of Denmark died, Tycho quarrelled with the new King. Luckily, Tycho was invited by Emperor Rudolf of Austria to come to his court in Prague as court astronomer.

丹麥國王去世後，第谷與新國王發生衝突。幸運的是，奧地利皇帝 Rudolf（魯道夫）邀請第谷到布拉格的宮廷擔任宮廷天文學家。


Meanwhile, a young German, Johannes Kepler, had worked for some years in Austria as professor of astronomy. Kepler thought that the earth is like a living being. It breathes in and out. As the blood goes round our body, so the waters of the earth go round, they rise as clouds, come down as rain and flow as streams back to the sea. The earth is like a living being, and living beings don't stand still, they move. Kepler's great quest was to find the answer to why God had made the cosmos as he did. Why had God placed the planets just at those distances from the sun, and not at other distances? And he wrote about this quest in his great book, The Mysteries of the Cosmos.

與此同時，一位年輕的德國人 Johannes Kepler（約翰尼斯·克卜勒）已在奧地利擔任天文學教授數年。克卜勒認為地球就像一個活的生命體。它呼吸著，有吸有吐。就像血液在我們體內循環一樣，地球上的水也在循環——水升為雲，降為雨，匯成溪流回到大海。地球就像一個生命體，而生命體不會靜止不動，他們會運動。克卜勒畢生的追尋，是要找到上帝為何如此創造宇宙的答案。上帝為什麼恰好把行星放在那些距離上，而不是別的距離？他在偉大的著作《宇宙的奧祕》中寫下了這個探索。


When war came to Austria, Kepler had to flee with his family, and came to Prague where he was appointed as Tycho's assistant. So these two great astronomers came together. But, as sometimes happens, the two did not get on. Tycho, the nobleman, was used to having many servants and assistants, who obeyed his instructions without question, and he treated Kepler like another of his assistants. Kepler who had been a university professor and was known for his writing throughout Europe felt he should be treated more as an equal, and not be left to eat at the servants' table. It also did not help that Kepler was a firm believer in Copernicus' system, while Tycho preferred his own.

戰爭降臨奧地利時，克卜勒不得不帶著家人逃離，來到布拉格，被任命為第谷的助手。兩位偉大的天文學家就這樣走到了一起。但正如有時會發生的那樣，兩人處不來。出身貴族的第谷習慣了有許多僕人和助手無條件服從指令，他把克卜勒當成又一個助手來對待。而克卜勒身為大學教授，著作聞名全歐洲，覺得自己應該被當作平等的人對待，而不是被安排在僕人桌上吃飯。更何況克卜勒堅定地信奉哥白尼體系，而第谷偏好自己的體系，這也加深了兩人的隔閡。


However, the two had a grudging respect for each other. For Tycho was the patient and accurate observer of the stars, while Kepler was a genius gifted with mathematical ability and insights.

不過，兩人之間仍存在著不情願的尊重。因為第谷是耐心而精確的觀星者，而克卜勒則是一位天賦異稟的數學天才，擁有深刻的洞察力。


When Kepler examined Tycho's accurate observations of the movement of the planets he found some irritating differences between the actual, observed position of the planet as Tycho had recorded, and the calculated position using the Copernican system. Kepler spent many years calculating. Only some years after Tycho Brahe had died, did Kepler at long last hit upon another idea. Perhaps things would work out more accurately if the planets and the earth were going round the sun not in a circle, but in an almost circular ellipse.

當克卜勒檢視第谷對行星運動的精確觀測紀錄時，他發現了一些惱人的差異——第谷記錄的行星實際觀測位置，與用哥白尼體系計算出的位置不完全吻合。克卜勒花了許多年進行計算。直到第谷·布拉赫去世數年之後，克卜勒終於靈光一閃，想到了另一個可能：如果行星和地球繞太陽運行的軌道不是圓形，而是近乎圓形的橢圓呢？


When Kepler worked out the paths of the planets and of earth round the sun as an ellipse, he found the planets really were in the places he had worked out. This is the world-picture which astronomers still have today: the moon moves round the earth in an ellipse, and the earth and the other planets move round the sun in ellipses.

當克卜勒以橢圓軌道計算行星和地球繞太陽的路徑時，他發現行星確實在他計算出的位置上。這就是天文學家至今仍然使用的宇宙圖像：月亮沿橢圓軌道繞地球運行，地球和其他行星沿橢圓軌道繞太陽運行。


The earth spins round on its axis, and we call this spin one day of 24 hours. And the earth moves in an ellipse round the sun, and one complete ellipse we call a year.

地球繞自身的軸旋轉，我們把這一次旋轉稱為一天，二十四小時。而地球沿著橢圓軌道繞太陽運行，走完一圈橢圓，我們稱之為一年。


To draw an ellipse with a piece of string: knot a string in a loop, stick two pins into a paper, a small distance apart, and draw the ellipse by running a pencil around the string. The closer the pins are, the more the ellipse becomes like a circle; the further apart they are, the flatter the ellipse becomes.

用一根繩子畫橢圓：把繩子打成一個環，在紙上釘兩根大頭針，兩針之間留一小段距離，然後用鉛筆繃緊繩圈，沿著繩子畫一圈，就能畫出橢圓。兩根針越靠近，橢圓就越像圓；兩根針越遠，橢圓就越扁。


But there is no real proof that the path of the earth is an ellipse: the calculations work out that way.
