And perhaps one day somebody will come with a quite new idea about the earth's movement or the sun's movement, and it will work out just as well. The only reason why the world-picture of Copernicus and Kepler is accepted today by all astronomers is that it is the easiest way for calculating where any planet will be, but that is not proof that the dance of the planets is as we imagine it.

但實際上並沒有真正的證據證明地球的軌道就是橢圓——只是計算結果符合這個模型。也許有一天，某個人會提出關於地球運動或太陽運動的全新想法，結果同樣行得通。哥白尼和克卜勒的宇宙圖像之所以被今天所有天文學家接受，唯一的理由是它是計算任何行星位置最方便的方法，但這並不能證明行星之舞真的如我們所想像的那樣。


# 38. Galileo and the Telescope
# 38. 伽利略與望遠鏡

While Johannes Kepler was still working on his ellipses, a man in Holland had made a curious discovery. There is a story that it was not his own discovery, it was made by children. This man, called Hans Lippershey, was a master lens grinder who made spectacles. He saw two children playing with his lenses in his shop who said they could make the far away weather-vane appear upside-down but much closer.

就在克卜勒還在鑽研他的橢圓軌道時，荷蘭有個人做出了一項奇妙的發現。有個故事說，這其實不是他自己的發現，而是孩子們發現的。這個人叫 Hans Lippershey（漢斯·利珀希），是一位製作眼鏡的磨鏡師傅。他看到兩個孩子在他的店裡玩弄鏡片，說他們能讓遠處的風向標看起來倒過來，但大了很多。


A neighbouring spectacle-maker, Sacharias Jansen, seems to have come up with the same idea around the same time. No one has managed to find out which of the two spectacle-makers was really first or whether one stole the idea from another. But that was the beginning of the telescope and binoculars.

鄰近的另一位眼鏡師傅 Sacharias Jansen（薩哈里亞斯·楊森）似乎在差不多同一時間也想到了同樣的點子。沒有人能查清楚兩位眼鏡師傅到底誰先想到，還是一個偷了另一個的點子。但這就是望遠鏡和雙筒望遠鏡的起源。


The Dutch spectacle makers were the first to discover the use of two lenses for telescopes, and it was also a Dutchman called Leeuwenhoek who made the first microscope. The Dutch wanted to keep their invention secret. At that time, the Dutch were at war against Spain and they thought it was a great advantage if they could observe with their telescopes what the enemies were doing far away, before the enemies could do so. They thought of the telescope only as something useful for their war. But, of course, such things cannot be kept secret, and rumours about the Dutch invention spread to other countries.

荷蘭的眼鏡師傅率先發現了用兩片鏡片製造望遠鏡的方法，而製造出第一台顯微鏡的也是一位叫 Leeuwenhoek（列文虎克）的荷蘭人。荷蘭人想把他們的發明保密。當時荷蘭正與西班牙交戰，他們認為如果能用望遠鏡觀察遠方敵人的動態，而敵人卻做不到，那將是巨大的優勢。他們只把望遠鏡當成戰爭中有用的工具。但這種事當然不可能保密，關於荷蘭發明的傳言很快傳到了其他國家。


At that time in Italy there lived a man who is another of these heroes of thought, a hero of science. His name was Galileo Galilei, and he was deeply interested in astronomy. He had read the books of Copernicus, Tycho Brahe and Kepler, and he was quite certain that Copernicus and Kepler were right: that the earth moved round the sun. And when rumours of this Dutch invention of the telescope reached Galileo, he immediately realized that this new invention could be used for watching the stars. As he could not get any telescopes from the Dutch, who would not part with their secret, Galileo experimented and made his own telescope.

在那時的義大利，住著一位思想英雄、科學英雄。他的名字叫 Galileo Galilei（伽利略·伽利萊），對天文學有著深切的興趣。他讀過哥白尼、第谷·布拉赫和克卜勒的著作，確信哥白尼和克卜勒是對的：地球繞太陽運行。當荷蘭望遠鏡發明的傳言傳到伽利略耳中時，他立刻意識到這項新發明可以用來觀測星辰。由於荷蘭人不肯透露祕密，他拿不到望遠鏡，於是伽利略自己動手實驗，造出了自己的望遠鏡。


And so Galileo became the first man who looked at the stars, at the sun, moon and planets with a telescope. Imagine how he felt: he could see things no one had ever seen before; he not only saw more stars, but saw details of the moon and the planets no one had even thought of before. He made three great discoveries. First, he saw that certain dark bits on the moon were shadows cast by mountains — so the moon had mountains like the earth. Secondly, when looking at the planet Venus, he saw that it had phases like the moon. But his proudest discovery was that not only did the earth have a moon going round it, but that the planet Jupiter had moons. Galileo could see not just one, but four moons going round Jupiter. He was proud of his discoveries and he became famous as the first man who had seen the moons of Jupiter.

就這樣，伽利略成為第一個用望遠鏡觀看星辰、太陽、月亮和行星的人。想像一下他的心情：他能看到從未有人見過的事物；他不僅看到了更多的星星，還看到了月亮和行星上從未有人想到的細節。他做了三大發現。第一，他看到月亮上某些暗色部分是山脈投下的陰影——所以月亮和地球一樣有山。第二，觀測金星時，他看到金星有像月亮一樣的盈虧變化。但他最自豪的發現是：不僅地球有一個月亮繞它運行，木星（Jupiter）也有衛星。伽利略看到的不是一個，而是四個衛星繞木星運行。他為自己的發現感到驕傲，也因成為第一個看到木星衛星的人而聞名。


But when Galileo wrote a book about his discoveries and defended the ideas of Copernicus and Kepler — that the earth travelled round the sun — it brought him into great trouble.

然而，當伽利略寫書闡述他的發現，並為哥白尼和克卜勒的觀點辯護——地球繞太陽運行——時，他陷入了巨大的麻煩。


At that time monks and priests were the only people who had any learning. And if the Pope in Rome, the head of the Church, decided this or that was not good for people to know or to hear about, then that was the end of it. But now things were changing. Not only had Luther rebelled against the authority of the Catholic church in Rome, but people who were not monks or priests, like Tycho, Kepler, Galileo, came with all sorts of new ideas. The Pope in Rome and his Cardinals did not like it.

在那個時代，僧侶和神父是唯一受過教育的人。如果羅馬教宗——教會的最高領袖——決定某件事不宜讓人知道或聽聞，那就到此為止了。但如今情況正在改變。不僅 Luther（路德）反抗了羅馬天主教會的權威，而且像第谷、克卜勒、伽利略這些不是僧侶也不是神父的人，紛紛帶來了各種新思想。羅馬教宗和他的樞機主教們很不高興。


So Galileo was called to Rome, and the Pope was so powerful in those days that Galileo could not refuse. In Rome he was told that the Pope did not approve of what he had written. These ideas of Pythagoras, of Copernicus and Kepler — about the earth going round the sun — were not proven, and they also contradicted the word of the Holy Bible. (For instance, during a battle Joshua prayed to God to make the sun stand still, so that he could finish the battle before dark. How, asked the Cardinals, could God make the sun stand still if it was standing still already?)

於是伽利略被召到羅馬，而教宗在當時權力極大，伽利略無法拒絕。在羅馬，他被告知教宗不認可他所寫的內容。這些 Pythagoras（畢達哥拉斯）、哥白尼和克卜勒的觀點——關於地球繞太陽運行——尚未被證實，而且與聖經的話語相悖。（例如，在一場戰役中，約書亞向上帝祈禱讓太陽停住，好讓他在天黑前打完仗。樞機主教們質問：如果太陽本來就是靜止的，上帝又怎能讓它停住呢？）


Galileo could choose between publicly apologizing and admitting that this idea was a great mistake, or being imprisoned for the rest of his life. Galileo was by then an old man, and he had no wish to end his days locked up, and so, against his real belief, he apologized, called his book a great mistake, and was allowed to go.

伽利略只能在兩者之間選擇：公開道歉、承認這個想法是一個巨大的錯誤，或者被終身監禁。伽利略當時已是老人，不想在牢獄中度過餘生，於是違背自己真正的信念，道了歉，稱自己的書是一大錯誤，才被允許離去。


From that time onwards he wrote and spoke no more about the ideas of Copernicus and Kepler, but, of course, he had not really changed his mind. So when science began it was not without danger to speak one's mind openly.

從那以後，他再也不談論、不書寫哥白尼和克卜勒的學說了。但他當然並沒有真正改變想法。可見科學萌芽之初，公開表達自己的觀點並非沒有危險。


From the time of Galileo onwards more and more people looked at the stars through telescopes, and more and more discoveries have been made. Modern observatories have much bigger telescopes than Galileo had. Instead of lenses nowadays they use large concave mirrors. So you look down into a mirror at the sky, not up to the stars. At present (2011), the largest of these telescopes is in the Canary Islands, and it has a mirror more than 10 metres (33 ft) in diameter.

從伽利略的時代開始，越來越多人透過望遠鏡觀看星辰，也做出了越來越多的發現。現代天文台擁有比伽利略的大得多的望遠鏡。如今不用透鏡，而是使用大型凹面鏡。所以你是往下看一面映照天空的鏡子，而不是仰望星辰。截至二〇一一年，最大的望遠鏡在加那利群島（Canary Islands），鏡面直徑超過十公尺（三十三英尺）。


But there is something very curious about all the discoveries made with the help of these telescopes. All kinds of things are seen which no one had seen before, but the telescopes did not answer any questions, they only brought new riddles. Looking at the stars through a telescope has not proven or explained everything, it has only brought us new questions, new mysteries and new problems. It is quite possible that the priests of Babylonia who had no telescopes knew less but understood more about the cosmos than we do.

但是，透過這些望遠鏡所做的一切發現，有一件非常奇妙的事。人們看到了各種以前從未見過的東西，但望遠鏡並沒有回答任何問題，只帶來了新的謎團。透過望遠鏡觀看星辰並沒有證明或解釋一切，只帶給我們新的問題、新的奧祕和新的難題。很可能巴比倫（Babylonia）的祭司們雖然沒有望遠鏡，知道的比我們少，但對宇宙的理解卻比我們深。


Of course astronomers do not look at the sun itself — this would ruin their eyesight. The telescope is directed at the sun and the picture of the sun caught on a screen. However, even with the largest telescope we do not see the sun itself. Just as the earth is surrounded by the atmosphere, so the sun, too, has a kind of atmosphere; but it is not air, it is shining light. As light in Greek is photos, this layer of light around the sun is called the photosphere, a sphere of light. This sphere of light around the sun is so bright that no human eye can see through it. So, no one has ever seen anything but the outer layer of light of the sun. What is inside this sphere of light, we do not know.

當然，天文學家不會直接觀看太陽本身——那會毀壞視力。他們把望遠鏡對準太陽，讓太陽的影像投射在螢幕上。然而，即使用最大的望遠鏡，我們也看不到太陽本身。就像地球被大氣層包圍一樣，太陽也有一種「大氣層」，但那不是空氣，而是發光的光。因為希臘文中光是「photos」，所以太陽周圍的這層光被稱為光球（photosphere），意思是光的球體。太陽周圍的光球如此明亮，人眼根本無法看穿它。所以，從來沒有人看到過太陽光球以內的東西。光球裡面是什麼，我們不得而知。


When Galileo first looked at the sun through a telescope (yes, he did ruin his eyesight, going almost blind in old age), he was puzzled. In the bright light he saw small dark spots. Galileo did not know what they were, and though we now know much more about these sunspots, we don't really know what they are. If we observe them for a few days, they appear to wander round the sun, indicating that the sun rotates about its axis, as earth does. But unlike the earth some parts of the sun rotate in about 21 days, other parts (away from the sun's equator) take longer, up to 26 days.

伽利略第一次用望遠鏡觀察太陽時（是的，他確實因此毀壞了視力，晚年幾乎失明），他感到困惑。在明亮的光中，他看到了一些小小的暗點。伽利略不知道那是什麼，而儘管我們現在對這些太陽黑子（sunspots）了解多了許多，卻仍不真正知道它們是什麼。如果連續觀察幾天，會發現它們似乎在太陽表面移動，這表明太陽和地球一樣繞著自己的軸旋轉。但與地球不同的是，太陽有些部分大約二十一天轉一圈，其他部分（遠離赤道處）則需要更久，長達二十六天。


These mysterious sunspots come and go, none of them ever lasting more than a few months, and others appear. Sometimes there are more, sometimes there are less; but there seems to be a certain rhythm. Every eleven years there is a large number of sunspots, and then they become less. And — no one can tell you why — every eleven years here on earth is a specially good year for wine-growers.

這些神祕的太陽黑子時隱時現，沒有一個能持續超過幾個月，又有新的出現。有時多一些，有時少一些；但似乎有一定的節律。每隔十一年，太陽黑子數量就特別多，然後逐漸減少。而且——沒有人能告訴你為什麼——每隔十一年，地球上就會有一個對葡萄酒農來說特別好的年份。


Something somehow connected with sunspots is that when there are so many of them, there are days when radio reception is poorer than usual, the magnetic compasses of ships go awry, and the northern lights are more prominent.

某種與太陽黑子有關聯的現象是：當太陽黑子特別多時，有些日子無線電接收比平常差，船上的磁羅盤失靈，極光也更加顯著。


Another thing which the telescopes show are enormous "flames" reaching out from the sun; they are called solar flares. Some of these mighty flares reach a height fifty times the size of our earth! They can only be seen during an eclipse or with a special telescope that blocks the light from the disc of the sun. At these times one can also see a wonderful halo of mother-of-pearl coloured light round the sun. It is called the corona of the sun (crown). But how the corona comes about, there are theories, but we don't really know.

望遠鏡還展示了另一樣東西：從太陽噴射出的巨大「火焰」，稱為太陽閃焰（solar flares）。有些壯觀的閃焰高度可達地球的五十倍！它們只有在日食時，或用能遮住太陽盤面光芒的特殊望遠鏡才看得到。在那些時候，人們還能看到太陽周圍一圈美妙的珍珠母色光暈，稱為日冕（corona，即「王冠」之意）。但日冕是如何形成的，雖然有各種理論，我們卻並不真正知道。


The telescope has brought more and more questions about the sun.

望遠鏡為我們帶來了關於太陽越來越多的問題。


# 39. Through the Telescope
# 39. 透過望遠鏡

The telescope brings new questions. Sunspots were discovered, but leave us with the question what sunspots really are. We don't know why their number increases every eleven years, or what causes the mighty solar flares or the beautiful corona. If we turn the telescope to our nearest neighbour in the cosmos, the moon, it is no different.

望遠鏡帶來了新的問題。太陽黑子被發現了，卻留給我們一個疑問——太陽黑子究竟是什麼。我們不知道為什麼它們的數量每十一年就會增加，也不知道是什麼引發了壯觀的太陽閃焰或美麗的日冕。如果我們把望遠鏡轉向宇宙中最近的鄰居——月球，情況也沒什麼不同。


With the naked eye we see dark patches. We call it the man in the moon, in India and Africa they call it the hare in the moon. Looking through a telescope at the face of the moon we see mountains, and each mountain is a ring with a hole in it. These holes are called craters. Crater is the name given to the opening on top of a volcano, the opening where lava used to come out. Are the mountains on the moon volcanoes, are the round holes craters? We don't know. Most astronomers today say that these craters have been caused by meteorites falling on the moon. But it is just guesswork. All we do know is that these strange mountains have no snow-caps, no rivers, no clouds, and nothing grows on them. And we see these mountains so clearly in the telescope that there can be no air on the moon. But we don't really know what caused the craters or the mountains. The telescope has again brought us new questions but few answers.

用肉眼看，月亮上有暗色斑塊。我們稱之為「月亮上的人影」，在印度和非洲，人們稱之為「月亮上的兔子」。透過望遠鏡看月球表面，我們看到山脈，每座山都是一個環形，中間有個洞。這些洞叫做環形山（craters）。「Crater」原是火山頂端開口的名稱，也就是岩漿曾經湧出的地方。月球上的山是火山嗎？那些圓形的洞是火山口嗎？我們不知道。今天大多數天文學家說這些環形山是隕石撞擊月球造成的，但那只是猜測。我們唯一確知的是，這些奇特的山沒有雪頂、沒有河流、沒有雲，也不生長任何東西。而且我們在望遠鏡中看得如此清晰，表明月球上不可能有空氣。但我們並不真正知道環形山或山脈的成因。望遠鏡再次帶給我們新的問題，卻少有答案。


Let us turn to Saturn. Saturn is not a very impressive sight for the naked eye, it is not very bright. But through the telescope, Saturn is the strangest sight of all the planets. There is a shiny globe (reflecting the sunlight, it has no light of its own), and around the globe there is a shining, broad ring. No other planet has such a ring. As a matter of fact, in a very strong telescope one can see that it is not really one ring but several concentric rings, one inside the other.

讓我們轉向土星（Saturn）。土星肉眼看來並不起眼，不太亮。但透過望遠鏡，土星是所有行星中最奇特的景象。有一個閃亮的球體（反射陽光，它本身不發光），球體周圍環繞著一圈寬闊而明亮的環。沒有其他行星有這樣的環。事實上，用非常強大的望遠鏡可以看到，那其實不是一個環，而是好幾個同心環，一個套在另一個裡面。


Again, these wonderful rings of Saturn pose all kinds of questions. For instance, why has only Saturn, of all the planets, such big rings? (Some of the other planets have very faint rings) What are the rings? One theory is that the rings are made up of thousands of tiny grains of dust which all go round Saturn, as our moon goes round the earth, but that is one theory. The strangest thing about these rings is that they form a very broad band around Saturn, with a diameter about 20 times that of the earth. But this enormous ring is very, very thin, only about 20 metres. When Saturn is at a certain angle, we cannot see the rings at all. It is as if we were looking at the edge of a sheet of paper held level to our eyes. So, here again, the telescope shows us the rings of Saturn, but they are a mystery and a question.

這些美妙的土星環又引發了各種問題。例如，為什麼在所有行星中，只有土星有這麼大的環？（其他一些行星有非常微弱的環。）這些環是什麼？一種理論認為，環是由成千上萬的微小塵粒組成的，它們都繞著土星運行，就像月球繞地球運行一樣，但那只是一種理論。這些環最奇特之處在於，它們形成一條圍繞土星的非常寬闊的帶，直徑大約是地球的二十倍。但這條巨大的環卻非常非常薄，只有大約二十公尺。當土星處於某個角度時，我們完全看不到環。就好像我們平視一張紙的邊緣一樣。所以，望遠鏡再次向我們展示了土星環，但它們仍是一個奧祕和疑問。


Jupiter, the next planet, has several moons. Galileo saw four of them, another was discovered at the end of the nineteenth century. Four more were found in the first few years of the twentieth century, and another four were found before 1980. Now (2011) with space probes, astronomers reckon there are 63 moons around Jupiter. Looking at Jupiter through a telescope one sees darker and lighter bands going across the globe, called the belts of Jupiter. And these horizontal belts are forever shifting and changing. Astronomers think the shifting bands are different kinds of gas. Strangely, besides these shifting, changing belts, there is a large red spot, the Great Red Spot of Jupiter, but this red spot is always in the same place. We do not really know what this red spot is, or why it does not change or shift. Again, the telescope has brought us new questions.

木星（Jupiter），這顆行星有好幾個衛星。伽利略看到了四個，十九世紀末又發現了一個，二十世紀最初幾年又發現了四個，一九八〇年之前又找到四個。到了二〇一一年，透過太空探測器，天文學家估計木星周圍有六十三個衛星。用望遠鏡看木星，可以看到球體上交替出現的深淺條紋，稱為木星帶。這些水平帶紋不斷移動變化。天文學家認為那些移動的帶紋是不同種類的氣體。奇怪的是，除了這些不斷移動變化的帶紋之外，還有一個巨大的紅斑——木星大紅斑（Great Red Spot），但這個紅斑卻總是在同一個位置。我們並不真正知道這個紅斑是什麼，也不知道它為什麼不移動、不變化。望遠鏡再次帶給我們新的問題。


The next planet is Mars, the "red" planet; when Mars is in the night-sky its red glow flashes like a ruby in the sky. Seen through a telescope Mars looks like a disc in a glowing orange colour. Astronomers say this orange colour is like some deserts here on earth, the yellow-orange desert sands on earth have this colour and so, perhaps, the whole of Mars is nothing but dead, dry desert. When, in the nineteenth century telescopes were powerful enough to see some detail of Mars, astronomers found a crisscross of lines which are of a grey-green colour, which were named canals. Later, with better telescopes, it was shown that these "canals" were optical illusions, like the dark spots we "see" where thick white lines intersect on a black background.

下一顆行星是火星（Mars），「紅色行星」；當火星出現在夜空中，它的紅光閃爍如天上的紅寶石。透過望遠鏡看去，火星像一個發著橙色光的圓盤。天文學家說這種橙色就像地球上某些沙漠——地球上黃橙色的沙漠沙地就是這個顏色，所以也許整個火星不過是一片死寂乾燥的沙漠。十九世紀時，望遠鏡已經強大到能看到火星的一些細節，天文學家發現了灰綠色的交叉線條，被命名為「運河」。後來用更好的望遠鏡觀察，證明這些「運河」其實是視覺錯覺，就像我們在黑色背景上看到粗白線交叉處出現「暗點」一樣。


Another puzzle on Mars remains. On opposite sides of the orange disc of Mars there are white patches, reminding us, of course, of our Arctic and Antarctic. These white caps appear to be ice, like our poles. Mars has seasons, just as we have, Mars has summer and winter, only they take twice as long as our seasons. Here on earth when it is summer on the northern half it is winter in the southern half, in Australia, for instance. It is the same on Mars and we can see it in the telescope. When it is summer in the northern half of Mars, the white ice cap becomes smaller and smaller and at the same time the southern white cap grows bigger and bigger. After half a Mars-year things change round again, the small patch grows again and the big patch opposite shrinks. But the strange thing is that while here on earth our polar ice caps shrink or grow very little in the course of a year, on Mars they shrink and grow enormously. Again the telescope has presented us with more questions.

火星上還有另一個謎。在火星橙色圓盤的兩端各有白色斑塊，自然讓我們想到北極和南極。這些白色冰冠看起來像冰，就像地球的兩極。火星也有四季，和我們一樣有夏天和冬天，只是持續時間是我們的兩倍。在地球上，北半球是夏天時，南半球就是冬天——比如在澳洲。火星也是如此，我們在望遠鏡中可以看到。當火星北半球是夏天時，白色冰冠越來越小，同時南方的白色冰冠越來越大。半個火星年之後又反過來，小的重新長大，對面大的則縮小。但奇怪的是，地球上的極地冰冠在一年之中只有很小的消長，而火星上的冰冠卻變化巨大。望遠鏡再次向我們提出了更多問題。


Now we come to the beautiful morning and evening star, Venus. The telescope can tell us nothing at all about Venus. Venus is surrounded by clouds, a complete, dense veil of clouds. The light of Venus is so dazzling white because the sun's rays are reflected by this unbroken veil of clouds. But the telescope cannot let us see through clouds and so we know nothing about what is below the clouds on Venus. The goddess of beauty is veiled by clouds.

現在我們來到美麗的晨星與昏星——金星（Venus）。關於金星，望遠鏡什麼也告訴不了我們。金星被雲層包圍，一層完整而濃密的雲的面紗。金星的光之所以如此耀眼的白，是因為太陽光被這片不斷的雲層面紗所反射。但望遠鏡無法穿透雲層，所以我們對金星雲層之下的情況一無所知。美之女神被雲紗所遮蔽。


And Mercury is so small and so near to the sun, that the telescope cannot tell us much about Mercury either.

而水星（Mercury）又小又靠近太陽，望遠鏡也無法告訴我們太多關於水星的事。


With the fixed stars we come again to mysteries. Most of the fixed stars are so far away that even with the strongest telescope they remain shining little dots of light. But the Milky Way which to our eyes looks like silvery dust, through the telescope is like a great river of countless stars. Some fixed stars through the telescopes are not points of light but are a shining cloud, called a nebula. A nebula is a shining cloud of some kind of gas. These nebulae have all kinds of shapes, but many have the beautiful shape of a spiral. One of the stars in Andromeda is such a shining, spiral cloud. These shining spiral nebulae are another mystery of the cosmos, presented to us through the telescope.

談到恆星，我們又回到了奧祕之中。大多數恆星如此遙遠，即使用最強大的望遠鏡，它們仍只是閃亮的小光點。但銀河——在我們肉眼看來像銀色的塵霧——透過望遠鏡卻像一條由無數星辰匯成的大河。有些恆星透過望遠鏡看不是光點，而是一團發光的雲，叫做星雲（nebula）。星雲是某種氣體形成的發光雲團。這些星雲形態各異，但許多有美麗的螺旋形狀。仙女座（Andromeda）中就有這樣一團發光的螺旋雲。這些閃耀的螺旋星雲是宇宙的又一個奧祕，透過望遠鏡呈現在我們面前。


The telescope keeps giving us new questions and sets new challenges to science. The more we discover about the cosmos, the more answers we find, the more we become aware of new enigmas, of further questions.

望遠鏡不斷給我們新的問題，為科學設下新的挑戰。我們對宇宙了解得越多，找到的答案越多，就越意識到還有新的謎團、更多的問題。


# 40. Comets and Meteorites
# 40. 彗星與隕石

There is another kind of strange wandering star, the comet. It is not often that a comet can be seen, but when it is visible in the sky it is such a strange sight that in the Middle Ages people used to be terrified when they saw them. When a comet first appears, it is simply noticed as a new star where none could be seen before. After a week or so, its position changes, and this new star not only grows brighter but also sprouts a kind of tail, a tail of light, which grows bigger and bigger. It is rather like a horse's tail, for it is finer and spread out towards the end. It is also curved, but it is a shining tail of light. After some months the tail fades, the head of the comet becomes fainter and then the whole comet disappears, and not even telescopes can find it.

還有另一種奇異的遊星——彗星（comet）。彗星不常被看到，但當它出現在天空中時，是如此怪異的景象，以致中世紀的人們看到它都會驚恐萬分。彗星剛出現時，只是被注意到原本看不見的地方多了一顆新星。大約一週後，它的位置變了，這顆新星不僅變得更亮，還長出一種尾巴——一條光的尾巴，越來越大。它很像馬尾，因為越到末端越細而散開。它也是彎曲的，但那是一條閃亮的光尾。幾個月後，尾巴消褪，彗頭越來越暗，然後整顆彗星消失了，連望遠鏡都找不到它。


Now astronomers were curious about two things: the tail of the comet, and its path. They noticed that the tail of every comet always pointed away from the sun. They also observed that at first no tail could be seen, and only when the comet came near to the sun did the tail appear, and then it disappeared as the comet went away from the sun. Astronomers think that the tail of the comet is a kind of air or gas, much finer and thinner than our air, so fine that the sun-rays can, like a wind, push it. The tail of the comet points away from the sun because it is pushed by the sun's rays. Astronomers think it is the sun's rays which make the tail shine, that make the gas glow.

天文學家對兩件事特別好奇：彗星的尾巴和它的軌跡。他們注意到每顆彗星的尾巴都總是指向背離太陽的方向。他們也觀察到，起初看不到尾巴，只有當彗星靠近太陽時尾巴才出現，而當彗星遠離太陽後尾巴又消失了。天文學家認為彗尾是一種氣體，比我們的空氣精細得多也稀薄得多，細到陽光可以像風一樣吹動它。彗尾之所以指向背離太陽的方向，是因為被太陽光線推開的。天文學家認為正是太陽光線讓尾巴發光，讓氣體發亮。


Some comets come regularly, reappearing regularly in times between 20 years and 200 years. These comets move in a great ellipse round the sun, following the same laws as Kepler discovered for the planets. But while the planets move in almost circular ellipses, comets move in very flat ellipses. Some comets move in such flat ellipses that astronomers can calculate it will take thousands of years or even much longer for them to return. But sometimes these comets appear a few times and then are never seen again. There are also comets which appeared suddenly and unexpectedly and have never been seen before. So we don't really know where they come from and what their path is once they go away.

有些彗星定期出現，每隔二十年到兩百年重複回來。這些彗星沿著巨大的橢圓軌道繞太陽運行，遵循與克卜勒為行星所發現的相同定律。但行星的橢圓軌道幾乎是圓形的，而彗星的橢圓卻非常扁平。有些彗星的橢圓軌道如此扁平，天文學家計算出它們需要數千年甚至更長時間才能回來。但有時候，這些彗星出現幾次後就再也看不到了。也有些彗星突然意外出現，以前從未被見過。所以我們並不真正知道它們從何而來，離去之後走的是什麼路徑。


There was a comet, Biela's Comet, which was observed for the first time in 1772. It came again a number of times in the nineteenth century and astronomers expected it to return in 1872, but they calculated that the comet would come right in the path of the earth and collide with the earth. Many people became terrified, believing the earth would be destroyed in the collision. But when 1872 came, there was no comet. All that happened was that there were more shooting stars, or meteorites, than usual. The comet was never seen again, and the meteorites were all that was left of this comet.

有一顆彗星叫做 Biela（比拉）彗星，在一七七二年被首次觀測到。十九世紀它又回來了好幾次，天文學家預測它會在一八七二年再次出現，但他們計算出這顆彗星會正好進入地球的軌道，與地球相撞。許多人嚇壞了，以為地球會在碰撞中毀滅。但一八七二年到來時，彗星並沒有出現。所發生的只是流星——或說隕石——比平常多了許多。那顆彗星再也沒有被看到，那些隕石就是它留下的全部。


Meteorites are visitors from the cosmos. Perhaps all meteorites are bits of some ancient comets, but this is not certain. For bright comets are rather rare, but meteorites fall quite regularly at certain times of year. For instance, between August 11 and 13, there are a large number of meteorites, and again November 16-18 is a time of many meteorites falling. Astronomers think that there are swarms of meteorites in the path of the earth (like swarms of bees) and every time the earth moves into such a swarm we have a shower of shooting stars. But, sometimes — and no one knows why — there is a real downpour of meteorites. On the night of November 12-13, 1833, people in North America were treated to a strange show of fireworks; for nine hours the sky was ablaze with continuous flashes of falling meteorites.

隕石是來自宇宙的訪客。也許所有隕石都是某些古老彗星的碎片，但這並不確定。因為明亮的彗星相當罕見，但隕石卻在每年的特定時期相當規律地降落。例如八月十一日到十三日之間會有大量隕石，十一月十六日到十八日也是隕石頻繁降落的時期。天文學家認為，在地球的軌道上存在著隕石群（就像蜂群一樣），每當地球進入這樣的隕石群，我們就會看到一場流星雨。但有時候——沒有人知道為什麼——會出現真正的隕石暴雨。一八三三年十一月十二日到十三日的夜晚，北美洲的人們目睹了一場奇異的煙火秀；整整九個小時，天空因持續不斷的隕石閃光而燃燒。


The meteorite does not shine until it comes into the atmosphere surrounding the earth. Falling at a great speed, it heats up with the friction of the air, becoming white hot. Most meteorites are completely burnt up high in the air but a number do reach the earth. The famous black stone, the Kaaba in Mecca which Muslims regard as holy, may well be a large meteorite. In 2007 a large meteorite fell in Peru near Lake Titicaca. It made a crater almost 5 metres deep, shattering the windows in a house 1 km away. And boiling water and foul-smelling gases started coming out of the crater. The meteorite had cracked the rocks allowing groundwater to rise together with trapped gases.

隕石直到進入地球周圍的大氣層時才會發光。以極高的速度墜落時，它因空氣摩擦而升溫，變得白熱。大多數隕石在高空就完全燒盡了，但也有一些確實到達了地面。麥加（Mecca）那塊著名的黑石——穆斯林視為神聖的天房（Kaaba）之石——很可能就是一顆巨大的隕石。二〇〇七年，一顆大隕石墜落在秘魯的的喀喀湖（Lake Titicaca）附近。它造成了一個近五公尺深的隕石坑，震碎了一公里外一棟房屋的窗戶。沸騰的水和惡臭的氣體開始從坑中冒出。隕石撞碎了岩石，讓地下水連同被困的氣體一起湧上來。


Although the most frequent meteorite falls are in August and November there are always meteorites falling. Some come to earth only as ash, as dust because they are burnt up, some come down in bigger lumps which are not completely burnt. Scientists have calculated that every year several hundred tons of meteorite come to earth. Over a thousand or ten thousand years, that is quite a lot, and one would expect the earth to grow bigger by thousands and thousands of tons over hundred thousands of years.

儘管隕石降落最頻繁的月份是八月和十一月，但其實總是有隕石在降落。有些因為燒盡了，到達地面時只剩灰燼和塵埃；有些則以較大的塊狀降落，沒有完全燒盡。科學家計算出，每年有數百噸隕石物質降落到地球。經過一千年或一萬年，數量相當可觀，人們會以為地球在十幾萬年間應該增重了成千上萬噸。


But scientists have also worked out that this does not seem to have happened; the earth has not grown heavier or bigger. So somehow the earth gives back to the cosmos what it gets from the fall of meteorites.

但科學家也發現，這種情況似乎並沒有發生；地球既沒有變重，也沒有變大。所以不知怎的，地球把從隕石降落中得到的東西又歸還給了宇宙。


The most interesting part of the meteorites is that some consist almost entirely of iron. Without iron we would have no machines, no cars, no railways or ships, no knives and no scissors. Not only that, but our blood contains iron. People who do not have enough iron in the blood are called anaemic, they are pale, feel weak and easily tire. It is the iron in the blood which gives us strength. And this iron which is in us, and in the earth, is also in the meteorites. These meteorites, these messengers from the cosmos, are nearly completely made of iron.

隕石最有趣的一點是，有些幾乎完全由鐵組成。沒有鐵，我們就沒有機器、沒有汽車、沒有鐵路和輪船、沒有刀子和剪刀。不僅如此，我們的血液中也含有鐵。血液中鐵質不足的人稱為貧血，他們面色蒼白、感覺虛弱、容易疲倦。正是血液中的鐵給予我們力量。而這種存在於我們體內、存在於大地之中的鐵，也存在於隕石之中。這些隕石——這些來自宇宙的使者——幾乎完全由鐵構成。


Where does the iron of the meteorites come from? Some scientists think that it comes from the sun, that the sunspots which have such an influence on the magnetism of the earth, are places where iron — so hot that it is a gas — is thrown out into the cosmos. And this iron-gas cools down and when it enters our atmosphere becomes the lump of iron which is either burnt in the air or is found here and there as meteorites. But that is not certain. Even iron from the cosmos, the meteorite, is a mystery. But when we see a shooting star, we can remember that it contains the same iron that gives strength to us through our blood.

隕石中的鐵從何而來？有些科學家認為它來自太陽——那些對地球磁場有巨大影響的太陽黑子，正是鐵被加熱成氣體後拋射到宇宙中的地方。這些鐵氣冷卻下來，進入我們的大氣層後就變成鐵塊，要麼在空中燒盡，要麼在地面各處被發現，成為隕石。但這並不確定。即使是來自宇宙的鐵、隕石，也是一個謎。但當我們看到流星時，可以想起它包含的正是那透過血液賦予我們力量的鐵。


# 41. The Atmosphere of the Earth
# 41. 地球的大氣層

Compared with the great vastness of the cosmos, our own planet earth appears very small. There are millions of other suns in the cosmos: the stars. Every star is a sun, but so far away that the light of it is only a little sparkle in the sky. But astronomers who study the cosmos realize that our earth is a special place. Let us consider the planets of our solar system, of which earth is one. As a planet, the earth is much smaller than Jupiter, for instance. In fact Jupiter is bigger than all the other planets put together. But astronauts who have been in space and observed the moon, the stars and the sun from there have come to realize that the earth is a very special place.

與宇宙的廣袤浩瀚相比，我們自己的地球顯得非常渺小。宇宙中有數百萬其他的太陽——那就是恆星。每一顆恆星都是一個太陽，只是距離太遠，它的光在天上只是一點微弱的閃爍。但研究宇宙的天文學家意識到，我們的地球是一個特別的地方。讓我們來看看太陽系的行星，地球就是其中之一。作為行星，地球比木星小得多——事實上，木星比所有其他行星加起來還大。但那些到過太空、從太空觀察月球、星辰和太陽的太空人，已經認識到地球是一個非常特別的地方。


James Irwin, an American who landed on the moon, said of the earth hanging in the blackness of space, "It diminished in size. Finally it shrank to the size of a marble, the most beautiful marble you can imagine. That beautiful, warm, living object looked so fragile, so delicate. Seeing this has to change a man, has to make a man appreciate the creation of God and the love of God."

James Irwin（詹姆斯·乘員），一位登上月球的美國人，談到懸浮在太空漆黑中的地球時說過，它漸漸縮小，最後縮成彈珠般的大小，是你能想像的最美麗的彈珠。那個美麗、溫暖、活生生的物體看起來如此脆弱、如此精緻。看到這一幕，必定會改變一個人，讓人感念上帝的創造與上帝的愛。


The earth has something that no other planet has: an atmosphere with a clear blue sky, the beauty of sunrise or sunset, the ever changing weather, the winds which blow over the earth. There might be life somewhere else, there might be beings of quite another kind than man, but they will never see a rainbow, they will never see a blue sky or the glow of sunrise.

地球擁有其他行星所沒有的：一層有著清澈藍天的大氣層、日出或日落的美景、不斷變化的天氣、吹拂大地的風。別處也許有生命，也許有與人類完全不同的存在，但他們永遠看不到彩虹，永遠看不到藍天或晨曦的光輝。


Whenever we look up to sun and stars, we see them through the atmosphere. Between us and the cosmos there is a great sphere surrounding the earth, the atmosphere. The atmosphere consists of air. Just as a fish lives at the bottom of the sea, so human beings, animals and plants live at the bottom of an ocean of air. People who climb high mountains or fly high in planes discover that the air gradually gets thinner the higher we go, and so they have to take air with them, they carry oxygen cylinders. Further down, we are always surrounded by this great ocean of air.

每當我們仰望太陽和星辰，都是透過大氣層在看。在我們和宇宙之間，有一個巨大的球體包圍著地球，那就是大氣層。大氣層由空氣組成。就像魚生活在海底一樣，人類、動物和植物生活在空氣之海的底部。登高山或搭飛機飛行很高的人會發現，越高空氣越稀薄，所以必須隨身攜帶空氣——他們帶著氧氣瓶。而在低處，我們始終被這片廣大的空氣之海所包圍。


But this ocean is not only air, the atmosphere also contains water in the form of vapour. If we boil water it goes up as steam, it evaporates. But water also evaporates without boiling, as you can see when washing is hung out to dry, or when you spill some drops. The water goes away, it evaporates. This evaporation goes on all the time over land, but also over oceans, lakes, rivers, streams. Water is continually evaporating, and so the air of the atmosphere is filled with vapour. The air can hold a certain amount of water vapour, but if there is too much vapour, then the vapour condenses back into water. If we have mist, fog, clouds, rain, then the air has more water than it can hold, and the air sends the water back to earth.

但這片海洋不只是空氣，大氣層還以水蒸氣的形式含有水分。燒開水時水會變成蒸汽上升，這就是蒸發。但水不用煮沸也會蒸發，比如把洗好的衣服晾出去乾燥，或灑了幾滴水在地上，水就會消失——蒸發掉了。這種蒸發隨時隨地都在發生，在陸地上如此，在海洋、湖泊、河流、溪澗上也是如此。水不斷蒸發，因此大氣中的空氣充滿了水蒸氣。空氣能容納一定量的水蒸氣，但如果水蒸氣太多，就會凝結回水。當我們遇到薄霧、濃霧、雲、雨，就表示空氣中的水分超過了它所能容納的量，空氣把水送回了大地。


Warm air can hold more water vapour, and cold air holds less, just like a warm-hearted person receives visitors gladly, and a cold-hearted person will turn them away. There are always currents of warm air as well as currents of cold air in the atmosphere. Warm air rises and cold air falls, so even without the wind the air is continually moving. And where cold air and warm air come together, there is a battle, a clash, between the warm air and the cold air. What shows us where this battle is, are the clouds.

暖空氣能容納更多水蒸氣，冷空氣容納得較少——就像熱心的人樂於接待訪客，而冷漠的人會把他們拒之門外。大氣中總是有暖氣流和冷氣流同時存在。暖空氣上升，冷空氣下沉，所以即使沒有風，空氣也在不斷流動。而冷空氣和暖空氣相遇的地方，就是一場冷暖的交鋒、碰撞。雲，就是告訴我們這場交鋒在哪裡的標誌。


We sometimes see clouds that change their shape very quickly. This means that there is a very strong current of either warm or cold air. But sometimes a cloud formation does not change its shape much for hours, it does not even change its place, and we might think that nothing is happening. But, actually, a lot is going on in this unmoving cloud. From below warm vapour rises continuously, and when it meets cold air, the vapour turns into tiny, tiny droplets of water which hang in the air, they are too small to fall, they have hardly any weight at all. But as warm air reaches the droplets in the clouds and around the edges the droplets evaporate again and rise higher. So there is continually new vapour coming from below and becoming drops, and drops becoming vapour and floating away. The cloud shape remains the same, but all the time the drops which make it are changing.

我們有時看到雲迅速變形，這意味著有非常強的暖氣流或冷氣流。但有時候一團雲好幾個小時都不太變形，甚至位置也不動，我們可能以為什麼都沒有發生。但實際上，在這團不動的雲裡面有很多事正在發生。下方的暖水蒸氣不斷上升，遇到冷空氣時，水蒸氣變成極小極小的水滴，懸浮在空中——它們太小了，無法落下，幾乎沒有重量。但當暖空氣觸及雲中和雲邊緣的水滴時，水滴又蒸發上升。所以持續有新的水蒸氣從下方升起變成水滴，水滴又變成水蒸氣飄散。雲的形狀保持不變，但構成它的水滴一直在更換。


To the west of Portugal there are islands called the Azores, and on one of these islands, Pico, there is a high mountain, and the top of this mountain is almost always surrounded by a cloud. This cloud has a quite regular shape, it does not change much, day and night, summer and winter. It keeps the same shape, stays in the same place, for years, even centuries. But the drops in the cloud change continually; new ones come from below, evaporate and disappear, floating away in warm air. The cloud is really like the course of a river, the riverbed remains the same, but the water is changing all the time.

在葡萄牙以西有一群島嶼叫做亞速爾群島（Azores），其中一個島——Pico（皮科島）——上有一座高山，山頂幾乎總是被一團雲環繞。這團雲有著相當規則的形狀，無論白天黑夜、夏天冬天都不太改變。它保持同樣的形狀，停在同樣的位置，年復一年，甚至數百年。但雲中的水滴不斷更換；新的從下方升起，蒸發消失，隨暖空氣飄走。這團雲其實就像一條河的河道——河床不變，但水一直在流動。


At first glance it may seem that clouds can have all kinds of shapes, but there are scientists who study the shapes of clouds. (This science is very important for pilots of planes who must know from the look of a cloud what kind of air-currents they will encounter.) These scientists have found that there are four main kinds of clouds. All the clouds we see belong to one of the four groups, or are a mixture of two kinds.

乍看之下，雲似乎可以有各種各樣的形狀，但有科學家專門研究雲的形態。（這門科學對飛行員非常重要，他們必須從雲的外觀判斷會遇到什麼樣的氣流。）這些科學家發現，雲有四種主要類型。我們看到的所有雲都屬於這四類之一，或者是兩類的混合。


Cumulus means "heap." Cumulus clouds look puffy like a sheep's fleece or like steam from a locomotive. Cumulus clouds have round forms, but the lower edge is always horizontal. The horizontal edge shows you exactly where the cold air begins. Here vapour becomes little drops.

Cumulus 的意思是「堆積」。積雲（cumulus）看起來蓬鬆得像羊毛，或像火車頭冒出的蒸汽。積雲是圓形的，但底部邊緣總是水平的。那條水平線告訴你冷空氣從哪裡開始——在那裡，水蒸氣變成了小水滴。


Cirrus means "streak." They are wispy, feathery clouds, sometimes called mares' tails. Cirrus clouds are much higher than the cumulus clouds, so high that the droplets freeze, becoming tiny ice crystals.

Cirrus 的意思是「絲縷」。卷雲（cirrus）是纖細、羽毛般的雲，有時被稱為「馬尾雲」。卷雲比積雲高得多，高到水滴凍結成微小的冰晶。


Stratus means "layer." These are low layers of clouds. These low stratus clouds often veil mountain tops. Mountaineers don't like stratus clouds, for in such clouds they can't see where they are going. Mist and fog are really stratus clouds.

Stratus 的意思是「層」。層雲（stratus）是低低的雲層。這些低矮的層雲常常遮蔽山頂。登山者不喜歡層雲，因為在這種雲裡他們看不清方向。霧氣和濃霧其實就是層雲。


Nimbus just means "rain cloud." This type is always in a mixture. Nimbostratus is a shapeless grey cloud with steady rain or drizzle. Cumulonimbus is a very big, puffy cloud which can cause a thunderstorm.

Nimbus 就是「雨雲」的意思。這種類型總是以混合型態出現。雨層雲（nimbostratus）是灰濛濛沒有固定形狀的雲，帶來持續的雨或毛毛雨。積雨雲（cumulonimbus）是非常巨大蓬鬆的雲，能引發雷暴。


Cirrus are the highest clouds, stratus are the lowest, cumulus are in-between. There are, of course, mixtures, for instance cumulostratus is the cloud we often see — large areas of lumpy clouds, often producing showers.

卷雲在最高處，層雲在最低處，積雲在中間。當然還有混合型，例如層積雲（cumulostratus）就是我們常見的——大片凹凸不平的雲，常帶來陣雨。


These clouds in the atmosphere — always changing — and the droplets in them continually evaporating and recondensing, are the carriers of life. For without clouds we would have no rain over the land, and without rain there would be no rivers, no lakes. The land would become desert, and all our precious life here on the earth would die out.

大氣中的這些雲——永遠在變化——以及雲中不斷蒸發又凝結的水滴，就是生命的承載者。因為沒有雲，陸地上就不會有雨；沒有雨，就不會有河流、沒有湖泊。大地會變成沙漠，地球上所有珍貴的生命都會消亡。


So having surveyed the vast expanses of the cosmos, we come to see that our own earth, with its atmosphere, its clouds, its rain and rivers, is truly a very special place in the universe.

這樣縱覽了宇宙的廣袤之後，我們終於看到：我們自己的地球，帶著它的大氣層、雲彩、雨水和河流，在宇宙中確實是一個非常特別的地方。
